Ruling on a Muhrim Slaughtering Game and Eating It
Explains ruling and compensations for a muhrim who kills and eats game.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a muhrim who slaughters game and then eats it, and identify the number of compensations required according to different Hanafi imams.

Core Idea
A muhrim's slaughter of game is haram; further actions may multiply compensations.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, detailing the prohibitions and compensations when a person in ihram (muhrim) kills game. It covers not only the basic ruling but also edge cases such as eating eggs, feeding dogs, and the disputed scenario of gifting game to another muhrim. Understanding these nuances is essential for correctly applying the rules of hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
Read the opening sentence: 'ذبح المحرم صيداً حرم وغرم بأكله'. The act is haram and requires compensation for eating. Note that this applies only to the muhrim who killed it, not to another muhrim.
The compensation (ghurm) is a financial penalty.
2
Analyze exceptions and inclusions
The text mentions eggs (no further compensation if already paid), feeding dogs (included in 'eating'), and the permissibility of selling with dislike. Understand why the egg exception exists: the egg is treated as the 'origin' of game, and breaking it ends that status.
These exceptions show the depth of Hanafi casuistry.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on gifted game
Focus on the al-Muhit quote: a muhrim gifts game to another muhrim who eats it. Abu Hanifa rules three compensations on the eater; Muhammad rules two. Identify the reasoning: the gift is fasid (invalid), so ownership remains with the donor, and each violation (slaughter, eating, donor's loss) may require separate compensation.
The dispute is recorded without tarjih, showing scholarly diversity.
4
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
Compare the practical outcomes: under Abu Hanifa, the eater pays three values; under Muhammad, two. This illustrates how different analyses of the same facts lead to different financial obligations.
The mufta bihi is not specified; later works may resolve the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذبح المحرم صيداً حرم وغرم بأكله لا محرم آخر وحل له لحم ما صاده حلال وذبحه إن لم يدل عليه ولم يأمره بصيده وبذبح الحلال صيد الحرم قيمة يتصدق بها لا صوم ومن شيء عليه اتفاقاً لأن وجوب الجزاء لفوات إلا من الثابت بالحرم للصيد لا للحمه. وقيد بأكله أي أكل لحمه لأن مأكول المحرم لو كان بيض صيد بعد ما كسره وأدى جزاءه لا شيء عليه اتفاقاً كما قدمناه عن المحيط لأن وجوب الجزاء فيه باعتبار أنه أصل الصيد وبعد الكسر انعدم هذا المعنى. وفي فتح القدير : ويكره بيعه فإن باعه جاز ويجعل ثمنه في الفداء إن شاء، وكذا شجر الحرم واللبن ا هـ . وأشار إلى أن مأكوله لو كان لحم جزاء الصيد فإنه يضمن قيمة ما أكل بالأولى وهو متفق عليه. وقد قدمناه وأراد بالأكل الانتفاع بلحمه فشمل ما إذا أطعمه لكلابه فإنه يضمن قيمته. وفي المحيط : محرم وهب لمحرم صيداً فأكله قال أبو حنيفة : على الأكل ثلاثة أجزية : قيمة للذبح وقيمة للأكل المحظور وقيمة للواهب لأن الهبة كانت فاسدة وعلى الواهب قيمته. وقال محمد على الآكل قيمتان قيمة للواهب وقيمة للذبح ولا شيء للأكل عنده اهـ. وهو صريح في لزوم قيمتين على المحرم بقتل الصيد المملوك كما ذكرناه أول الفصل
If a muhrim slaughters game, it becomes forbidden and he must pay compensation for eating it, not for another muhrim. And it is permissible for him to eat meat that a non-muhrim hunted and slaughtered if the muhrim did not indicate it or order its hunting. And for a non-muhrim slaughtering game of the Haram, he must pay its value in charity, not fasting. And there is no disagreement about something because the obligation of compensation is due to the loss of the game established in the Haram, for the game itself not its meat. He restricted it to eating, meaning eating its meat, because if what the muhrim eats is the egg of game after he broke it and paid its compensation, there is nothing on him by agreement, as we mentioned from al-Muhit, because the obligation of compensation in that case is based on it being the origin of the game, and after breaking this meaning ceased. In Fath al-Qadir: it is disliked to sell it, but if he sells it, it is permissible and he may use its price for the fidyah if he wishes, and similarly for trees of the Haram and milk. He indicated that if what he eats is the meat of the compensation of game, then he guarantees the value of what he ate by a stronger reason, and it is agreed upon. And we mentioned it, and he meant by eating benefiting from its meat, so it includes if he feeds it to his dogs, then he guarantees its value. In al-Muhit: A muhrim gave game as a gift to another muhrim and he ate it. Abu Hanifa said: on the eater are three compensations: value for the slaughter, value for the prohibited eating, and value for the donor because the gift was invalid, and on the donor is its value. Muhammad said: on the eater are two values: value for the donor and value for the slaughter, and nothing for the eating according to him. This is clear in the necessity of two values on the muhrim for killing owned game as we mentioned at the beginning of the chapter.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion of the matn from Kanz al-Daqaiq. It states the ruling for a muhrim (person in ihram) who slaughters game: the meat becomes forbidden (haram) for him, and he must pay compensation (ghurm) for eating it. The phrase 'لا محرم آخر' indicates that this prohibition and compensation are specific to the muhrim who kills it, not to another muhrim who might eat it. The passage then covers several subsidiary issues: first, if the muhrim eats the egg of game after breaking it and already paid compensation, no further penalty is due because the egg was considered the 'origin' of the game, and that origin is gone. Second, from Fath al-Qadir, selling the slaughtered game is disapproved (makruh) but valid, and the proceeds can be used for fidyah; this ruling extends to Haram trees and milk. Third, if a muhrim eats meat from the compensation for game (i.e., game that was already expiated), he must pay its value by an even stronger reason, and this is agreed upon. Fourth, the term 'eating' includes any beneficial use, like feeding dogs, requiring compensation. Finally, a significant intra-Hanafi dispute is presented from al-Muhit: if a muhrim gives game as a gift to another muhrim who eats it, Abu Hanifa holds that the eater owes three compensations (for slaughter, prohibited eating, and the value to the donor), while Muhammad al-Shaybani holds only two (for the donor and slaughter, not for eating). This highlights the principle that multiple violations can accumulate.

Key Terms
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, who is prohibited from hunting.
صيد (sayd): Game animals that are permissible to hunt when not in ihram, but forbidden for a muhrim.
جزاء (jaza'): Compensation required for violating hunting prohibitions, usually by slaughtering a similar animal or paying its value.
هبة فاسدة (hibah fasidah): A gift that is legally invalid due to a defect, such as the gift of something that is not owned or not deliverable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many compensations does a muhrim owe if he gifts game to another muhrim who eats it, according to Abu Hanifa?
A) One compensation for the slaughter
B) Two compensations: for the donor and for slaughter
C) Three compensations: for slaughter, prohibited eating, and the donor
D) Four compensations for all violations

Key Takeaway
A muhrim who slaughters game incurs a haram act and must pay compensation for both slaughter and eating, and further actions like gifting can multiply compensations.

Conditions for a Muhrim Eating Game Hunted by a Non-Muhrim
Establishes permissibility for muhrim to eat game hunted by halal with conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions under which a muhrim may eat game hunted by a non-muhrim, apply the hadith of Abu Qatada to derive the ruling, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of indication.

Core Idea
If a muhrim indicates or orders the hunt, he cannot eat—the hadith proves permissibility hinges on no involvement.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a specific rule for pilgrims in ihram: they may eat game hunted by someone not in ihram, but only if they themselves had no hand in prompting the hunt. The ruling is derived from a well-known hadith, and the Hanafi masters differed on what counts as 'prompting.' Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the rules of ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a muhrim (one in ihram) eating game meat that was hunted and slaughtered by a non-muhrim (halal). The ruling in the matn is that it is halal (permissible), but with conditions.
The permissibility is not absolute; it is conditional on the absence of two factors.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Abu Qatada, found in Bukhari and Muslim. He hunted a wild donkey while not in ihram and brought it to the Prophet ﷺ and some Companions who were muhrim. The Prophet did not immediately permit; he asked if anyone pointed to the game or ordered its hunting. When they said no, he permitted.
Note the Prophet's methodology: he checked for potential preventers before giving the ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's question shows that the permissibility depends on the absence of 'indication' (dalalah) and 'ordering' (amr). The hadith explicitly links the conditional answer 'Then eat' to the absence of these two. Thus, if either is present, the ruling would be the opposite.
This is a mafhum al-mukhalafah: the opposite implication of the condition.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Within the Hanafi school, there is a dispute over whether indication or ordering actually makes the game haram for the muhrim. Al-Tahawi held it becomes haram; al-Jurjani held it remains permissible (the indication is only a sin but does not affect the meat).
Al-Quduri considered al-Jurjani mistaken and relied on al-Tahawi's narration.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text states that the chosen (mukhtar) view is that the game becomes haram for the muhrim if he indicated or ordered. This is the mufta bihi position supported by al-Quduri and later Hanafi works.
Practical outcome: a muhrim who points at game and a non-muhrim hunts it cannot eat from that game.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وحل له لحم ما صاده حلال وذبحه إن لم يدل عليه وإن لم يأمره بصيده) الحديث أبي قتادة الثابت في الصحيحين حين اصطاد وهو حلال حماراً وحشياً وأتى به لمن كان محرماً من الصحابة فإنهم لما سألوه عليه السلام لم يجب بحله لهم حتى سألهم عن موانع الحل أكانت موجودة أم لا فقال عليه السلام هل منكم أحد أمره أن يحمل عليها أو أشار إليها؟ قالوا : لا . فقال : كلوا إذا ، فدل على حله للمحرم ولو صاده الحلال لأجله لأنه لو كان من الموانع أن يصاد لهم لنظمه في سلك ما يسأل عنه منها قيد بعدم الدلالة والأمر لأنه لو وجد أحدهما من المحرم للحلال فإنه يحرم على المحرم أكله على ما هو المختار وفيه روايتان، وذكر الطحاوي تحريمه. وقال الجرجاني : لا يحرم. وغلطه القدوري واعتمد رواية الطحاوي، وظاهر ما في غاية البيان أن الروايتين في حرمة الصيد على الحلال بدلالة المحرم مع أن ظاهر الكتب أن الدلالة من المحرم محرمة عليه للصيد لا على الصائد الحلال. ثم اعلم أن عطفهم محرم أو حلال، سواء اصطاده هو أي ذابحه أو غيره محرم أو حلال ولو في الحل، فلو أكل المحرم الذابح منه شيئاً قبل أداء الضمان أو بعده فعليه قيمة ما أكل ولو أكل منه غير الذابح فلا شيء عليه، ولو أكل الحلال مما ذبحه في الحرم بعد الضمان لا شيء عليه للأكل، ولو اصطاد حلال فذبح له محرم أو اصطاد محرم فذبح له حلال فهو ميتة ا هـ . الأمر على الدلالة هنا يفيد أنه غيرها وهو مؤيد لما قدمناه أول الفصل فراجعه
His statement: 'And it is permissible for him to eat meat that a non-muhrim hunted and slaughtered, if he did not indicate it and did not order its hunting.' The hadith of Abu Qatada, established in the two Sahihs, when he, while non-muhrim, hunted a wild donkey and brought it to the Companions who were muhrim. When they asked him (peace be upon him), he did not answer regarding its permissibility for them until he asked them about the preventers of permissibility: 'Are any of you who ordered him to carry it or pointed to it?' They said: No. He said: 'Then eat.' So this indicates its permissibility for the muhrim even if the non-muhrim hunted it for his sake, because if it were among the preventers that it be hunted for them, he would have included it in what he asked about. So he conditioned it on the absence of indication and order, because if either occurs from the muhrim to the non-muhrim, then it becomes forbidden for the muhrim to eat it according to the chosen view, and there are two narrations. Al-Tahawi mentioned its prohibition, and al-Jurjani said it is not prohibited. Al-Quduri considered him mistaken and relied on al-Tahawi's narration. The apparent from Ghayat al-Bayan is that the two narrations concern the prohibition of hunting upon the non-muhrim due to the muhrim's indication, while the apparent from the books is that the indication from the muhrim is prohibited for him regarding the hunt, not upon the hunter who is non-muhrim. Then know that their inclusion of 'muhrim or non-muhrim' whether he hunted it himself, i.e., the slaughterer, or someone else, muhrim or non-muhrim even if in the non-sanctuary, so if the muhrim slaughterer eats something from it before or after paying compensation, he owes the value of what he ate, but if someone other than the slaughterer eats, there is nothing on him. And if a non-muhrim eats from what was slaughtered in the Haram after compensation, there is nothing on him for eating. And if a non-muhrim hunted and a muhrim slaughtered for him, or a muhrim hunted and a non-muhrim slaughtered for him, it is carrion. The matter regarding indication here indicates that it is other than that, and it supports what we mentioned at the beginning of the chapter, so consult it.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage expands on the matn ruling that a muhrim may eat game hunted by a halal (non-muhrim) under two conditions: (1) the muhrim did not indicate (dalla) the game to the hunter, and (2) he did not order (amara) the hunt. The proof is the authentic hadith of Abu Qatada, who, while non-muhrim, hunted a wild donkey and brought it to the Prophet ﷺ and his Companions who were in ihram. The Prophet asked if anyone had pointed to it or ordered its hunting; when they said no, he permitted them to eat. This shows that the permissibility hinges on the absence of these actions. The text then discusses an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: if the muhrim does indicate or order, is it haram for him to eat? Al-Tahawi says it becomes haram, al-Jurjani says it does not. al-Quduri favored al-Tahawi's view, and this is considered the relied-upon position. Further, the passage clarifies that the prohibition of indication applies to the muhrim himself, not to the halal hunter. The commentary also addresses scenarios of mixed actions: if a muhrim eats from game he himself slaughtered, he owes value; if another muhrim eats, no penalty; if a halal person eats from game slaughtered in the Haram, no penalty; and if roles are reversed in hunting and slaughtering, the result is carrion (maytah). The final sentence reaffirms that indication is different from the ruling, supporting earlier points.

Key Terms
دلالة (dalalah): The act of a muhrim pointing out or indicating game to a hunter, which if done, makes the game haram for the muhrim.
الأمر بالصيد (al-amr bi al-sayd): Explicitly ordering a halal person to hunt game; like dalalah, it prevents the muhrim from eating.
موانع الحل (mawani' al-hill): Factors that prevent the permissibility of eating game for a muhrim, primarily indication and ordering.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Abu Qatada, what condition allows a muhrim to eat game hunted by a non-muhrim?
A) The game must be a wild donkey
B) The muhrim must not have indicated or ordered the hunt
C) The non-muhrim must be a Companion
D) The game must be cooked

Key Takeaway
A muhrim may eat game hunted by a non-muhrim only if he did not indicate or order the hunt; otherwise, it becomes haram.

Compensation for Game Killed in the Haram by a Non-Muhrim
States the requirement of value (qimah) for a halal person killing game in the Haram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a non-muhrim killing game in the Haram and explain why fasting is not an option, citing the hadith and the principle of property-based compensation (daman).

Core Idea
A non-muhrim killing game in the Haram pays its value; fasting is invalid because daman is property-related, not expiatory.

When a person who is not in the state of ihram (halal) kills game within the sacred boundaries of the Haram, Islamic law imposes a specific compensation. The Hanafi school, drawing on the hadith 'لا ينفر صيدها' and consensus, rules that the killer must give the value of the game in charity, and unlike a muhrim, fasting is not an acceptable substitute. This lesson unpacks the proof, the school's internal differences, and the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the matn phrase: 'وبذبح الحلال صيد الحرم قيمة يتصدق بها لا صوم'. The act is a halal person slaughtering game within the Haram. The ruling is wajib: he must give the game's value in charity and cannot fast instead.
Contrast with a muhrim who may fast.
2
Locate the dalil
The source cites the authentic hadith 'ولا ينفر صيدها' (its game shall not be chased away) and the consensus (ijma) that compensation is obligatory.
The hadith is ahad but sahih; ijma gives certainty.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith prohibits chasing, and by mafhum awla (greater implication) killing is even more prohibited. Thus, compensation is wajib. Moreover, the compensation is property-based because the game's inviolability is due to the place (Haram), not due to ihram. Hence, fasting—which is an expiation for ihram violations—does not apply.
This is why the rule differs from a muhrim's case.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The matn's negation of fasting implies that offering a sacrifice (hady) is permissible (zahir al-riwayah). However, al-Hasan ibn Ziyad holds that sacrifice does not suffice; only full value must be paid. Zufar allows fasting.
Practical difference: if the sacrificed animal is of lesser value than the game, or if it is stolen.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text favors the zahir al-riwayah (majority) because it aligns with the principle of equivalence in reparation. The mufta bihi is: slaughtering a similar animal suffices if its value equals the game's; otherwise pay the difference. Fasting is never valid for a halal person.
This is the position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وبذبح الحلال صيد الحرم قيمة يتصدق بها لا صوم) أي وتجب قيمة بذبح صيد الحرم ويلزمه التصدق بها ولا يجزئه الصوم لأن الصيد استحق الأمن بسبب الحرم للحديث الصحيح «ولا ينفر صيدها» فأفاد حرمة التنفير فالقتل أولى. وانعقد الإجماع على وجوب الجزاء بقتله فيتصدق بقيمته على الفقراء ولا يجزئه الصوم لأن الضمان فيه باعتبار المحل وهو الصيد فصار كغرامة الأموال بخلاف المحرم فإن الضمان ثمة جزاء الفعل لإجزاء المحل والصوم يصلح له لأنه كفارة له ولصريح النص أو عدل ذلك صياما وإنما اقتصر المصنف على نفي الصوم ليفيد أن الهدي جائز وهو ظاهر الرواية لأنه فعل مثل ما جنى لأن جنايته كانت بالإراقة وقد أتى بمثل ما فعل وفي رواية الحسن لا تجزئه الإراقة وفائدة الخلاف تظهر فيما إذا كانت قيمة المذبوح قبل الذبح أقل من قيمة الصيد ؛ فعلى ظاهر الرواية تكفيه الإراقة وعلى رواية الحسن يتصدق بتمام القيمة، وفيما إذا سرق المذبوح فعلى الظاهر لا يجب أن يقيم غيره مقامه . وعلى رواية الحسن تجب الإقامة وإنما قيد بالحلال ليفيد أن حكم المحرم في صيد الحرم كحكم الحلال بالأولى، والقياس أن يلزمه جزاءان لوجود الجناية في الإحرام والحرم، وفي الاستحسان يلزمه جزاء واحد لأن حرمة الإحرام أقوى لتحريمه القتل في الحل والحرم فاعتبر الأقوى وأضيفت الحرمة إليه عند تعذر الجمع بينهما ولهذا وجب الجزاء به لا لنفسه. وأما شجر الحرم وحشيشه فهما فيه سواء لأنه ليس من محظورات الإحرام والظاهر أنه قيد احترازي يأتي عند قوله وبطل بيع المحرم صيد أو شراؤه» تأمل . قوله : (كحكم الحلال أي في وجوب القيمة، وإن كان بينهما فرق من جهة أن المحرم يجوز له الصوم كما يصرح به قريباً قوله : (والظاهر أن قيد (احترازاي أي التقييد بالحلال للاحتراز عن المحرم، فإن المحرم مخير كما مر متناً في أول هذا الفصل بخلاف الحلال فإنه لا يجزئه الصوم كما علمت. وفي عزوه المسألة إلى الهداية إيهام أنها لم تذكر هنا. وفي اللباب وأما الصوم في صيد الحرم فلا يجوز للحلال ويجوز للمحرم ا هـ . نعم عبارة المصنف أول الفصل مطلقة يمكن تقييدها بصيد المحرم في غير الحرم فلذا لم يعز إليها. وفي شرح اللباب قال في شرح القدوري : إن الإطعام يجزئ في صيد الحرم ولا يجوز الصوم عند علمائنا الثلاثة وعند زفر يجزئ ، وفي المختلف لا يجوز الصوم بالإجماع. قال صاحب المجمع فيجوز أن يكون في الصوم عن زفر روايتان فنقل كل واحد رواية، في | الحلال، أما المحرم فظاهر كلامهم أنه يجوز له الصوم والهدي بلا خلاف لأنه لما اجتمع حرمة الإحرام والحرم وتعذر الجمع بينهما وجب اعتبار أقواهما وهو الإحرام فأضيف إليه ورتب عليه أحكامه ضرورة، وبه صرح في شرح القدوري فقال: أما المحرم إذا قتل في الحرم فإنه تتأدى كفارته بالصوم ا هـ وتمامه فيه قوله : (وليس مقصودة تقييد الضمان بالذبح الخ نظر فيه في النهر بأن بتقديره ثم هذا :
His statement: 'And for a non-muhrim slaughtering game of the Haram, a value to be given in charity, not fasting.' Meaning, a value is obligatory for slaughtering game of the Haram, and he must give it in charity, and fasting does not suffice him. Because the game is entitled to safety due to the Haram, due to the authentic hadith: 'Its game shall not be chased away.' So this indicates the prohibition of chasing, and killing is even more so. Consensus has been reached on the obligation of compensation for killing it, so he gives its value in charity to the poor, and fasting does not suffice him because the guarantee here is based on the place, which is the game, so it becomes like a monetary fine, unlike the muhrim, where the guarantee is a penalty for the act due to the inviolability of the place, and fasting is suitable for him because it is an expiation for him, and due to the explicit text 'or the equivalent of that in fasting.' The author only negated fasting to indicate that offering a sacrifice (hady) is permissible, and that is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) because he does a similar act to what he transgressed, since his transgression was by spilling blood, and he has done a similar act. According to the narration of al-Hasan, slaughtering does not suffice him. The benefit of the difference appears when the value of the slaughtered animal before slaughter is less than the value of the game; according to the apparent narration, slaughter suffices him, and according to al-Hasan's narration, he gives charity for the full value. Also, if the slaughtered animal is stolen, according to the apparent narration it is not necessary to replace it, while according to al-Hasan's narration, replacement is obligatory. The restriction to 'halal' (non-muhrim) is to indicate that the ruling of the muhrim regarding game of the Haram is like that of the non-muhrim by a stronger reason. By analogy (qiyas), two compensations would be required due to transgression in both ihram and Haram, but by istihsan, one compensation is required because the sanctity of ihram is stronger, as it prohibits killing in both the non-sanctuary and the sanctuary, so the stronger is considered and the sanctity is attributed to it when joining them is impossible, and for this reason the compensation is due to it, not for itself. As for trees and grass of the Haram, they are the same in that it is not among the prohibitions of ihram. It appears that the restriction is precautionary... His statement: 'like the ruling of the halal' i.e., regarding the obligation of value, although there is a difference between them in that the muhrim is permitted to fast, as will be clarified shortly. His statement: 'And it appears that the restriction is precautionary' i.e., the restriction to halal is to exclude the muhrim, for the muhrim has a choice as mentioned in the matn at the beginning of this chapter, unlike the halal, for whom fasting does not suffice as you learned. In attributing the issue to al-Hidayah, there is an illusion that it is not mentioned here. In al-Lubab: 'As for fasting in game of the Haram, it is not permissible for the halal, and it is permissible for the muhrim.' Yes, the author's expression at the beginning of the chapter is absolute and can be restricted to the muhrim's hunting outside the Haram, so it was not attributed to it. In Sharh al-Lubab, it is said in Sharh al-Quduri: 'Feeding suffices in game of the Haram, and fasting is not permissible according to our three imams; according to Zufar, it suffices, and in al-Mukhtalaf, fasting is not permissible by consensus.' The author of al-Majma' said: It is possible that there are two narrations from Zufar regarding fasting, and each narrated one. As for the halal, while the muhrim, apparently their statements indicate that fasting and sacrifice are permissible for him without disagreement, because when the sanctity of ihram and Haram combine and joining them is impossible, the stronger of them must be considered, which is ihram, so it is attributed to it and its rulings are applied out of necessity. This is clarified in Sharh al-Quduri: 'As for the muhrim if he kills in the Haram, his expiation is fulfilled by fasting.' And its completion is in his statement: 'And it is not intended to restrict the guarantee to slaughter...' Consider this.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage expands on the matn ruling that if a non-muhrim (halal) person slaughters game within the Haram (sanctuary of Mecca), he must pay the value of that game in charity; fasting is not accepted as a substitute. The proof is the hadith 'لا ينفر صيدها' (its game shall not be chased away), which implies a prohibition on dislodging game, and killing is even more severe. Consensus (ijma) affirms the obligation of compensation. The reason fasting is not accepted is that the guarantee (daman) here is based on the property aspect of the game, similar to monetary damages, unlike the case of a muhrim where the guarantee is a penalty for violating ihram and fasting is suitable as expiation. The author notes that the matn's negation of fasting implies that offering a sacrifice (hady) is permissible, which is the position of the zahir al-riwayah. However, there is a riwayah from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad that mere slaughter does not suffice; one must pay the full value. The practical difference appears when the value of the slaughtered animal is less than the game's value, or if the slaughtered animal is stolen. The text then compares a muhrim who kills in the Haram: by qiyas he would owe two compensations (for ihram and Haram), but by istihsan (juristic preference) he owes only one because the sanctity of ihram is stronger. Thus, a muhrim may also expiate by fasting, unlike the halal person. The restriction to 'halal' is precautionary to exclude the muhrim. The passage concludes with a discussion of the source of this ruling in various texts, noting that the matn's absolute statement can be qualified.

Key Terms
صيد الحرم (sayd al-haram): Game animals within the boundaries of the Haram (sanctuary of Mecca), which are inviolable due to the sanctity of the place.
قيمة (qimah): The monetary value of the game, to be given in charity as compensation for killing it in the Haram.
الهدي (al-hady): An animal sacrificed as expiation; in this context, it is permissible for a halal person instead of fasting, but of similar value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi ruling for a non-muhrim who kills game in the Haram?
A) He must fast for three days.
B) He must give the value of the game in charity, and fasting is invalid.
C) He may choose between fasting, feeding the poor, or sacrificing an animal.
D) He must sacrifice a similar animal regardless of value.

Key Takeaway
A non-muhrim who kills game in the Haram must pay its value in charity; fasting is never an alternative because the compensation is property-based, not expiatory.

Halal Killing Game in Haram: Value Due, Not Fasting
States ruling for halal person killing game in Haram, contrasting with muhrim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a non-muhrim who kills game in the Haram, explain the dalil from hadith and ijma, and distinguish why fasting is not valid.

Core Idea
For a halal in Haram, killing game requires paying its value in charity; fasting is invalid because the guarantee is on the place.

The passage establishes a clear ruling for a person not in ihram who kills game within the sacred boundaries of Mecca. Unlike a muhrim who has multiple expiation options, the halal is limited to financial compensation. We'll examine the proof, the rationale, and the contrast with the muhrim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Determine exactly what action is being ruled upon and what the hukm (legal classification) is. Here: a halal person slaughtering game in the Haram → wajib to pay its value in charity.
The ruling is explicit in the matn: 'قيمة يتصدق بها لا صوم'.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited. The hadith 'ولا ينفر صيدها' and the consensus (ijma) on the obligation of compensation.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but supported by ijma.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the dalil proves the ruling. The prohibition of chasing away (tanfir) implies prohibition of killing by primary inference (mafhum awla).
This is a standard Hanafi usul principle: khiṭāb al-taḥrīm yushʿir bi-ʿadam al-jawāz.
4
Understand the rationale
Why is fasting not an option? Because the guarantee (ḍamān) is based on the place (the game itself), like a property guarantee. Financial compensation is the only appropriate remedy.
Contrast with the muhrim where the guarantee is a penalty for the act (jazāʾ al-fiʿl).
5
Note the contrast with muhrim
The author specifies 'halal' to indicate the muhrim's ruling is a fortiori. For a muhrim, the penalty includes options (dam, it'am, siyam) because the place is not the basis of the guarantee.
This sets up the later discussion of the qiyas-istihsan conflict.

Source Text

And by the halal person slaughtering game of the Haram, a value is owed to be given in charity, not fasting. That is, a value is owed for slaughtering game of the Haram, and he must give it in charity, and fasting does not suffice for him. Because the game earned safety due to the Haram, due to the authentic hadith: 'Its game should not be chased away.' So it indicates the prohibition of chasing away, so killing is even more [prohibited]. And consensus has been reached on the obligation of compensation for killing it. So he gives its value in charity to the poor, and fasting does not suffice for him, because the guarantee here is based on the place (the game), so it becomes like a property guarantee. Unlike the muhrim, for whom the guarantee is a penalty for the act, because the place is excusable, and fasting is suitable for him because it is an expiation for him, and due to the explicit text: 'or the equivalent of that in fasting.' The author only restricted to negating fasting to indicate that the sacrificial animal is permissible, and that is the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwaya), because he did a similar act to what he perpetrated: his perpetration was by spilling blood, and he has done a similar act. In the narration of al-Hasan, spilling blood does not suffice. And if the slaughtered animal is stolen, according to the apparent narration he does not have to replace it; according to al-Hasan's narration, replacement is obligatory. And by analogy, two penalties would be obligatory due to the transgression in ihram and the Haram. But by istihsan, one penalty is obligatory because the sanctity of ihram is stronger, as it prohibits killing inside and outside the Haram, so the stronger is considered and the sanctity is attributed to it when combining both is impossible.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary on the matn. It addresses the case where a non-muhrim (halal) person kills game within the Haram. The ruling: he must pay the value of the game and give it in charity; fasting is not a valid substitute. The proof is the hadith prohibiting chasing away the game of Mecca, which implies prohibition of killing, and the consensus on compensation. The rationale is that the guarantee is tied to the inviolable location (the game itself as property), similar to financial guarantees. For a muhrim in the Haram, by contrast, the guarantee is a penalty for the act, so fasting is allowed as expiation. The author then discusses an internal Hanafi dispute: in the Zahir al-Riwaya, offering a sacrificial animal suffices even if its value is less; in a narration by Hasan ibn Ziyad, one must pay the full value. The restriction to 'halal' is to signal that the ruling for a muhrim in the Haram is a fortiori. The passage then addresses a qiyas-istihsan conflict: analogically, two penalties would be due (one for ihram, one for haram), but istihsan favors one because ihram's sanctity is stronger. This is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
صيد الحرم (sayd al-haram): Game animals that have sought refuge within the boundaries of the Haram (Mecca), thus gaining inviolability.
الحلال (al-halal): A person who is not in the state of ihram; a non-muhrim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He must fast as expiation.
B) He must pay the value of the game in charity, and fasting is not valid.
C) He owes nothing because it was accidental.
D) He must sacrifice an animal of equivalent value.

Key Takeaway
A non-muhrim who kills game in the Haram must pay its value in charity; fasting is not a valid substitute because the guarantee is tied to the inviolability of the place.

The Internal Hanafi Dispute and the Qiyas–Istihsan Conflict on Muhrim in Haram
States ruling for halal person killing game in Haram, contrasting with muhrim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Zahir al-Riwaya and Hasan ibn Ziyad's positions on whether a sacrificial animal of lesser value suffices, and state the Hanafi resolution of the qiyas–istihsan conflict for a muhrim killing game in the Haram.

Core Idea
Two issues: (1) For halal in Haram, a sacrificial animal suffices even if worth less (Zahir al-Riwaya), but Hasan requires full value. (2) For muhrim in Haram, istihsan gives one penalty, overriding qiyas that would give two.

The passage extends beyond the basic ruling to address two points of ihtilaf. First, within the Hanafi school, there is a dispute about whether offering a sacrificial animal of lesser value fulfills the obligation. Second, for a muhrim who kills game in the Haram, there is a tension between qiyas (two penalties) and istihsan (one penalty). We'll unpack these arguments and see the relied-upon positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the internal Hanafi dispute
Note two narrations: Zahir al-Riwaya (suffices) and Hasan ibn Ziyad (full value required).
The author presents Zahir al-Riwaya as the relied-upon position.
2
Follow the thamarah (practical difference)
Two scenarios illustrate the dispute: if the slaughtered animal's value is less than the game, and if it is stolen.
These show how the ruling changes based on which narration is followed.
3
Identify the qiyas-istihsan conflict
For a muhrim in the Haram, qiyas would require two penalties, but istihsan gives one.
This is a classic example of istihsan overriding qiyas.
4
Understand the istihsan argument
Ihram's sanctity is stronger (it prohibits killing even outside Haram), so it subsumes the Haram's sanctity when combined.
The principle: 'al-aqwa yughlib al-aḍʿaf wa yuḍāf al-ḥurmah ilayh.'
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Zahir al-Riwaya is the mufta bihi for the internal dispute, and istihsan (one penalty) is the mufta bihi for the muhrim case.
These are the operative positions for fatwa.

Source Text

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many penalties does a muhrim owe for killing game inside the Haram?
A) Two: one for ihram and one for the Haram.
B) One: because istihsan prioritizes the stronger sanctity of ihram.
C) None: because the game is already inviolable in the Haram.
D) Three: one for each sanctity plus a penalty for the combination.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses istihsan to resolve the conflict between two sanctities, giving one penalty for a muhrim in the Haram; internally, the relied position is that a sacrificial animal suffices for a halal even if of lesser value.

The Ihtirazi Nature of 'Halal' and the Muhrim's Option to Fast
Explains ihtirazi restriction and muhrim's fasting option.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the halal and muhrim in the Hanafi ruling on expiation for game in the Haram and explain why the text restricts the ruling to 'halal'.

Core Idea
The restriction to 'halal' is ihtirazi: it excludes the muhrim, who may fast, whereas the halal may not.

In the chapter on hunting in the Haram, the author of Kanz al-Daqaiq states that the halal cannot fast as expiation. This lesson unpacks why the text specifies 'halal'—it is a precautionary restriction to avoid applying the same rule to the muhrim, who has a different ruling. We will explore the dispute with Zufar and the istihsan reasoning behind the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key phrase
The original text says 'halal' is restricted. Recognize that this is not accidental but a deliberate ihtirazi qualification.
The commentator stresses that the restriction serves to exclude the muhrim.
2
State the ruling for each category
For the halal, fasting does not suffice; only dam or it'am. For the muhrim, fasting is valid along with the other options.
3
Locate the dispute
Zufar held that fasting suffices even for the halal. The majority (three imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) disagree.
The commentator mentions possible dual narrations from Zufar.
4
Understand the proof
The istihsan reasoning: when two sanctities (ihram and haram) conflict, the stronger (ihram) is given precedence, so the muhrim can fast.
This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
5
Apply the principle
If a muhrim kills game in the Haram, he fulfills expiation by any of the three options; a halal cannot fast.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والظاهر أن قيد (احترازاي أي التقييد بالحلال للاحتراز عن المحرم، فإن المحرم مخير كما مر متناً في أول هذا الفصل بخلاف الحلال فإنه لا يجزئه الصوم كما علمت. وفي عزوه المسألة إلى الهداية إيهام أنها لم تذكر هنا. وفي اللباب وأما الصوم في صيد الحرم فلا يجوز للحلال ويجوز للمحرم ا هـ . نعم عبارة المصنف أول الفصل مطلقة يمكن تقييدها بصيد المحرم في غير الحرم فلذا لم يعز إليها. وفي شرح اللباب قال في شرح القدوري : إن الإطعام يجزئ في صيد الحرم ولا يجوز الصوم عند علمائنا الثلاثة وعند زفر يجزئ ، وفي المختلف لا يجوز الصوم بالإجماع. قال صاحب المجمع فيجوز أن يكون في الصوم عن زفر روايتان فنقل كل واحد رواية، في | الحلال، أما المحرم فظاهر كلامهم أنه يجوز له الصوم والهدي بلا خلاف لأنه لما اجتمع حرمة الإحرام والحرم وتعذر الجمع بينهما وجب اعتبار أقواهما وهو الإحرام فأضيف إليه ورتب عليه أحكامه ضرورة، وبه صرح في شرح القدوري فقال: أما المحرم إذا قتل في الحرم فإنه تتأدى كفارته بالصوم ا هـ وتمامه فيه قوله : (وليس مقصودة تقييد الضمان بالذبح الخ نظر فيه في النهر بأن بتقديره ثم هذا
His saying: (And it is apparent that the restriction is precautionary) i.e., the restriction to 'halal' is to exclude the muhrim. For the muhrim has a choice, as mentioned earlier in the chapter text, unlike the halal for whom fasting does not suffice, as you learned. And attributing the issue to al-Hidayah gives the impression that it was not mentioned here. In al-Lubab: 'As for fasting in the case of game of the Haram, it is not permissible for the halal, but it is permissible for the muhrim.' Yes, the wording of the author at the beginning of the chapter is absolute, and could be restricted to game of a muhrim outside the Haram, so he did not attribute it to it. In Sharh al-Lubab, he said in Sharh al-Quduri: 'Feeding suffices in game of the Haram, and fasting is not permissible according to our three imams; according to Zufar, it suffices. And in al-Mukhtalaf, fasting is not permissible by consensus.' The author of al-Majma' said: 'It is possible that there are two narrations from Zufar about fasting, so each one transmitted a narration.' As for the halal, for the muhrim, the apparent position of the scholars is that fasting and offering a sacrificial animal are permissible without dispute, because when the sanctity of ihram and the Haram come together and combination is impossible, the stronger (ihram) must be considered, so it is attributed to it and its rulings are applied out of necessity. This is clearly stated in Sharh al-Quduri: 'As for the muhrim if he kills in the Haram, his expiation is fulfilled by fasting.' The rest is therein. His saying: (And his intention is not to restrict the guarantee to slaughter only...) there is consideration in al-Nahr with an estimation. Then this.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a commentary clarifying why the original author restricted the ruling to 'halal'. It explains that this restriction is precautionary (ihtirazi) to indicate that the muhrim is excluded because his ruling differs: a muhrim has the option to fast, while a halal does not. The passage surveys various Hanafi texts (al-Hidayah, al-Lubab, Sharh al-Quduri) and mentions a disagreement with Zufar, who held that fasting is permissible for a halal, though the Hanafi consensus among the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is that it is not. The commentator then reiterates the istihsan reasoning: when both sanctities (ihram and haram) conflict, the stronger (ihram) prevails, so the muhrim can fast. This is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
احترازي (ihtirazi): A qualification in legal texts that serves to exclude a known exception.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the author intended to confuse the reader.
B) To exclude the muhrim from the ruling that fasting is not allowed.
C) To indicate that only halal persons are addressed.
D) Because the muhrim is not mentioned elsewhere.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between the halal and muhrim in expiation for game in the Haram: the halal cannot fast, but the muhrim may, due to istihsan.

Guarantee for Game in Haram: Direct and Indirect Causation
Expands guarantee for Haram game to indirect acts and parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for guarantee of game in the Haram and differentiate between liable and non-liable indirect causation.

Core Idea
Guarantee for Haram game applies to direct and indirect acts, but indirect acts are only liable if wrongful.

The sacred precinct of the Haram extends protection to its game; harming it incurs a guarantee (daman). This passage from al-Muhit clarifies that liability arises not only from direct killing but also from indirect acts and even mere possession, as long as the act is wrongful. It also addresses the important nuance that if the indirect act is obligatory (like releasing a falcon for falconry), it does not trigger guarantee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act of destruction (itlaf)
Determine whether the act directly or indirectly caused the death or injury of game in the Haram. Both direct and indirect acts can incur guarantee.
Indirect causation (tasabbub) requires the intermediary act to be wrongful (udwan).
2
Classify the nature of the causal link
Decide if the act was direct (mubasharah) or indirect (tasabbub). For indirect, assess whether the cause was wrongful.
The text gives examples: removing game from Haram (wrongful) vs. releasing a falcon to hunt (performing an obligation, hence not wrongful).
3
Apply the conditions of safety (amn)
Game is only in a state of safety if three conditions are met: hunter's ihram, game inside Haram, and hunter inside Haram. If any is missing, the game is not 'safe' and guarantee may not apply.
Zufar disagrees on the third condition; Hanafi position holds that entering Haram alone prohibits hunting.
4
Consider parts of game
Parts of game (egg, milk, wound) are treated like the whole. Breaking an egg or wounding the animal incurs guarantee.
The text explicitly states wounding is guaranteed, and the part is considered with the whole.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال في المحيط : ومن أخرج صيداً من الحرم يرده إلى مأمنه فإن أرسله في الحل ضمنه لأنه أزال أمنه بالإخراج فما لم يعده إلى مأمنه بإرساله في الحرم لا يبرأ الضمان اهـ. فعلم أن المراد بالذبح إتلافه حقيقة أو حكماً، ولا فرق في الإتلاف بين المباشرة والتسبب بشرط أن يكون التسبب عدواناً كما قدمناه في صيد المحرم ولهذا قال في المحيط هنا : ولو أدخل المحرم بازياً فأرسله فقتل حمام الحرم لم يضمن لأنه أقام واجباً وما قصد الاصطياد فلم يكن متعدياً في السبب بل كان مأموراً به فلا يضمن انتهى. فعلم بهذا أن صيد الحرم يضمن بالمباشرة وبالتسبب ووضع اليد حتى لو وضع يده على صيد الحرم فتلف بآفة سماوية فإنه يكون ضامناً كما سيأتي صريحاً في الكتاب. والصيد يضمن على المحرم بهذه الثلاثة أيضاً ويزاد عليها رابع وهو الإعانة على قتله حتى لو أحرم وفي يده حقيقة صيد فلم يرسله حتى هلك بآفة سماوية لزمه جزاؤه كما صرح به في فتح القدير، ولم أر من صرح بحكم جزء صيد الحرم كبيضه ولبنه ولعله لفهمه من صيد الحرم فإنه لا شك أن الجزء معتبر بالكل. فإذا كسر بيض صيد الحرم أو جرحه ضمن ثم رأيت التصريح في المحيط بأن جراحته مضمونة فقال : حلال جرح صيداً في الحرم فزادت قيمته من شعر أو بدن ثم مات من الجراحة فعليه ما نقصته الجراحة وقيمته يوم مات وتمام تفاريعه فيه . وأطلق المصنف في صيد الحرم فشمل ما إذا كان الصيد في الحرم والصائد في الحل أو عكسه وقد صرحوا به. قال في المحيط : ثم الصيد إنما يصير آمناً بثلاثة أشياء : بإحرام الصائد وبدخول الصيد الحرم وبدخول الصائد في الحرم، وفي الأخير خلاف زفر ونحن نقول : إن الداخل للحرم يحرم عليه الاصطياد مطلقاً كما يحرم بالإحرام. والعبرة لقوائم الصيد لا لرأسه حتى لو كان بعض قوائمه في الحل
And he said in al-Muhit: 'Whoever removes game from the Haram must return it to its safe place; if he releases it in the Halal, he is liable because he removed its safety by taking it out. So as long as he does not return it to its safe place by releasing it in the Haram, the guarantee is not discharged.' So it is understood that what is meant by 'slaughter' is destruction in reality or in ruling. And there is no difference in destruction between direct and indirect causation, provided that the indirect cause is wrongful, as we presented earlier in the case of a muhrim's game. For this reason, he said in al-Muhit here: 'If a muhrim brought in a falcon and released it, and it killed pigeons of the Haram, he is not liable because he performed an obligatory act and did not intend to hunt, so he was not wrongful in the cause; rather, he was commanded to do it, so he is not liable.' So it is known that game of the Haram is guaranteed by direct action, indirect causation, and by placing a hand (possession). So much so that if one places his hand on game of the Haram and it perishes by a heavenly affliction, he is liable, as will come explicitly in the book. And game is guaranteed against the muhrim by these three as well, and a fourth is added: assistance in killing it. So if a person enters ihram while having actual game in his hand and does not release it until it dies by a heavenly affliction, its compensation is due from him, as clearly stated in Fath al-Qadir. I have not seen anyone explicitly state the ruling on a part of game of the Haram, like its egg or milk, perhaps because it is understood from 'game of the Haram'; there is no doubt that the part is considered with the whole. So if one breaks an egg of game of the Haram or wounds it, he is liable. Then I saw an explicit statement in al-Muhit that wounding it is guaranteed. He said: 'A halal person wounded a game in the Haram, and its value increased in feathers or body, then it died from the wound. He owes the amount its value decreased due to the wound and its value on the day it died.' The full details are in it. And the author spoke absolutely about game of the Haram, covering both when the game is in the Haram and the hunter in the Halal, or the opposite. They explicitly stated this. He said in al-Muhit: 'Then the game only becomes safe by three things: by the ihram of the hunter, by the game entering the Haram, and by the hunter entering the Haram. In the last, there is a difference with Zufar. We say: the one who enters the Haram is absolutely prohibited from hunting, just as he is prohibited by ihram. Consideration is given to the legs of the game, not its head, so much so that if some of its legs are in the Halal,'
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the guarantee (daman) for game in the Haram. It expands on the concept of 'destruction' (itlaf) by stating that it includes both direct and indirect causation, provided the indirect cause is wrongful (udwan). It quotes from al-Muhit to illustrate: if one removes game from the Haram and releases it outside, he is liable until he returns it to safety; if a muhrim releases a falcon that kills game, he is not liable because he was performing an obligation (releasing the falcon for hunting is not intended) and was not wrongful. The passage then lists three ways guarantee applies: direct action, indirect causation, and placing a hand (possession). For muhrim, a fourth is added: assistance in killing. The commentator notes that parts of game (egg, milk) are also covered by the guarantee, citing al-Muhit for the case of wounding. The passage also discusses the three conditions that make game 'safe' (amn): the hunter's ihram, the game entering the Haram, and the hunter entering the Haram. It mentions a disagreement with Zufar regarding the third condition, but the Hanafi position is that entering the Haram itself prohibits hunting. Finally, it notes that consideration is given to the game's legs (if they are in the Haram or Halal) not its head.

Key Terms
التسبب (al-tasabbub): Indirect causation; bringing about the destruction through an intermediary act.
الأمن (al-amn): The state of safety for game, achieved by three conditions: hunter's ihram, game entering Haram, hunter entering Haram.
المباشرة (al-mubasharah): Direct causation; acting directly upon the game causing destruction.
المأمن (al-maman): The safe place; the area where the game is secure (inside Haram for Haram game).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Yes, because he caused the death.
B) No, because he did not intend to hunt and was performing an obligation.
C) Yes, because the falcon is his property.
D) No, because the game was not in the Haram.

Key Takeaway
Guarantee for Haram game covers direct and indirect acts, but indirect acts only incur liability if they are wrongful (udwan); performing an obligatory act that leads to harm is not wrongful.

Liability of a Muhrim for Killing Game and Directing Others
States the ruling for Muhrim killing game and distinguishes liability for directing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a Muhrim who kills game, apply the qiyas to the case of directing, and distinguish liability based on ihram commitment.

Core Idea
A Muhrim who kills or directs to game is liable; a Halal is not, because liability follows the commitment of ihram.

This passage from Bahar al-Raiq clarifies the Hanafi ruling for a person in ihram (Muhrim) who kills game in the Haram. It also addresses the subtle case where a Muhrim directs someone else to the game, using a qiyas (analogy) to a depositee betraying trust. We will unpack the ruling, the proof, and the reasoning that distinguishes a Muhrim from a non-Muhrim in liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage discusses two situations: (1) Muhrim directly kills game, (2) Muhrim or Halal directs another to game. Identify the ruling for each.
The ruling for direct killing is clearly wajib compensation; for directing, liability depends on the status of the director.
2
State the compensation ruling
For the Muhrim who kills, compensation is wajib with three options: sacrificing an animal (hady), feeding the poor (it'am), or fasting (sawm). This is based on Qur'an 5:95.
The three options are a choice; the person may select any.
3
Analyze the qiyas for directing
The author analogizes a Muhrim directing someone to game to a depositee directing a thief to the deposit. The effective cause (illa) is the violation of a commitment (iltizam).
The Muhrim undertook to refrain from hunting; directing breaks that undertaking.
4
Distinguish the Halal
A Halal (non-Muhrim) has no such commitment to refrain from hunting, so even if he directs a Muhrim to game, he is not liable.
The Halal is like a stranger who directs a thief to someone's property — no trust betrayed.
5
Extract the principle
Liability for directing hinges on the existence of a prior undertaking (iltizam). Causation alone does not create liability; the breach of a specific duty does.
This principle can apply in other fiqh areas where a person's special status creates obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج فصل إن قتل محرم صيداً لأن المحرم تلزمه قيمة يخير فيها بين الهدي والإطعام والصوم كما صرح به في النهاية في صيد المحرم في الحرم. وقيد بذبح الحلال لأنه لو دل إنساناً على صيد الحرم فإنه لا يلزمه شيء ولو كان المدلول محرماً، والفرق بين دلالة المحرم ودلالة الحلال أن المحرم التزم ترك التعرض بالإحرام فلما دل ترك ما التزمه فضمن كالمودع إذا دل السارق على الوديعة ولا التزام الحلال فلا ضمان بها كالأجنبي إذا دل السارق على مال إنسان والتحقيق أن الضمان على المحرم جزاء الفعل والدلالة فعل وعلى الحلال في صيد الحرم جزاء المحل، وفي الدلالة لم يتصل بالمحل شيء وليس مقصوده تقييد الضمان بالذبح فقط لأنه سيصرح آخر الفصل أن من أخرج ظبية الحرم فإنه يضمنها.
Book of Hajj, Chapter: If a Muhrim kills game. Because the Muhrim is liable for a value in which he has a choice between sacrifice, feeding, and fasting, as clarified in al-Nihayah regarding the game of a Muhrim in the Haram. And it is restricted by the slaughter of a Halal (non-Muhrim), because if a person directs someone to the game of the Haram, nothing is incumbent upon him, even if the one directed is a Muhrim. The difference between the direction of a Muhrim and the direction of a Halal is that the Muhrim undertook to refrain from attacking by virtue of ihram, so when he directed, he abandoned what he undertook, so he becomes liable, like a depositee if he directs a thief to the deposit. The Halal has no undertaking, so no liability for him, like a stranger if he directs a thief to someone's property. The verification is that liability upon the Muhrim is a penalty for the act, and directing is an act. Upon the Halal regarding the game of the Haram is the penalty of the non-Muhrim, and in directing, nothing is connected to the game. And his intention is not to restrict liability to slaughter only, because he will clarify at the end of the chapter that whoever takes out a doe from the Haram is liable for it.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on a Muhrim killing game. It first states the ruling that a Muhrim must pay compensation (fidyah) with a choice between three options: sacrificing an animal (hady), feeding the poor (it'am), or fasting (sawm). This is based on Qur'anic injunction (al-Ma'idah 5:95). The author then clarifies a restriction: the phrase 'slaughter by a Halal' is a restriction (qayd). He explains that if a Halal person (non-Muhrim) directs someone to game in the Haram, he is not liable, even if the one directed is a Muhrim. The reasoning is that a Muhrim has taken a commitment to refrain from hunting, so if he directs, he violates that commitment, analogous to a depositee who betrays trust. A Halal has no such commitment, so no liability. The underlying principle is that liability on the Muhrim is for the act of causing the killing, while on the Halal it is for the location (the Haram). But in merely directing, the Halal does not directly affect the game.

Key Terms
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, prohibited from hunting.
حلال (halal): A person not in the state of ihram; a non-Muhrim.
دلالة (dalalah): Directing or indicating the location of game to someone else.
المودع (al-mudi'): A depositee, someone entrusted with another's property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because directing is not considered an act.

Key Takeaway
A Muhrim's liability for killing or directing to game arises from violating his ihram commitment, unlike a Halal who has no such commitment.

Liability for Game in the Haram and Forms of Causation
Explains liability for removing game from the Haram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four modes of liability for game in the Haram and explain the condition that causation must be wrongful to incur liability.

Core Idea
Removing game from the Haram creates liability; Muhrims face four modes: direct, causal, possession, assistance.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on the liability for game within the Haram. It clarifies that destruction of game, whether by direct action or indirect causation, incurs liability provided the causation is wrongful. The text also distinguishes between the general liability for game in the Haram and the specific additional mode for a Muhrim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on removing game from the Haram
Note that anyone who removes game from the Haram must return it to a safe place; releasing it outside incurs liability because safety was removed.
The ruling is about restoring the game's safety.
2
Extract the three common modes of liability for Haram game
The text lists direct action (mubasharah), causation (tasabbub), and possession (wad' al-yad) as grounds for liability for any person.
Causation must be wrongful ('udwan).
3
Identify the fourth mode specific to a Muhrim
For a person in ihram, a fourth mode is added: assistance (i'anah) in killing, even without direct causation or possession.
This is illustrated by the case of a Muhrim who holds game and fails to release it.
4
Understand the nuance of wrongful causation vs. commanded act
The falcon example shows that if a Muhrim releases a falcon to perform an obligatory duty (e.g., scaring pests), and it kills game, there is no liability because the act was commanded, not wrongful.
Intention and justificiation matter.
5
Apply the rules to a hypothetical
Consider a Muhrim who shouts at a deer causing it to fall. Determine liability based on whether the causation was wrongful or commanded.
If the shouting was unnecessary and intended to harm, liability arises.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال في المحيط : ومن أخرج صيداً من الحرم يرده إلى مأمنه فإن أرسله في الحل ضمنه لأنه أزال أمنه بالإخراج فما لم يعده إلى مأمنه بإرساله في الحرم لا يبرأ الضمان اهـ. فعلم أن المراد بالذبح إتلافه حقيقة أو حكماً، ولا فرق في الإتلاف بين المباشرة والتسبب بشرط أن يكون التسبب عدواناً كما قدمناه في صيد المحرم ولهذا قال في المحيط هنا : ولو أدخل المحرم بازياً فأرسله فقتل حمام الحرم لم يضمن لأنه أقام واجباً وما قصد الاصطياد فلم يكن متعدياً في السبب بل كان مأموراً به فلا يضمن انتهى. فعلم بهذا أن صيد الحرم يضمن بالمباشرة وبالتسبب ووضع اليد حتى لو وضع يده على صيد الحرم فتلف بآفة سماوية فإنه يكون ضامناً كما سيأتي صريحاً في الكتاب. والصيد يضمن على المحرم بهذه الثلاثة أيضاً ويزاد عليها رابع وهو الإعانة على قتله حتى لو أحرم وفي يده حقيقة صيد فلم يرسله حتى هلك بآفة سماوية لزمه جزاؤه كما صرح به في فتح القدير.
And he said in al-Muhit: Whoever takes out game from the Haram must return it to its safe place. If he releases it in the Halal (outside), he is liable because he removed its safety by taking it out. So unless he returns it to its safe place by releasing it in the Haram, he is not free from liability. So it is known that what is meant by 'slaughter' is destruction actually or constructively. And there is no difference in destruction between direct action and causation, provided the causation is wrongful, as we have presented in the game of the Muhrim. Hence he said in al-Muhit here: If a Muhrim brings in a falcon and releases it and it kills a pigeon of the Haram, he is not liable because he performed an obligatory act and did not intend to hunt, so he was not wrongful in the cause, but rather was commanded, so no liability. So it is known from this that game of the Haram is liable by direct action, by causation, and by possession (placing a hand), such that if he places his hand on game of the Haram and it perishes by a heavenly affliction, he is liable, as will come explicitly in the book. And game is liable upon the Muhrim by these three as well, and a fourth is added: assistance in killing, such that if he enters ihram and in his hand is a real game and he does not release it until it perishes by a heavenly affliction, he is liable for its compensation, as clarified in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage discusses the liability for game in the Haram. It first cites al-Muhit: anyone who removes game from the Haram must return it to a safe place (maman); if they release it outside, they are liable because they removed its safety. The ruling applies whether the destruction is direct (e.g., slaughter) or indirect (causation), as long as the causation is wrongful (udwan). However, if a Muhrim brings a falcon and releases it to perform an obligatory duty (like scaring birds from crops), and the falcon kills a pigeon, he is not liable because his intention was not to hunt and his action was commanded. The passage then states that liability for game in the Haram arises from three things: direct action (mubasharah), causing (tasabbub), and possession (wad' al-yad). For a Muhrim, a fourth is added: assistance (i'anah) in killing. For example, if a person enters ihram while holding game and does not release it until it dies naturally, he must pay compensation.

Key Terms
مأمن (ma'man): Safe place; the sanctuary where the game is protected.
تسبّب (tasabbub): Causation; indirect action that leads to destruction.
عُدوان (udwan): Wrongful, transgressive act; here, causing harm without justification.
وضع اليد (wad' al-yad): Physical possession or control over the game.
إعانة (i'anah): Assistance in killing; helping to cause the death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what are the four ways a Muhrim can become liable for game in the Haram?
A) Direct action, causation, possession, and assistance.
B) Slaughter, hunting, trapping, and cooking.
C) Shooting, stabbing, strangling, and poisoning.
D) Caging, selling, releasing, and eating.

Key Takeaway
Liability for game in the Haram arises from direct action, causation (if wrongful), possession, and for a Muhrim additionally from assistance in killing; the condition of 'udwan is crucial.

Liability for Parts of Game and the Criterion for 'In the Haram'
Ruling on parts and location criterion for game in Haram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle that the part follows the whole for liability, and apply the feet-based criterion to determine whether killing game incurs a penalty in the Haram.

Core Idea
The part follows the whole; a game is in the Haram if its feet are inside, not its head.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two interconnected issues: Are you liable for harming parts of game such as eggs or milk in the Haram? And how exactly do you determine if an animal is considered 'in the Haram'? The author first notes a gap in the literature, then uses the principle that the part is like the whole. He then clarifies that the decisive factor is the animal's feet, not its head, and derives practical consequences for hunting near the Haram boundary. The discussion also includes a minority intra-Hanafi view from Zufar regarding the hunter entering the Haram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue for parts of game
Recognize that the text first discusses liability for harming parts of game like eggs and milk. The principle is that the part is considered by the whole (الجزء معتبر بالكل), so any harm to a part incurs the same liability as harming the whole animal.
This is an a priori ruling; the author found explicit support in al-Muhit.
2
Locate the definition of 'safe' (amin) in the Haram
The text states that game becomes 'safe' (آمناً) by three factors: the hunter's ihram, the game entering the Haram, or the hunter entering the Haram. The last factor is contested by Zufar.
The Hanafi position is that entering the Haram itself prohibits hunting absolutely.
3
Apply the feet criterion
The decisive criterion for whether a game is in the Haram is its feet (قوائم), not its head. If any foot is in the Haram, the penalty applies; if all feet are in the Halal, even if the head is in the Haram, no penalty.
This is based on the principle of giving priority to prohibition over permissibility.
4
Derive rulings from the criterion
Apply the rule to specific cases: if the game is lying on the ground with its head in the Haram but body in the Halal, the penalty applies because it is not standing in the Halal. Shooting from the Halal into the Haram incurs no penalty for the hunter. The same applies to releasing a dog or falcon.
These derivations follow logically from the feet criterion.
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute with Zufar
Zufar held that a hunter entering the Haram without ihram is not prohibited from hunting, unlike the mainstream Hanafi view. The pragmatic consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that under Zufar's view, a person could hunt in the Haram if not in ihram, whereas the Hanafi position forbids it absolutely.
The Hanafi view is the mufta bihi (relied-upon position).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم أر من صرح بحكم جزء صيد الحرم كبيضه ولبنه ولعله لفهمه من صيد الحرم فإنه لا شك أن الجزء معتبر بالكل. فإذا كسر بيض صيد الحرم أو جرحه ضمن ثم رأيت التصريح في المحيط بأن جراحته مضمونة فقال : حلال جرح صيداً في الحرم فزادت قيمته من شعر أو بدن ثم مات من الجراحة فعليه ما نقصته الجراحة وقيمته يوم مات وتمام تفاريعه فيه . وأطلق المصنف في صيد الحرم فشمل ما إذا كان الصيد في الحرم والصائد في الحل أو عكسه وقد صرحوا به. قال في المحيط : ثم الصيد إنما يصير آمناً بثلاثة أشياء : بإحرام الصائد وبدخول الصيد الحرم وبدخول الصائد في الحرم، وفي الأخير خلاف زفر ونحن نقول : إن الداخل للحرم يحرم عليه الاصطياد مطلقاً كما يحرم بالإحرام. والعبرة لقوائم الصيد لا لرأسه حتى لو كان بعض قوائمه في الحل ورأسه في الحرم فلا شيء عليه في قتله ولا يشترط أن تكون جميع قوائمه في الحرم حتى لو كان بعض قوائمه في الحرم وبعضها في الحل وجب الجزاء بقتله لتغليب الخطر على الإباحة، ولهذا لو كان الصيد ملقى على الأرض في الحل ورأسه في الحرم وجب الجزاء بقتله لأنه ليس بقائم في الحل وبعضه في الحرم. وبما ذكرنا علم أنه لو رمى إلى صيد من الحل في الحل غير السهم في الحرم فإنه لا شيء عليه، وكذلك حكم الكلب والبازي إذا أرسلهما كما الأسبيجابي.
And I have not seen anyone who explicitly stated the ruling on a part of the game of the Haram, like its egg and its milk; perhaps because it is understood from 'game of the Haram' that there is no doubt that the part is considered by the whole. So if one breaks the egg of game of the Haram or wounds it, he is liable. Then I saw explicit statement in al-Muhit that its wound is liable: 'A Halal wounded a game in the Haram, and its value increased in hair or body, then it died from the wound; he is liable for the decrease by the wound and its value on the day it died, and all its subdivisions are there.' And the author gave an absolute ruling on game of the Haram, encompassing whether the game is in the Haram and the hunter in the Halal or vice versa, and they have explicitly stated it. He said in al-Muhit: 'Then the game only becomes safe (amins) by three things: by the ihram of the hunter, by the game entering the Haram, and by the hunter entering the Haram. In the last, there is a difference from Zufar. We say that the one who enters the Haram is prohibited from hunting absolutely, just as it is prohibited by ihram. And the consideration is for the legs of the game, not its head, such that if some of its legs are in the Halal and its head is in the Haram, then there is nothing upon him for killing it. And it is not required that all its legs be in the Haram; such that if some of its legs are in the Haram and some in the Halal, the penalty is obligatory for killing it, due to giving priority to prohibition over permissibility. Hence if the game is lying on the ground in the Halal with its head in the Haram, the penalty is obligatory for killing it, because it is not standing in the Halal with part of it in the Haram. And from what we have mentioned, it is known that if one shoots at a game from the Halal in the Halal, and the arrow goes into the Haram, then there is nothing upon him. And the same ruling applies to a dog and a falcon if he sends them, as in al-Asbijabi.'
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
The author first notes a gap in the literature: no explicit ruling exists for parts of game like eggs or milk, but logically the part follows the whole. He then discovers that al-Muhit explicitly states that wounding game in the Haram is liable, including for changes in value. Next, he explains the definition of when game is considered in the Haram. An animal becomes safe (amin) due to three factors: the hunter's ihram, the animal's entry into the Haram, or the hunter's entry into the Haram. According to the Hanafis, a person entering the Haram is prohibited from hunting just as if in ihram, contrary to Zufar. The key criterion for the animal's location is its feet: if its feet are in the Halal, even if its head is in the Haram, no penalty for killing it. But if any foot is in the Haram, the penalty applies, giving priority to the prohibition. If the animal is lying down with head only in Haram, the penalty applies because its body is not entirely in the Halal. From this, it follows that shooting from the Halal with the arrow entering the Haram incurs no penalty, and similarly for releasing a dog or falcon.

Key Terms
جزء (juz'): Part of the game, such as an egg or milk.
قوائم (qawa'im): The legs or feet of the animal; the basis for determining location in Haram.
آمناً (aminan): Safe, under the protection of the Haram; game is secure from hunting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the criterion for a game to be considered in the Haram for liability purposes?
A) Its head being inside the Haram.
B) Its entire body being inside the Haram.
C) Its feet (legs) being inside the Haram.
D) Whether the hunter is in ihram.

Key Takeaway
Liability for parts follows from the whole; the location of a game in the Haram is determined by its feet, not its head, and entering the Haram prohibits hunting absolutely.
