قدمنا أن الصيد يصير بواحد من ثلاثة، وقد يقال لما خرج من الحرم لم يبق واحد من فحل له، ويجاب بأن الكلام في حل سعيه في الحرم مع أن المقصود بالسعي أمن. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية وغيرها ومقدار الحرم من قبل المشرق ستة أميال، ومن الجانب الثاني اثنا عشر ميلاً، ومن الجانب الثالث ثمانية عشر ميلاً، ومن الجانب الرابع أربعة وعشرون ميلاً، هكذا قال الفقيه أبو جعفر، وهذا شيء لا يعرف قياساً وإنما يعرف نقلاً. قال الصدر الشهيد فيما قاله نظر فإن من الجانب الثاني ميقات العمرة وهو التنعيم وهذا قريب من ثلاثة أميال ا هـ. وذكر الإمام النووي في شرح المهذب أن حده من جهة المدينة دون التنعيم على ثلاثة أميال مكة، ومن طريق اليمن على سبعة أميال من مكة ومن طريق الطائف على عرفات من بطن نمرة على سبعة أميال، ومن طريق العراق على ثنية جبل بالمقطع على سبعة أميال، ومن طريق الجعرانة في شعب أبي عبد الله خالد بن على تسعة أميال، ومن طريق جدة على عشرة أميال من مكة وأن عليه علامات منصوبة في جميع جوانبه نصبها إبراهيم الخليل عليه السلام وكان جبريل يريه مواضعها ثم أمر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بتجديدها ثم ثم الله عثمان ثم معاوية رضي عنهم وهي إلى الآن بينة وقد جمعها القاضي أبو الفضل النويري فقال : و للحرم التحديد من أرض طيبة ثلاثة أميال إذا رمت إتقانه عمر بيضه . ثم رأيت المسألة مصرحاً بها في متن اللباب فقال : لو ماتا ضمن الفرخ لا الأم قوله : (إن قلنا إن إمساكه عن فرخه معصية) في بعض النسخ عن الحل بدل قوله عن فرخه» ولم يظهر لي معناه . وإنما قيد بذلك لما قدمه أن السبب كالمباشرة بشرط كونه عدواناً قوله : (ومنها لو وقف على غصن في الحل الخ) قال في النهر في السراج لو كان الرامي في الحرم والصيد في الحل أو على العكس فهو من صيد الحرم، ولو رمى إلى صيد في الحل فنفر فأصابه في الحرم فعليه الجزاء، ولو أصابه في الحل ومات في الحرم يحل أكله قياساً ويكره استحساناً اهـ. قوله : (ومنها لو رأى حلال جالس في الحرم الخ) قال في النهر : لا ينبغي أن يتوقف في الجواز إذ لا منع ثمة قوله : (ومن يمن سبع إلى آخر وسبعة أميال عراق وطائف وجدة عشر ثم تسع جعرانه حرم ومن يمن سبع بتقديم سينها وقد كملت فاشكر لربك إحسانه
The Book of Hajj: Chapter: If a pilgrim kills game - safe in the sanctuary, then the chick dies, and it should be that he is liable for the chick because it is from the game of the sanctuary and he caused its death if we say that preventing it from its chick is a sin. And among them: if he stood on a branch in the outer precinct while the tree's root is in the sanctuary and he shot at game in the outer precinct, or the branch was in the sanctuary and the tree and game in the outer precinct, and it should be that the one standing on the branch has the same ruling as the bird if it was on the branch, so no liability in the first case and liability in the second. And among them: if he brought in something of birds of prey and it destroyed something not by its action, and it should be that if he did not send it and it destroyed, he is liable, but if he sent it, we have previously mentioned from al-Muhit that there is no liability. And among them: if a non-muhrim sitting in the sanctuary saw game in the outer precinct, is it permissible for him to intend [to go] towards it to kill it in the outer precinct? And we have previously mentioned that game becomes [protected] by one of three [reasons]. It could be said: when it left the sanctuary, none of the [reasons] remains that would permit him [to hunt it]. And the answer is that the discussion is about the permissibility of his pursuit in the sanctuary while the purpose of pursuit is safety. And in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya and others: The extent of the sanctuary from the east side is six miles, from the second side twelve miles, from the third side eighteen miles, from the fourth side twenty-four miles. Thus said al-Faqih Abu Ja'far, and this is not known by analogy but known by transmission. Al-Sadr al-Shahid said: In what he said there is consideration, for from the second side is the miqat of 'Umra, which is al-Tan'im, and that is close to three miles. And Imam al-Nawawi mentioned in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab that its boundary from the direction of Medina is before al-Tan'im at three miles from Mecca, from the Yemen road at seven miles from Mecca, from the Ta'if road at 'Arafat from Batn Namira at seven miles, from the Iraq road at Thaniyya Jabal al-Muqta' at seven miles, from the Ji'rana road in Shi'b Abi 'Abdillah Khalid ibn 'Ali at nine miles, from the Jeddah road at ten miles from Mecca, and that there are markers erected on all its sides that Ibrahim al-Khalil set up, and Jibril would show him their locations, then the Prophet ordered their renewal, then 'Uthman, then Mu'awiya (may Allah be pleased with them), and they are still evident until now. And al-Qadi Abu al-Fadl al-Nuwayri compiled them and said: 'For the sanctuary the boundary from the land of Tayba (is) three miles, if you want to perfect it ...' Then I saw the issue explicitly stated in Matn al-Lubab: He said: 'If both die, the chick is liable, not the mother.' He said: (If we say that preventing it from its chick is a sin) in some copies: 'from the outer precinct' instead of 'from its chick', and I did not see its meaning. He only conditioned it because of what was previously mentioned: that the cause is like direct action with the condition that it be transgression. He said: (And among them: if he stood on a branch in the outer precinct...) He said in al-Nahr from al-Siraj: If the shooter was in the sanctuary and the game in the outer precinct or vice versa, it is from the game of the sanctuary. If he shot at game in the outer precinct and it fled and was hit in the sanctuary, he owes the penalty. If it was hit in the outer precinct and died in the sanctuary, it is permissible to eat it by analogy and it is makruh by istihsan. He said: (And among them: if a non-muhrim sitting in the sanctuary saw game...) He said in al-Nahr: It should not be hesitated in permissibility since there is no prohibition there. He said: (And from Yemen seven to the end: And seven miles [for] 'Iraq and Ta'if and Jeddah ten, then nine for Ji'rana, sanctuary, and from Yemen seven with its sin [letter] advanced, and it is complete, so thank your Lord for His favor.)
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter concerning a pilgrim killing game. The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) expands on rulings from the original matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq). The first part deals with various scenarios: (1) If a pilgrim kills a mother bird and her chick dies as a result, the pilgrim is liable for the chick only if preventing the mother from her chick is considered a transgression. (2) If a person stands on a branch in the hal (outside Haram) but the tree's root is in the Haram, or vice versa, the liability depends on where the bird is when killed. (3) If someone brings a bird of prey into the Haram and it kills something not by his command, he is liable only if he did not send it; if he sent it, no liability according to al-Muhit. (4) If a non-muhrim sitting in the Haram sees game in the hal, may he go to kill it? The answer is yes, because the game has left the Haram and lost its protection. The commentator then shifts to a discussion of the boundaries of the Haram, citing multiple authorities and a poem by al-Nuwayri. The boundaries vary: from the east 6 miles, from the second side 12 miles, etc., but al-Sadr al-Shahid criticizes this as not matching al-Tan'im. Al-Nawawi gives different measurements from various roads. The commentator concludes by noting that the issue is known by transmission, not analogy.

Key Terms
نقل (naql): Transmission; knowledge based on reports rather than reason.
ميقات (miqat): The designated station for entering ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the text say the Haram boundaries are 'not known by analogy but by transmission'?
A) Because analogical reasoning cannot determine such specific distances.
B) Because the boundaries are secret knowledge.
C) Because analogy would give different results for each side.
D) Because analogy is not used in fiqh.

Key Takeaway
The Haram boundaries are fixed by transmitted reports (naql), not by analogy; al-Nawawi's measurements are the most relied-upon.

The Eternal Sanctity of Mecca: A Hanafi Stance
Historical debate on the eternal sanctity of Mecca

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the origin of Mecca's sanctity and identify the opposing view.

Core Idea
Mecca's sanctuary status is eternal, not contingent on Ibrahim's supplication.

Did Mecca become a sanctuary through Prophet Ibrahim's prayer, or was it always sacred? This short passage presents a classical dispute, with the Hanafi school affirming that Mecca has been a sanctified territory since creation. Understanding this helps clarify the basis for the unique rulings of the Haram, such as prohibitions on hunting and cutting trees.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
The passage mentions two views: (1) Mecca became a sanctuary by Ibrahim's request, (2) it was a sanctuary before Ibrahim. Recognize both as the subject of scholarly disagreement.
The first view is attributed to some scholars, the second is the preferred (asahh) view.
2
Recognize the Hanafi preferred view
The text states 'al-asahh' (the most correct) is that Mecca has been sacred from the creation of the heavens and earth. This is the position relied upon in the Hanafi school.
This view is often linked to the verse 'Indeed, the first House established for mankind was that at Bakkah' (Quran 3:96).
3
Understand the basis of the dispute
The dispute stems from interpreting Quranic verses and prophetic traditions. Some scholars see Ibrahim's supplication (Quran 14:35) as the cause of sanctity, while others see it as a declaration of pre-existing sanctity.
The Hanafi reliance on 'asahh' indicates a methodological preference for the view that aligns with the eternity of divine decrees.
4
Note practical implications for fiqh
The ruling affects the status of Mecca's Haram: its inviolability (hurma) is considered perpetual and not subject to change. This underpins the strictness of penalties for violations within the Haram.
Differences in this theological point do not change the fiqh rulings themselves, but reinforce the sanctity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلف العلماء في أن مكة مع حرمها هل صارت حرماً آمناً بسؤال إبراهيم عليه السلام أم كانت قبله كذلك؟ والأصح أنها ما زالت محرمة من حين خلق الله السموات والأرض ا هـ
And the scholars differed concerning Mecca along with its sanctuary: Did it become a secure sanctuary by the request of Ibrahim (peace be upon him) or was it so before him? And the correct view is that it has remained sacred from the time Allah created the heavens and the earth.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This short passage presents a doctrinal dispute about the origin of Mecca's sanctity. The majority view (as stated) is that Mecca has been a sanctuary since creation, not that it became so due to Ibrahim's supplication. This is an inter-madhhab issue but not a fiqh ruling; it pertains to history and theology. The commentator affirms the correct view as per the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
حرم (haram): Sanctuary; a sacred territory with specific legal restrictions (e.g., no hunting, cutting trees).
الأصح (al-asahh): The most correct or sound opinion among multiple scholarly views.
سؤال إبراهيم (su'al Ibrahim): The supplication of Prophet Ibrahim asking Allah to make Mecca a secure sanctuary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct (asahh) view regarding when Mecca became a sanctuary?
A) At the time of Prophet Ibrahim.
B) At the time of Prophet Muhammad.
C) From the creation of the heavens and earth.
D) After the conquest of Mecca.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that Mecca's sanctity is eternal, dating back to creation, not merely a result of Ibrahim's supplication.

Medina Has No Sanctuary in the Hanafi School
Hanafi position that Medina has no Haram status, with hadith rebuttal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on Medina's Haram status and explain the Hanafi rebuttal to hadiths that claim Medina has a sanctuary, using usul al-fiqh principles.

Core Idea
Hanafis hold Medina has no Haram because ahad hadiths on matters of general affliction are rejected.

The question of whether Medina has a sacred sanctuary (Haram) like Mecca is a classical inter-madhhab dispute. While many hadiths seem to prohibit hunting and cutting trees in Medina, the Hanafi school maintains that these prohibitions do not establish a Haram. This lesson examines the key evidence and usul reasoning that lead to the Hanafi conclusion, focusing on a famous hadith about the young boy Abu Umayr and his nightingale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi Position
Read the first sentence of the passage. What does the Hanafi school rule about hunting and cutting trees in Medina?
The ruling is mubah (permissible) because there is no Haram.
2
Analyze the Opposing Evidence
The text mentions that many hadiths in Sahihayn explicitly prohibit these actions. Identify the specific hadith quoted from Sahih Muslim and note its apparent meaning.
The Prophet says he declared Medina sacred between its two lava fields.
3
Examine the Hanafi Rebuttal
The commentator first notes that some Hanafis interpreted 'prohibition' as mere reverence. Then a stronger argument is given: the hadith of Anas about Abu Umayr's nightingale. Explain why this hadith supports the Hanafi view.
The Prophet did not order the release of the bird, indicating no Haram.
4
Understand the Usul Principle
The passage cites al-Muhit's response: the hadiths claiming a Haram are ahad (single-narrator) and the matter is 'umum al-balwa' (general affliction). State why ahad hadiths are not accepted in such cases according to Hanafi usul.
If it were authentic, it would have been widely transmitted.
5
Conclude the Dispute
Summarize the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical difference between the Hanafi and other schools regarding actions in Medina.
Hanafi: hunting and cutting trees are allowed. Others: prohibited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أنه ليس للمدينة حرم عندنا فيجوز الاصطياد فيها وقطع أشجارها وقد وردت أحاديث كثيرة في الصحيحين وغيرها صريحة في تحريم المدينة كمكة وأولها أصحابنا بأن المراد بالتحريم التعظيم ويرده ما ثبت في صحيح مسلم أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال إني حرمت المدينة ما بين لابتيها لا تقطع أغصانها ولا يصاد صيدها فهو صريح في أن لها حرماً كمكة فلا يجوز قطع شجرها ولا الاصطياد فيها والأحسن الاستدلال بحديث أنس الثابت في الصحيحين أنه كان له أخ صغير يقال له أبو عمير وكان له نغير يلعب به فمات النغير فكان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : يا أبا عمير ما فعل النغير؟ ولو كان للمدينة لكان إرساله واجباً عليه ولأنكر عليه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في إمساكه ولا يمازحه. وأجاب في المحيط عن الأحاديث الصحيحة في أن لها حرماً أنها من أخبار الآحاد فيما تعم به البلوى لأن الشجر للمدينة أمر تعم به البلوى وخبر الواحد إذا ورد فيما تعم به البلوى لا يقبل إذ لو كان صحيحاً لاشتهر نقله فيما عم به البلوى ا هـ
Then know that according to us [the Hanafis] there is no sanctuary for Medina, so hunting and cutting its trees are permissible. And many hadiths have been reported in the Sahihayn and others explicitly prohibiting Medina like Mecca. Our scholars initially responded that the intended meaning of prohibition is reverence. But this is refuted by what is established in Sahih Muslim that the Messenger of Allah said: 'I have declared Medina sacred between its two lava fields: its branches should not be cut and its game should not be hunted.' This is explicit that it has a sanctuary like Mecca, so cutting its trees and hunting are not permissible. The better argument is the hadith of Anas established in the Sahihayn that he had a young brother called Abu Umayr who had a nightingale (nughayr) to play with, and the nightingale died, and the Prophet used to say, 'O Abu Umayr, what happened to the nightingale?' If Medina had a sanctuary, it would have been obligatory for him to release it, and the Prophet would have rebuked him for keeping it and would not have joked with him. And al-Muhit answered concerning the authentic hadiths that it has a sanctuary: They are khabar ahad in matters of general affliction (umum al-balwa) because trees in Medina are a matter of general affliction, and khabar ahad when it comes in a matter of general affliction is not accepted, because if it were authentic, its transmission would have become widespread in that matter of general affliction.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position that Medina has no legal sanctuary (Haram). Initially, Hanafis interpreted hadiths prohibiting cutting trees and hunting as merely reverential. However, the explicit hadith in Sahih Muslim seems to contradict that. The commentator then offers a better argument: the hadith of Anas about his nightingale shows that if Medina had sanctuary status, the Prophet would have ordered the release of the bird. But he didn't, so no sanctuary. Then he cites al-Muhit's response: the hadiths claiming sanctuary are ahad, and since the matter is of general affliction (everyone deals with trees), ahad reports are not accepted in such cases. This is a classic Hanafi usul principle.

Key Terms
حرم (haram): Sanctuary where hunting and cutting plants are prohibited.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith transmitted by a single narrator or a few narrators, not reaching tawatur.
عموم البلوى (umum al-balwa): A matter of general affliction, i.e., a situation that occurs frequently and involves many people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Hanafi evidence that Medina does not have a sanctuary?
A) Hadith of the Prophet declaring Medina sacred.
B) The practice of the Companions.
C) The hadith of Anas and the nightingale.
D) Quranic verses.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school maintains that Medina has no Haram, relying on the hadith of Abu Umayr and the usul principle that ahad hadiths in generally afflicting matters are not accepted.

Ruling on Entering the Haram with Game
Ruling that one must release game when entering the Haram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on entering the Haram with game and identify the condition that triggers the obligation to release it.

Core Idea
Game in hand upon entering Haram must be released safely; game in cage or house is exempt.

This passage from Ibn Nujaym's commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies the ruling for anyone entering the sacred precinct of Makkah with game. The key distinction is whether the game is physically held by the person or confined in a cage or house. The release must also be in a manner that ensures the animal's safety, not mere abandonment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
The ruling is that whoever enters the Haram with game must release it. The subject is the person entering, whether muhrim or not.
2
Determine the condition that obligates release
Release is wajib only if the game is in the person's hand (or held by a bird of prey). If in a cage or house, release is not required.
The text uses 'holding with hand or bird of prey' as the criterion.
3
Understand the meaning of 'release'
'Release' does not mean abandonment (tasyib), which is haram; rather, it must be done in a safe way, such as placing it in a house or entrusting it to someone.
The commentator distinguishes between itlaq (permissible release) and tasyib (forbidden abandonment).
4
Apply the analogy to ihram
Similarly, if a muhrim has game in hand, he must release it. If in his house or cage, he does not. The text uses the Haram case to teach the ihram case.
The author alerts the reader to the parallelism between the two cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن دخل الحرم بصيد أرسله) أي فعليه أن يطلقه لأنه لما حصل في الحرم وجب ترك التعرض لحرمة الحرم إذ هو صار من صيد الحرم فاستحق الأمن أراد به ما إذا دخل به وهو ممسك له بيده الجارحة لأنه سيصرح بأنه إذا أحرم وفي بيته أو في قفصه صيد لا يرسله فكذلك إذا دخل الحرم ومعه صيد في قفصه يرسله لأنه لا فرق بينهما. فالحاصل أن من أحرم وفي يده صيد حقيقة أو دخل كذلك وجب إرساله وإن كان في بيته أو قفصه لا يجب إرساله فيهما فنبه بمسألة دخول الحرم هنا على مسألة المحرم ونبه بمسألة المحرم الآتية على مسألة الحرم، وعمم الداخل ليشمل الحلال والمحرم وليس المراد من إرساله تسييبه لأن تسييب الدابة حرام بل يطلقه على وجه لا يضيع سيأتي تفسيره بأن يرسله في بيت أو يودعه عند إنسان قول المصنف : (فإن باعه الخ قال في اللباب : لا يجوز بيع المحرم صيداً في الحل والحرم أي سواء
He said: (And whoever enters the sanctuary with game, let him release it) i.e., he must release it because when it is in the sanctuary, it becomes necessary to avoid violating the sanctity of the sanctuary, for it has become part of the game of the sanctuary and deserves safety. He intended by this the case when he enters holding it with his hand or a bird of prey, because he will explicitly state that when he enters ihram and has game in his house or cage, he does not release it. So likewise, if he enters the sanctuary with game in his cage, he releases it because there is no difference between them. The conclusion is that whoever enters ihram with game in his hand actually, or enters the sanctuary similarly, must release it; but if it is in his house or cage, release is not obligatory in those two cases. Thus he alerts by the issue of entering the sanctuary here to the issue of the muhrim, and alerts by the issue of the muhrim (coming later) to the issue of the sanctuary. And he generalized the entrant to include both the non-muhrim and the muhrim. And the intended meaning of its release is not to abandon it, because abandoning an animal is haram; rather, he releases it in a way that it is not lost, and its explanation will come: that he releases it in a house or entrusts it to a person. The author said: (If he sells it…) He said in al-Lubab: It is not permissible for a muhrim to sell game in the hal or in the haram, i.e., in both cases.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling that anyone entering the Haram with game must release it, because the game becomes part of the Haram's protected game. The release is required if the game is held in hand or by a bird of prey; but if it is in a cage or house, it does not need to be released. The commentary distinguishes between the case of a muhrim (who likewise must release game in his hand) and a non-muhrim entering the Haram. The release must be in a safe manner (e.g., in a house or entrusted to someone), not simply abandoned, because abandonment of an animal is haram. The commentator also notes that the author (al-Haskafi) mentioned selling: a muhrim cannot sell game whether inside or outside the Haram.

Key Terms
تسييب (tasyib): Abandoning an animal without care, which is haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a person do if he enters the Haram with game in his hand?
A) Keep it and care for it.
B) Release it immediately anywhere.
C) Release it in a safe manner such as in a house or with a trusted person.
D) Sell it to someone in the Haram.

Key Takeaway
Entering the Haram with game in hand obligates its safe release; game in cage or house is exempt.

Dispute on the Origin of Makkah's Sacredness and Madinah's Haram
Discusses two ikhtilafaat: origin of Makkah's haram and whether Madinah has a legal haram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position regarding the origin of Makkah's sanctity and explain why Madinah does not have a legal haram, using evidence from the hadith of Anas and the usul principle of 'umum al-balwa.

Core Idea
Madinah has no legal haram; its sanctity is reverential (ta'zim), not juristic.

This lesson examines two scholarly disputes: (1) whether Makkah's sacredness began with Ibrahim (as) or is primordial, and (2) whether Madinah has a legal sanctuary (haram) like Makkah. The Hanafi school holds that Makkah's sanctity is from creation, and more significantly, that Madinah does not possess a legal haram. Therefore, hunting and cutting trees in Madinah are permissible. This position is supported by the hadith of Anas regarding Abu 'Umayr's nightingale and by the usul principle that a khabar wahid is not accepted in matters of 'umum al-balwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Disputes
Read the source passage carefully. The first dispute concerns whether Makkah became a sanctuary by Ibrahim's supplication or was already sacred from creation. The second dispute is whether Madinah has a legal haram with prohibitions like Makkah.
These are two separate ikhtilafaat; focus on the Madinah dispute as it is more extensive.
2
State the Hanafi Position on Each
For Makkah: The correct view is that it has been sacred since creation. For Madinah: According to the Hanafi school, Madinah has no legal haram, so hunting and cutting trees are permissible.
The passage states 'indana' – according to us.
3
Analyze the Opposing Evidence
Other schools cite explicit hadiths from Sahih Muslim where the Prophet said: 'I have declared Madinah sacred between its two lava plains; its branches should not be cut nor its game hunted.' Identify this as the primary dalil for the opposing view.
The passage acknowledges these hadiths are 'sahih' and 'sarih' (explicit).
4
Examine the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response is twofold. First, the prohibition is interpreted as ta'zim (reverence), not legal sanctity. Second, these hadiths are khabar wahid on a matter of 'umum al-balwa, and according to Hanafi usul, such reports are not accepted as binding because if authentic, the transmission would have been widespread.
The Anas hadith about the nightingale is presented as stronger evidence.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence is that Hanafis allow hunting and cutting trees in Madinah, while other schools prohibit them. This affects pilgrims and residents in Madinah.
This is an active legal difference with daily implications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلف العلماء في أن مكة مع حرمها هل صارت حرماً آمناً بسؤال إبراهيم عليه السلام أم كانت قبله كذلك؟ والأصح أنها ما زالت محرمة من حين خلق الله السموات والأرض ا هـ . ثم اعلم أنه ليس للمدينة حرم عندنا فيجوز الاصطياد فيها وقطع أشجارها وقد وردت أحاديث كثيرة في الصحيحين وغيرها صريحة في تحريم المدينة كمكة وأولها أصحابنا بأن المراد بالتحريم التعظيم ويرده ما ثبت في صحيح مسلم أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال إني حرمت المدينة ما بين لابتيها لا تقطع أغصانها ولا يصاد صيدها (۱) فهو صريح في أن لها حرماً كمكة فلا يجوز قطع شجرها ولا الاصطياد فيها والأحسن الاستدلال بحديث أنس الثابت في الصحيحين أنه كان له أخ صغير يقال له أبو عمير وكان له نغير يلعب به فمات النغير فكان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : يا أبا عمير ما فعل النغير؟ ولو كان للمدينة لكان إرساله واجباً عليه ولأنكر عليه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في إمساكه ولا يمازحه. وأجاب في المحيط عن الأحاديث الصحيحة في أن لها حرماً أنها من أخبار الآحاد فيما تعم به البلوى لأن الشجر للمدينة أمر تعم به البلوى وخبر الواحد إذا ورد فيما تعم به البلوى لا يقبل إذ لو كان صحيحاً لاشتهر نقله فيما عم به البلوى ا هـ.
The scholars differed as to whether Makkah with its sanctuary became a sacred sanctuary through the request of Ibrahim, peace be upon him, or whether it was like that before him? The correct view is that it has never ceased to be sacred from when Allah created the heavens and the earth. End. Then know that Madinah has no sanctuary according to us, so hunting within it and cutting its trees are permissible. Indeed many ahadith have been reported in the Sahihain and others explicitly forbidding Madinah like Makkah. Our companions interpreted them as meaning that the prohibition is [for] reverence/glorification (ta'zim). But this is refuted by what is established in Sahih Muslim that the Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'I have declared Madinah sacred between its two lava plains; its branches should not be cut nor its game hunted.' So this is explicit that it has a sanctuary like Makkah, so it is not permissible to cut its trees nor hunt within it. The best evidence is the hadith of Anas established in the Sahihain that he had a small brother called Abu 'Umayr who had a nightingale (nughayr) with which he played, then the nightingale died. The Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, used to say, 'O Abu 'Umayr, what happened to the nightingale?' If Madinah had a sanctuary, it would have been obligatory upon him to release it, and the Messenger of Allah would have disapproved of his keeping it and would not have jested with him. And it was answered in al-Muhit regarding the authentic ahadith that it (Madinah) has a sanctuary: that they are khabar wahid (singular reports) concerning matters of general necessity ('umum al-balwa) because the trees of Madinah are a matter of general necessity, and a khabar wahid when reported concerning matters of general necessity is not accepted, because if it were authentic, its transmission would have become widespread in matters of general necessity. End.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage presents two related ikhtilafaat (disputes) concerning the sacred precincts (haram). First, regarding Makkah: the correct view according to our school is that Allah made it a sanctuary from the moment of creation, not by the supplication of Ibrahim (peace be upon him). Second, and more extensively, the passage addresses whether Madinah has a legal sanctuary (haram) like Makkah. The Hanafi position, stated firmly as 'at our school' (indana), is that Madinah does not have a haram; consequently, hunting and cutting trees there are permissible. The author then acknowledges that there are explicit sahih hadiths forbidding these acts in Madinah, such as the Prophet's statement, 'I have declared Madinah sacred...' The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) These hadiths are interpreted as indicating glorification (ta'zim) rather than legal sanctity. (2) Even if taken literally, they are ahad reports on a matter of 'umum al-balwa (general necessity), and according to Hanafi usul, such reports are not accepted because if they were authentic, the transmission would have been widespread. To support the Hanafi position, the author cites the hadith of Anas regarding Abu 'Umayr's nughayr (nightingale), arguing that if Madinah were a haram, the Prophet would have ordered the release of the bird, but he did not; instead he jested with the boy. This indicates to us that Madinah does not have the legal status of a sanctuary.

Key Terms
حرم (haram): Sacred precinct or sanctuary with special legal rulings; here it refers to the area where hunting and cutting trees is prohibited. The Hanafis apply this strictly to Makkah and not to Madinah.
تعظيم (ta'zim): Reverence or glorification; used here to explain that the Prophet's pronouncement about Madinah is for showing respect, not for establishing a legal prohibition.
خبر الواحد (khabar wahid): A singly transmitted report; in Hanafi usul, a khabar wahid is zanni al-thubut and not accepted in matters of 'umum al-balwa.
عموم البلوى ('umum al-balwa): A matter of general necessity (i.e., widespread occurrence); such matters require widespread transmission according to Hanafi usul, so a khabar wahid is insufficient.
النغير (nughayr): A small bird (typically a nightingale or a type of sparrow) that was a pet of the Prophet's companion Abu 'Umayr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on hunting in Madinah?
A) It is haram because Madinah has a haram like Makkah.
B) It is makruh but permissible.
C) It is permissible because Madinah does not have a legal haram.
D) It is wajib to release any caught game.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that Madinah has no legal haram; its sanctity is reverential, not juristic, and thus hunting and cutting trees are permissible.

Obligation to Release Hunted Animal upon Entering the Haram
Explains the obligation to release a hunted animal brought into the Haram, with conditions and manner of release.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation to release a hunted animal brought into the Haram and identify the conditions that trigger this obligation.

Core Idea
A hunted animal gains immunity in the Haram; releasing it is wajib if you physically hold it.

Entering the Haram with a hunted animal imposes a sacred duty: the animal must be released because it now shares the sanctuary's immunity. But this obligation is not absolute—it depends on how you are carrying the animal. The scholars distinguish between having it in your hand (obligatory release) and having it in a cage or house (no obligation). This lesson unpacks that distinction and explains the proper manner of release.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is entering the Haram while in possession of a hunted animal (sayd). The ruling is that the animal must be released (irsal). This is wajib.
2
Determine the condition for obligation
The obligation applies only if the animal is in the person's hand (literally) or under direct physical control via a trained predator (jariha).
If the animal is in a cage or house, release is not obligatory.
3
Understand the manner of release
Release does not mean abandonment (tasyib), which is haram. Instead, the animal should be placed in a safe environment, like a house or with a trustee.
4
Note the ownership consequence
The animal does not leave the owner's ownership upon release. If it goes to the Hal, the owner may retake it. If someone else takes it, the owner can recover it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قدمناه. وفرق الإمام بأن البيع ليس بتعرض له حساً بل حكماً وليس هو بأبلغ من أمره بذبح هذا الصيد بخلاف ما لو رماه من الحرم للاتصال الحسي. هذا ما ذكر الشارحون وفي المحيط خلافه فإن قال : كان في يده أو قفصه أو منزله ولا بيع الحلال في الحرم ولا شراؤهما من محرم ولا حلال، فإن باعه أو ابتاعه فهو باطل، سواء كان حياً أو مذبوحاً في الإحرام أو الحرم. ولو هلك الصيد في يد المشتري، فإن كانا محرمين أو حلالين في قال في البدائع : روى ابن سماعة عن محمد في رجل أخرج صيداً من الحرم إلى الحل أن ذبحه والانتفاع بلحمه ليس بمحرم، سواء أدى جزاءه أو لم يؤد غير أني أكره هذا الصنع فإن باعه واستعان بقيمته في جزائه جاز ا.هـ. وانظر من أين يستفاد ضعفه من كلام أنه جزم به في الخانية فقال : ولو ذبح هذا الصيد قبل التكفير أو بعده كره أكله تنزيهاً، ولو استعان بثمنه في الجزاء كان له ذلك ويجوز به الانتفاع للمشتري قوله : (فإن باعه) أي الصيد هو في الحرم ضمير وهو راجع إلى الصيد أيضاً. وقوله لا مطلقاً» أي ليس المراد الإطلاق أي سواء كان
His statement: (Whoever enters the Haram with a hunted animal, let him release it) meaning it is upon him to release it, because when it has reached the Haram, it becomes obligatory to avoid violating the sanctity of the Haram, as it has become part of the game of the Haram and has earned safety. He intended by it when he enters with it while holding it in his hand or an animal of prey, because he will explicitly state that if he enters ihram and there is a hunted animal in his house or cage, he does not release it. So also if he enters the Haram and has a hunted animal in his cage, he releases it because there is no difference between them. The conclusion is that whoever enters ihram with a hunted animal in his hand literally, or enters the Haram likewise, must release it. But if it is in his house or cage, he is not required to release it in either case. So by the case of entering the Haram he alerts to the case of the muhrim, and by the upcoming case of the muhrim he alerts to the case of the Haram. He generalizes 'the one who enters' to include the non-muhrim and the muhrim. The intent of releasing it is not to let it loose and abandon it, because abandoning a quadruped is haram, but he releases it in a manner that it is not wasted. His statement: (But he releases it in a manner that it is not wasted) will later be explained as: he releases it in a house or entrusts it to a person. The statement of the author: (If he sells it, etc.) It was said in al-Lubab: It is not permissible for a muhrim to sell a hunted animal in the Hal or the Haram, meaning whether ... [He who enters the Haram with a hunted animal, if he sells it, the sale is rescinded if it still exists, and if it is lost then he must pay the penalty (jaza'). And whoever enters ihram in a manner that it is not wasted, it does not leave his ownership by this release, so that if it goes out to the Hal, he may take hold of it, and if someone takes it, he recovers it. And he generalizes the hunted animal to include whether it is an animal of prey or not, so if he enters the Haram with a falcon and releases it and it kills a dove of the Haram, then nothing is upon him because he did what was obligatory upon him, as we have set forth earlier. His statement: (If he sells it, the sale is rescinded if it still exists, and if it is lost then he must pay the penalty) because the sale did not occur due to the assault on the hunted animal, and that is haram, and the penalty becomes due by its being lost for causing loss of the deserved security. And by his statement 'return the sale' he indicated that it is fasid (voidable) not batil (void). And he generalizes in his sale to include whether he sells it in the Haram or after taking it out to the Hal because by the act of bringing it in it becomes part of the game of the Haram, so its removal to the Hal is not permissible after that. And he restricts that the hunted animal is inside the Haram because if it were in the Hal and the two parties of the sale are in the Haram, then the sale is valid according to Abu Hanifa, but Muhammad forbids it by qiyas on the prohibition of shooting from the Haram to a hunted animal in the Hal, as we have set forth earlier. And the Imam (Abu Hanifa) distinguished by saying that selling is not a physical assault but a legal one, and it is not stronger than ordering the slaughter of this hunted animal, unlike shooting from the Haram due to physical connection. This is what the commentators have mentioned. But in al-Muhit there is a difference: he said: it is in his hand or cage or house, and there is no sale for a non-muhrim in the Haram nor their purchase from a muhrim or non-muhrim. If he sells it or buys it, it is batil (void), whether it is alive or slaughtered in ihram or the Haram. If the hunted animal perishes in the possession of the buyer, if both are muhrim or non-muhrim in the Haram, the penalty is upon both; if they are in the Hal, it is upon the muhrim of them. If he gives it as a gift to a muhrim and it perishes with him, then upon the recipient is the penalty of the hunted animal and compensation to its owner due to the gift being fasid. If he eats it, upon him is a third penalty and upon the giver one penalty. If he takes a hunted animal out of the Haram and sells it in the Hal to a muhrim or non-muhrim, the sale is batil. Likewise if he brings a hunted animal of the Hal into the Haram then takes it out and sells it. If a muhrim appoints a delegation for a hunted animal, it is permissible. If a non-muhrim appoints a non-muhrim, then the principal enters ihram before taking possession, it is also permissible. If he sells his hunted animal in the Hal while he is in the Haram, it is permissible but he handovers after exiting to the Hal. If two persons make a sale of a hunted animal in the Hal then both enter ihram, then the buyer finds a defect of deficiency, he does not have the right to return. If two non-muhrim sell a hunted animal, then one of them enters ihram before taking possession, the non-muhrim returns to the sale? the sale is rescinded. Its completion is in it and some of this will come. His statement: (that it is fasid not batil) is a declaration of fasid quoted in al-Sharnabaliyya from al-Kafi and al-Tabyin. His statement: (And in al-Muhit there is a difference) so the author decided in al-Nahr that what is in al-Muhit is weak, agreeing with the transmission of Ibn Sama'a. He said in al-Bada'i: Ibn Sama'a transmitted from Muhammad regarding a man who took a hunted animal out of the Haram to the Hal that slaughtering it and benefiting from its meat is not prohibited, whether he paid its penalty or not, but I dislike this action. If he sells it and uses its price for his penalty, it is permissible. End. Look: from where is its weakness deduced? From his statement that he decided it in al-Khaniyya: if one slaughters this hunted animal before expiation or after, its consumption is disliked as tanzih, and if he uses its price for the penalty, that is permissible for him, and the buyer may benefit from it. His statement: (If he sells it) means the hunted animal is in the Haram; the pronoun refers to the hunted animal also. And his statement: 'not absolutely' means the absolute is not intended, i.e. whether it is...
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the ruling for a person who enters the Haram (sanctuary) with a hunted animal (sayd). The author explains that the individual must release the animal because it acquires immunity upon entering the Haram. The obligation applies whether the person is in ihram or not (muhrim or halal), but only if the animal is physically in his hand (or under his actual control). If the animal is in his house or cage, he is not required to release it. The release must be done in a manner that does not waste the animal (e.g., placing it in a house or with a trustee). The passage then discusses the sale of such an animal. The general rule is that if a person sells a hunted animal that is inside the Haram, the contract is fasid (voidable): if the animal still exists, the sale is rescinded; if it has perished, the seller must pay the penalty (jaza') because he has forfeited the animal's guaranteed security. Notably, the author clarifies that the sale is fasid, not batil, meaning it can be rescinded rather than being automatically void. A significant intra-madhhab dispute arises between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad. According to Abu Hanifa, if the hunted animal is actually in the Hal (outside the Haram) and both parties to the sale are inside the Haram, the sale is valid. Muhammad, however, prohibits such a sale by qiyas (analogy) on the prohibition of shooting from within the Haram at game in the Hal. Abu Hanifa distinguishes: selling is a legal act (hukmi) not a physical one, and it is not stronger than ordering the slaughter of the animal (which is permissible). The passage then recounts further rulings from al-Muhit, which are considered weak by the author, who follows the stronger position of Abu Hanifa. Additional subsidiary rulings cover cases where the animal is given as a gift, consumed, or sold after removal from the Haram.

Key Terms
صيد (sayd): Hunted animal, or game. It includes any animal hunted, whether a bird or quadruped, including trained falcons (jawaarih).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a person NOT obligated to release a hunted animal upon entering the Haram?
A) When the animal is a falcon.
B) When the animal is in a cage.
C) When the person is in ihram.
D) When the animal is a bird.

Key Takeaway
Releasing a hunted animal upon entering the Haram is wajib only if the animal is under your direct physical control; release must be done without wasting the animal.

Sale of a Hunted Animal Brought into the Haram: Fasid and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains the ruling on selling a hunted animal brought into the Haram, the fasid vs batil distinction, and the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding location.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the sale of a hunted animal brought into the Haram is fasid (voidable) and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad regarding sales when the animal is in the Hal.

Core Idea
Selling a hunted animal that has been brought into the Haram is fasid, not batil, and Abu Hanifa permits the sale if the animal is in the Hal.

When a hunted animal has acquired immunity by entering the Haram, any sale involving it is problematic. The general ruling is that the sale is fasid (voidable), requiring rescission if the animal still exists or a penalty if it is lost. However, a key intra-Hanafi dispute arises concerning the location of the animal: if the animal is outside the Haram (Hal) but the parties are inside, Abu Hanifa rules the sale valid, while Muhammad prohibits it by analogy to shooting from the Haram. This lesson analyzes the core dispute and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
For a hunted animal brought into the Haram, if it is sold while still inside, the sale is fasid: if the animal still exists, the sale is rescinded; if lost, the seller must pay the penalty (jaza').
2
Understand the fasid vs batil distinction
The author explicitly indicates that the sale is fasid (voidable) not batil (void). This means the contract can be rescinded rather than being automatically null. The difference affects remedies.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
If the hunted animal is in the Hal and both buyer and seller are in the Haram, Abu Hanifa says the sale is valid. Muhammad forbids it by qiyas on shooting from Haram into Hal.
Abu Hanifa's dalil: selling is a legal (hukmi) act, not a physical assault, and is not stronger than ordering the animal's slaughter (which is permissible).
4
Apply the tarjih
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq considers the view in al-Muhit (supporting Muhammad) weak, so the mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's ruling that the sale is valid.

قوله : (ومن دخل الحرم بصيد أرسله) أي فعليه أن يطلقه لأنه لما حصل في الحرم وجب ترك التعرض لحرمة الحرم إذ هو صار من صيد الحرم فاستحق الأمن أراد به ما إذا دخل به وهو ممسك له بيده الجارحة لأنه سيصرح بأنه إذا أحرم وفي بيته أو في قفصه صيد لا يرسله فكذلك إذا دخل الحرم ومعه صيد في قفصه يرسله لأنه لا فرق بينهما. فالحاصل أن من أحرم وفي يده صيد حقيقة أو دخل كذلك وجب إرساله وإن كان في بيته أو قفصه لا يجب إرساله فيهما فنبه بمسألة دخول الحرم هنا على مسألة المحرم ونبه بمسألة المحرم الآتية على مسألة الحرم، وعمم الداخل ليشمل الحلال والمحرم وليس المراد من إرساله تسييبه لأن تسييب الدابة حرام بل يطلقه على وجه لا يضيع. قوله : (بل يطلقه على وجه لا يضيع) سيأتي تفسيره بأن يرسله في بيت أو يودعه عند إنسان. قول المصنف : (فإن باعه الخ) قال في اللباب : لا يجوز بيع المحرم صيداً في الحل والحرم أي سواء (۱). دخل الحرم بصيد أرسله فإن باعه رد البيع إن بقي وإن فات فعليه الجزاء ومن أحرم وجه لا يضيع ولا يخرج عن ملكه بهذا الإرسال حتى لو خرج إلى الحل فله أن يمسكه، ولو أخذه إنسان يسترده. وأطلق في الصيد فشمل ما إذا كان من الجوارح أو لا، فلو دخل الحرم ومعه بازي فأرسله فقتل حمام الحرم فإنه لا شيء عليه لأنه فعل ما هو الواجب عليه وقد قدمناه . قوله : (فإن باعه رد البيع إن بقي وإن فات فعليه الجزاء) لأن البيع لم يجز لما فيه من التعرض للصيد وذلك حرام ولزمه الجزاء بفوته لتفويت الأمن المستحق. وأشار بقوله «رد البيع» إلى أنه فاسد لا باطل وأطلق في بيعه فشمل ما إذا باعه في الحرم أو بعد ما أخرجه إلى الحل لأنه صار بالإدخال من صيد الحرم فلا يحل إخراجه إلى الحل بعد ذلك. وقيد بكون الصيد داخل الحرم لأنه لو كان في الحل والمتبايعان في الحرم فإن البيع صحيح عند أبي حنيفة، ومنعه محمد قياساً على منع رميه من الحرم إلى صيد في الحل كما قدمناه. وفرق الإمام بأن البيع ليس بتعرض له حساً بل حكماً وليس هو بأبلغ من أمره بذبح هذا الصيد بخلاف ما لو رماه من الحرم للاتصال الحسي. هذا ما ذكر الشارحون وفي المحيط خلافه فإن قال : كان في يده أو قفصه أو منزله ولا بيع الحلال في الحرم ولا شراؤهما من محرم ولا حلال، فإن باعه أو ابتاعه فهو باطل، سواء كان حياً أو مذبوحاً في الإحرام أو الحرم. ولو هلك الصيد في يد المشتري، فإن كانا محرمين أو حلالين في الحرم لزمهما الجزاء، وإن كانا في الحل فعلى المحرم منهما. ولو وهبه لمحرم فهلك عنده فعلى الموهوب له جزاء الصيد وضمان لصاحبه أي لفساد الهبة، ولو أكله فعليه جزاء ثالث وعلى الواهب جزاء واحد ولو أخرج صيداً من الحرم فباعه في الحل من محرم أو حلال فالبيع باطل، وكذا لو أدخل صيد الحل الحرم ثم أخرجه وباعه. ولو وكل محرم . صيد جاز، ولو وكل حلال حلالاً ثم أحرم الموكل قبل القبض جاز أيضاً. ولو باع صيداً له في الحل وهو في الحرم جاز ولكن يسلمه بعد الخروج إلى الحل، ولو تبايعاً صيداً في الحل ثم أحرما فوجد المشتري به عيباً بالنقصان وليس له الرد، ولو باع حلالان صيداً فأحرم أحدهما قبل القبض رجع حلالاً ببيع انفسخ البيع وتمامه فيه وسيأتي بعض هذا قوله : (إلى أنه فاسد لا باطل نقل التصريح بالفساد في الشرنبلالية عن الكافي والتبيين قوله : ( وفي المحيط خلافه (الخ جزم في النهر بأن ما في المحيط ضعيف موافقة لرواية ابن سماعة. قال في البدائع : روى ابن سماعة عن محمد في رجل أخرج صيداً من الحرم إلى الحل أن ذبحه والانتفاع بلحمه ليس بمحرم، سواء أدى جزاءه أو لم يؤد غير أني أكره هذا الصنع فإن باعه واستعان بقيمته في جزائه جاز ا.هـ. وانظر من أين يستفاد ضعفه من كلام أنه جزم به في الخانية فقال : ولو ذبح هذا الصيد قبل التكفير أو بعده كره أكله تنزيهاً، ولو استعان بثمنه في الجزاء كان له ذلك ويجوز به الانتفاع للمشتري قوله : (فإن باعه) أي الصيد هو في الحرم ضمير وهو راجع إلى الصيد أيضاً. وقوله لا مطلقاً» أي ليس المراد الإطلاق أي سواء كان
His statement: (Whoever enters the Haram with a hunted animal, let him release it) meaning it is upon him to release it, because when it has reached the Haram, it becomes obligatory to avoid violating the sanctity of the Haram, as it has become part of the game of the Haram and has earned safety. He intended by it when he enters with it while holding it in his hand or an animal of prey, because he will explicitly state that if he enters ihram and there is a hunted animal in his house or cage, he does not release it. So also if he enters the Haram and has a hunted animal in his cage, he releases it because there is no difference between them. The conclusion is that whoever enters ihram with a hunted animal in his hand literally, or enters the Haram likewise, must release it. But if it is in his house or cage, he is not required to release it in either case. So by the case of entering the Haram he alerts to the case of the muhrim, and by the upcoming case of the muhrim he alerts to the case of the Haram. He generalizes 'the one who enters' to include the non-muhrim and the muhrim. The intent of releasing it is not to let it loose and abandon it, because abandoning a quadruped is haram, but he releases it in a manner that it is not wasted. His statement: (But he releases it in a manner that it is not wasted) will later be explained as: he releases it in a house or entrusts it to a person. The statement of the author: (If he sells it, etc.) It was said in al-Lubab: It is not permissible for a muhrim to sell a hunted animal in the Hal or the Haram, meaning whether ... [He who enters the Haram with a hunted animal, if he sells it, the sale is rescinded if it still exists, and if it is lost then he must pay the penalty (jaza'). And whoever enters ihram in a manner that it is not wasted, it does not leave his ownership by this release, so that if it goes out to the Hal, he may take hold of it, and if someone takes it, he recovers it. And he generalizes the hunted animal to include whether it is an animal of prey or not, so if he enters the Haram with a falcon and releases it and it kills a dove of the Haram, then nothing is upon him because he did what was obligatory upon him, as we have set forth earlier. His statement: (If he sells it, the sale is rescinded if it still exists, and if it is lost then he must pay the penalty) because the sale did not occur due to the assault on the hunted animal, and that is haram, and the penalty becomes due by its being lost for causing loss of the deserved security. And by his statement 'return the sale' he indicated that it is fasid (voidable) not batil (void). And he generalizes in his sale to include whether he sells it in the Haram or after taking it out to the Hal because by the act of bringing it in it becomes part of the game of the Haram, so its removal to the Hal is not permissible after that. And he restricts that the hunted animal is inside the Haram because if it were in the Hal and the two parties of the sale are in the Haram, then the sale is valid according to Abu Hanifa, but Muhammad forbids it by qiyas on the prohibition of shooting from the Haram to a hunted animal in the Hal, as we have set forth earlier. And the Imam (Abu Hanifa) distinguished by saying that selling is not a physical assault but a legal one, and it is not stronger than ordering the slaughter of this hunted animal, unlike shooting from the Haram due to physical connection. This is what the commentators have mentioned. But in al-Muhit there is a difference: he said: it is in his hand or cage or house, and there is no sale for a non-muhrim in the Haram nor their purchase from a muhrim or non-muhrim. If he sells it or buys it, it is batil (void), whether it is alive or slaughtered in ihram or the Haram. If the hunted animal perishes in the possession of the buyer, if both are muhrim or non-muhrim in the Haram, the penalty is upon both; if they are in the Hal, it is upon the muhrim of them. If he gives it as a gift to a muhrim and it perishes with him, then upon the recipient is the penalty of the hunted animal and compensation to its owner due to the gift being fasid. If he eats it, upon him is a third penalty and upon the giver one penalty. If he takes a hunted animal out of the Haram and sells it in the Hal to a muhrim or non-muhrim, the sale is batil. Likewise if he brings a hunted animal of the Hal into the Haram then takes it out and sells it. If a muhrim appoints a delegation for a hunted animal, it is permissible. If a non-muhrim appoints a non-muhrim, then the principal enters ihram before taking possession, it is also permissible. If he sells his hunted animal in the Hal while he is in the Haram, it is permissible but he handovers after exiting to the Hal. If two persons make a sale of a hunted animal in the Hal then both enter ihram, then the buyer finds a defect of deficiency, he does not have the right to return. If two non-muhrim sell a hunted animal, then one of them enters ihram before taking possession, the non-muhrim returns to the sale? the sale is rescinded. Its completion is in it and some of this will come. His statement: (that it is fasid not batil) is a declaration of fasid quoted in al-Sharnabaliyya from al-Kafi and al-Tabyin. His statement: (And in al-Muhit there is a difference) so the author decided in al-Nahr that what is in al-Muhit is weak, agreeing with the transmission of Ibn Sama'a. He said in al-Bada'i: Ibn Sama'a transmitted from Muhammad regarding a man who took a hunted animal out of the Haram to the Hal that slaughtering it and benefiting from its meat is not prohibited, whether he paid its penalty or not, but I dislike this action. If he sells it and uses its price for his penalty, it is permissible. End. Look: from where is its weakness deduced? From his statement that he decided it in al-Khaniyya: if one slaughters this hunted animal before expiation or after, its consumption is disliked as tanzih, and if he uses its price for the penalty, that is permissible for him, and the buyer may benefit from it. His statement: (If he sells it) means the hunted animal is in the Haram; the pronoun refers to the hunted animal also. And his statement: 'not absolutely' means the absolute is not intended, i.e. whether it is...
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the ruling for a person who enters the Haram (sanctuary) with a hunted animal (sayd). The author explains that the individual must release the animal because it acquires immunity upon entering the Haram. The obligation applies whether the person is in ihram or not (muhrim or halal), but only if the animal is physically in his hand (or under his actual control). If the animal is in his house or cage, he is not required to release it. The release must be done in a manner that does not waste the animal (e.g., placing it in a house or with a trustee). The passage then discusses the sale of such an animal. The general rule is that if a person sells a hunted animal that is inside the Haram, the contract is fasid (voidable): if the animal still exists, the sale is rescinded; if it has perished, the seller must pay the penalty (jaza') because he has forfeited the animal's guaranteed security. Notably, the author clarifies that the sale is fasid, not batil, meaning it can be rescinded rather than being automatically void. A significant intra-madhhab dispute arises between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad. According to Abu Hanifa, if the hunted animal is actually in the Hal (outside the Haram) and both parties to the sale are inside the Haram, the sale is valid. Muhammad, however, prohibits such a sale by qiyas (analogy) on the prohibition of shooting from within the Haram at game in the Hal. Abu Hanifa distinguishes: selling is a legal act (hukmi) not a physical one, and it is not stronger than ordering the slaughter of the animal (which is permissible). The passage then recounts further rulings from al-Muhit, which are considered weak by the author, who follows the stronger position of Abu Hanifa. Additional subsidiary rulings cover cases where the animal is given as a gift, consumed, or sold after removal from the Haram.

Key Terms
فاسد (fasid): Voidable contract; not automatically invalid (batil) but requires rescission. Here, the sale of sayd inside Haram is fasid, meaning it can be reversed if the animal still exists.
جزاء (jaza'): Penalty for killing or forfeiting game in the Haram or while in ihram. It can be offering an animal, feeding the poor, or fasting.
صيد (sayd): Hunted animal, or game. It includes any animal hunted, whether a bird or quadruped, including trained falcons (jawaarih).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of Abu Hanifa on the sale of a hunted animal when the animal is in the Hal and both parties are in the Haram?
A) The sale is fasid.
B) The sale is batil.
C) The sale is valid.
D) The sale is makruh.

Key Takeaway
The sale of a hunted animal brought into the Haram is fasid; however, if the animal is in the Hal, the sale is valid according to Abu Hanifa, which is the relied-upon position.

Ruling on a Muhrim Selling Game in the Haram
Explains the ruling of a muhrim selling game brought into the Haram, including its invalidity and penalty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of a muhrim selling game brought into the Haram, distinguish fasid from batil, and apply the penalty rule.

Core Idea
A muhrim’s sale of game in the Haram is fasid; if the game is lost, a penalty is due.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a specific prohibition during ihram: the sale of game that has been brought into the Haram. The ruling distinguishes between sale being fasid (corrupt) rather than batil (void) and imposes a penalty if the game perishes. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the correct legal consequences in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
A muhrim sells game he brought into the Haram. The ruling: if the game remains, the sale is fasid and must be rescinded; if the game is gone, the seller owes the penalty (jaza').
The text says 'رد البيع إن بقي وإن فات فعليه الجزاء'.
2
Understand the reason for the ruling
The sale involves transgression (تعرض) against the game, which is prohibited in the Haram. The penalty compensates for the loss of the protected status (الأمن المستحق) of the game.
3
Distinguish fasid from batil
The term 'رد البيع' indicates the sale is fasid, not batil. Fasid means the contract is inherently valid but prohibited due to external factors (sanctity of Haram). Batil would be void ab initio with no legal effects.
This distinction affects consequences: in a fasid sale, the object is returned, and if lost, compensation is due.
4
Apply the ruling to related scenarios
The ruling applies whether the sale occurs inside the Haram or after the game is taken out to the Hal, because once brought in, it becomes part of Haram's protected game. However, if the game was originally in the Hal and the parties are in the Haram, the ruling differs (see next lesson).
The text explicitly states: 'وأطلق في بيعه فشمل ما إذا باعه في الحرم أو بعد ما أخرجه إلى الحل'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج فصل إن قتل محرم صيداً دخل الحرم بصيد أرسله فإن باعه رد البيع إن بقي وإن فات فعليه الجزاء ومن أحرم وجه لا يضيع ولا يخرج عن ملكه بهذا الإرسال حتى لو خرج إلى الحل فله أن يمسكه، ولو أخذه إنسان يسترده. وأطلق في الصيد فشمل ما إذا كان من الجوارح أو لا، فلو دخل الحرم ومعه بازي فأرسله فقتل حمام الحرم فإنه لا شيء عليه لأنه فعل ما هو الواجب عليه وقد قدمناه . قوله : (فإن باعه رد البيع إن بقي وإن فات فعليه الجزاء لأن البيع لم يجز لما فيه من التعرض للصيد وذلك حرام ولزمه الجزاء بفوته لتفويت الأمن المستحق. وأشار بقوله «رد البيع» إلى أنه فاسد لا باطل وأطلق في بيعه فشمل ما إذا باعه في الحرم أو بعد ما أخرجه إلى الحل لأنه صار بالإدخال من صيد الحرم فلا يحل إخراجه إلى الحل بعد ذلك. وقيد بكون الصيد داخل الحرم لأنه لو كان في الحل والمتبايعان في الحرم فإن البيع صحيح عند أبي حنيفة، ومنعه محمد قياساً على منع رميه من الحرم إلى صيد في الحل كما قدمناه. وفرق الإمام بأن البيع ليس بتعرض له حساً بل حكماً وليس هو بأبلغ من أمره بذبح هذا الصيد بخلاف ما لو رماه من الحرم للاتصال الحسي. هذا ما ذكر الشارحون وفي المحيط خلافه فإن قال : كان في يده أو قفصه أو منزله ولا بيع الحلال في الحرم ولا شراؤهما من محرم ولا حلال، فإن باعه أو ابتاعه فهو باطل، سواء كان حياً أو مذبوحاً في الإحرام أو الحرم. ولو هلك الصيد في يد المشتري، فإن كانا محرمين أو حلالين في الحرم لزمهما الجزاء، وإن كانا في الحل فعلى المحرم منهما. ولو وهبه لمحرم فهلك عنده فعلى الموهوب له جزاء الصيد وضمان لصاحبه أي لفساد الهبة، ولو أكله فعليه جزاء ثالث وعلى الواهب جزاء واحد ولو أخرج صيداً من الحرم فباعه في الحل من محرم أو حلال فالبيع باطل، وكذا لو أدخل صيد الحل الحرم ثم أخرجه وباعه. ولو وكل محرم . صيد جاز، ولو وكل حلال حلالاً ثم أحرم الموكل قبل القبض جاز أيضاً. ولو باع صيداً له في الحل وهو في الحرم جاز ولكن يسلمه بعد الخروج إلى الحل، ولو تبايعاً صيداً في الحل ثم أحرما فوجد المشتري به عيباً بالنقصان وليس له الرد، ولو باع حلالان صيداً فأحرم أحدهما قبل القبض رجع حلالاً ببيع انفسخ البيع وتمامه فيه وسيأتي بعض هذا قوله : (إلى أنه فاسد لا باطل نقل التصريح بالفساد في الشرنبلالية عن الكافي والتبيين قوله : ( وفي المحيط خلافه (الخ جزم في النهر بأن ما في المحيط ضعيف موافقة لرواية ابن سماعة. قال في البدائع : روى ابن سماعة عن محمد في رجل أخرج صيداً من الحرم إلى الحل أن ذبحه والانتفاع بلحمه ليس بمحرم، سواء أدى جزاءه أو لم يؤد غير أني أكره هذا الصنع فإن باعه واستعان بقيمته في جزائه جاز ا.هـ. وانظر من أين يستفاد ضعفه من كلام أنه جزم به في الخانية فقال : ولو ذبح هذا الصيد قبل التكفير أو بعده كره أكله تنزيهاً، ولو استعان بثمنه في الجزاء كان له ذلك ويجوز به الانتفاع للمشتري قوله : (فإن باعه) أي الصيد هو في الحرم ضمير وهو راجع إلى الصيد أيضاً. وقوله لا مطلقاً» أي ليس المراد الإطلاق أي سواء كان البدائع مع
Book of Hajj. Chapter: If a Muhrim kills game. He entered the Haram with game and released it. If he sells it, the sale is returned (invalid) if it remains; if it is gone, he owes the penalty. And whoever enters ihram, it does not perish nor leave his ownership by this release, so that if it goes out to the Hal, he may hold it, and if someone takes it, he gets it back. And he made it unrestricted in game, so it includes whether it is of prey or not. So if he enters the Haram with a falcon and releases it, and it kills doves of the Haram, then nothing is due from him because he did what was obligatory. We have already mentioned it. His statement: (If he sells it, the sale is returned if it remains; if it is gone, he owes the penalty) because the sale is not permitted due to the transgression against the game, and that is haram, and he owes the penalty for its destruction due to losing the security entitled. And he indicated by his saying 'the sale is returned' that it is fasid (corrupt), not batil (void). And he made it unrestricted in its sale, so it includes whether he sold it in the Haram or after taking it out to the Hal because by entry it becomes from the game of the Haram, so its removal to the Hal is not permissible after that. And he restricted it to the game being inside the Haram because if it were in the Hal and the two parties are in the Haram, then the sale is valid according to Abu Hanifa; Muhammad forbids it by analogy to forbidding shooting from the Haram at game in the Hal as we mentioned. The Imam distinguished because sale is not a sensory transgression but a legal one, and it is not more severe than ordering the slaughter of this game, unlike shooting from the Haram due to sensory connection. This is what the commentators mentioned, and in al-Muhit there is a contrary view. He said: It was in his hand or his cage or his house, and there is no sale of the non-muhrim in the Haram nor their purchase from a muhrim or non-muhrim; if he sells or buys, it is batil, whether alive or slaughtered, in ihram or in the Haram. And if the game perishes in the buyer's hand, if both are muhrims or both non-muhrims in the Haram, they both owe the penalty; if they are in the Hal, only the muhrim owes it. And if he gifts it to a muhrim and it perishes with him, the donee owes the penalty for the game and compensation to its owner due to the invalidity of the gift; if he eats it, he owes a third penalty and the donor owes one penalty. And if he takes game out of the Haram and sells it in the Hal to a muhrim or non-muhrim, the sale is batil; similarly, if he brings game of the Hal into the Haram and then takes it out and sells it. And if a muhrim appoints an agent for game, it is permissible; if a non-muhrim appoints another non-muhrim, then the principal enters ihram before taking possession, it is also permissible. And if he sells his game in the Hal while he is in the Haram, it is permissible, but he hands it over after leaving to the Hal. And if two people trade a game in the Hal, then both enter ihram, and the buyer finds a defect of decrease, he does not have the right of return. And if two non-muhrims sell a game, then one becomes muhrim before taking possession, the non-muhrim returns to the sale; the sale is rescinded. Its completion is in it, and some of this will come later. His statement: (to that it is fasid not batil) he transmits the declaration of fasad in al-Shurnubalaliyya from al-Kafi and al-Tabyin. His statement: (and in al-Muhit there is a contrary view, etc.) He affirms in al-Nahr that what is in al-Muhit is weak, agreeing with the narration of Ibn Sama'a. He said in al-Bada'i: Ibn Sama'a narrated from Muhammad concerning a man who took game out of the Haram to the Hal that slaughtering it and benefiting from its meat is not forbidden, whether he paid the penalty or not, except that I dislike this act. If he sells it and uses its price for his penalty, it is permissible. End. See how its weakness is derived from his statement, for he affirmed it in al-Khaniyya: if he slaughters this game before or after the expiation, he disliked its eating as a tanzihan, and if he uses its price for the penalty, that is permissible, and the buyer may benefit from it. His statement: (If he sells it) meaning the game is in the Haram, the pronoun refers to the game as well. And his statement 'not absolutely' means that the intent is not absolute, i.e., whether it is [with] the Bada'i'?
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It discusses the ruling of a muhrim (one in ihram) who brings game (صيد) into the Haram and then sells it. The matn states: if he sells it and the game is still in existence, the sale is invalid (رد البيع); if it has perished, he must pay the penalty (جزاء). The commentator explains that the reason is that the sale involves transgression against the game, which is haram. He clarifies that 'رد البيع' indicates the sale is fasid (corrupt) not batil (void). The ruling applies whether the sale occurs inside the Haram or after bringing it out to the Hal, because once the game is brought in, it becomes part of the Haram's protected game. However, if the game was in the Hal (outside) and the two parties are in the Haram, the sale is valid according to Abu Hanifa, but Muhammad ibn al-Hasan prevents it by analogy. The distinction is that sale is not a physical transgression like shooting. The text then discusses various scenarios: if the game was in his hand or cage, etc., citing different views from al-Muhit. It also includes rulings on gifting the game, agency, and other details. The passage presents the Hanafi position with internal differences.

Key Terms
صيد (sayd): Game animals or birds that are hunted
مُحرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram (during Hajj or Umrah)
جزاء (jaza'): The penalty or compensation for violating the prohibitions of ihram, often by slaughtering an animal or giving charity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a muhrim sells game he brought into the Haram and the game is still in existence, what is the ruling?
A) The sale is valid and the buyer keeps the game.
B) The sale is batil and the buyer must return the game.
C) The sale is fasid and must be rescinded; the seller returns the price.
D) The sale is valid but the seller must pay a penalty.

Key Takeaway
A muhrim’s sale of game brought into the Haram is fasid; if the game perishes, the seller owes the jaza' penalty.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Selling Game from Hal while in Haram
Explains the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on selling game from Hal while in Haram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad regarding the validity of selling game when the game is in the Hal and the parties are in the Haram, and evaluate the qiyas reasoning.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa validates sale of Hal game from within Haram; Muhammad invalidates via qiyas to shooting, but the distinction is sensory vs. legal transgression.

This lesson delves into an important intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad concerning a specific scenario: game is in the Hal (outside the Haram) while the seller and buyer are inside the Haram. Imam Muhammad analogizes this to the prohibition of shooting from the Haram, while Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes between physical and legal acts. Understanding this disagreement clarifies the limits of qiyas in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the two positions
Scenario: Game is in the Hal, and the muhrim (or non-muhrim) parties are in the Haram. Abu Hanifa: sale is valid. Muhammad: sale is invalid (batil/fasid?) by qiyas.
The text: 'وقيد بكون الصيد داخل الحرم لأنه لو كان في الحل والمتبايعان في الحرم فإن البيع صحيح عند أبي حنيفة، ومنعه محمد قياساً...'
2
Understand Muhammad's qiyas
Muhammad analogizes the sale to shooting game from the Haram into the Hal, which is prohibited. The illa is 'transgression' (تعرض) against the game. Since both involve affecting the game outside, the sale should also be prohibited.
The qiyas panel pre-populated shows the asl is shooting, hukm haram.
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's distinction
Abu Hanifa argues that sale is a legal (hukmi) transgression, not a sensory (hissi) one. It is not as severe as ordering the slaughter of the game, which is permissible. The analogy fails because the means are different.
The text: 'وفرق الإمام بأن البيع ليس بتعرض له حساً بل حكماً وليس هو بأبلغ من أمره بذبح هذا الصيد'
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentator (and al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) supports Abu Hanifa's view. Thus, the mufta bihi position is that the sale is valid in this scenario.
This is from the tarjih authority in the hanafi_position_box.

Source Text

كتاب الحج فصل إن قتل محرم صيداً دخل الحرم بصيد أرسله فإن باعه رد البيع إن بقي وإن فات فعليه الجزاء ومن أحرم وجه لا يضيع ولا يخرج عن ملكه بهذا الإرسال حتى لو خرج إلى الحل فله أن يمسكه، ولو أخذه إنسان يسترده. وأطلق في الصيد فشمل ما إذا كان من الجوارح أو لا، فلو دخل الحرم ومعه بازي فأرسله فقتل حمام الحرم فإنه لا شيء عليه لأنه فعل ما هو الواجب عليه وقد قدمناه . قوله : (فإن باعه رد البيع إن بقي وإن فات فعليه الجزاء لأن البيع لم يجز لما فيه من التعرض للصيد وذلك حرام ولزمه الجزاء بفوته لتفويت الأمن المستحق. وأشار بقوله «رد البيع» إلى أنه فاسد لا باطل وأطلق في بيعه فشمل ما إذا باعه في الحرم أو بعد ما أخرجه إلى الحل لأنه صار بالإدخال من صيد الحرم فلا يحل إخراجه إلى الحل بعد ذلك. وقيد بكون الصيد داخل الحرم لأنه لو كان في الحل والمتبايعان في الحرم فإن البيع صحيح عند أبي حنيفة، ومنعه محمد قياساً على منع رميه من الحرم إلى صيد في الحل كما قدمناه. وفرق الإمام بأن البيع ليس بتعرض له حساً بل حكماً وليس هو بأبلغ من أمره بذبح هذا الصيد بخلاف ما لو رماه من الحرم للاتصال الحسي. هذا ما ذكر الشارحون وفي المحيط خلافه فإن قال : كان في يده أو قفصه أو منزله ولا بيع الحلال في الحرم ولا شراؤهما من محرم ولا حلال، فإن باعه أو ابتاعه فهو باطل، سواء كان حياً أو مذبوحاً في الإحرام أو الحرم. ولو هلك الصيد في يد المشتري، فإن كانا محرمين أو حلالين في الحرم لزمهما الجزاء، وإن كانا في الحل فعلى المحرم منهما. ولو وهبه لمحرم فهلك عنده فعلى الموهوب له جزاء الصيد وضمان لصاحبه أي لفساد الهبة، ولو أكله فعليه جزاء ثالث وعلى الواهب جزاء واحد ولو أخرج صيداً من الحرم فباعه في الحل من محرم أو حلال فالبيع باطل، وكذا لو أدخل صيد الحل الحرم ثم أخرجه وباعه. ولو وكل محرم . صيد جاز، ولو وكل حلال حلالاً ثم أحرم الموكل قبل Book of Hajj. Chapter: If a Muhrim kills game. He entered the Haram with game and released it. If he sells it, the sale is returned (invalid) if it remains; if it is gone, he owes the penalty. And whoever enters ihram, it does not perish nor leave his ownership by this release, so that if it goes out to the Hal, he may hold it, and if someone takes it, he gets it back. And he made it unrestricted in game, so it includes whether it is of prey or not. So if he enters the Haram with a falcon and releases it, and it kills doves of the Haram, then nothing is due from him because he did what was obligatory. We have already mentioned it. His statement: (If he sells it, the sale is returned if it remains; if it is gone, he owes the penalty) because the sale is not permitted due to the transgression against the game, and that is haram, and he owes the penalty for its destruction due to losing the security entitled. And he made it unrestricted in its sale, so it includes whether he sold it in the Haram or after taking it out to the Hal because by entry it becomes from the game of the Haram, so its removal to the Hal is not permissible after that. Key Terms
تعرض (ta'arrud): Transgression or interference with the game

What is the mufta bihi position regarding a muhrim selling game that is in the Hal while the muhrim is in the Haram?
A) The sale is valid according to Abu Hanifa.

C) The sale is makruh tanzihan.
