Muhrim's Confined Game and the Sender's Liability
Explains rulings and dispute on muhrim's game in confinement and liability of sender.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a muhrim with game in his house/cage and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the liability of a sender who becomes muhrim.

Core Idea
Confinement by house/cage is not interference; but sending game then becoming muhrim creates liability according to Imam, not Sahibayn.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq tackles two practical scenarios for a person in ihram. The first clarifies that a muhrim does not have to release game already confined in his home or cage. The second involves a more complex case: if a non-muhrim takes game with permission, and the owner later enters ihram, is the owner liable if the game is killed? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples differed, and their debate illustrates how principles of causation, ownership, and ĥurma interact in Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage presents two distinct cases: (1) a muhrim with game in his house/cage is not required to release it; (2) if a halal takes game and the sender becomes muhrim, the sender's liability is disputed. First, locate each ruling in the Arabic text.
The first ruling is stated as 'لا يرسله' (does not release). The second is 'ضمن مرسله' (the sender is liable) with an immediate qualification 'عند الإمام' (according to Imam).
2
Analyze the proof for the first ruling
The text gives two proofs: the practice of the Companions who had game in their homes while in ihram and did not release it, and the principle that the obligation is only to avoid direct interference (عدم التعرض). The game is already confined by the house/cage, so the muhrim is not interfering.
The custom (عرف) is also cited as a proof. Note that if the cage is in his hand, some scholars said he must release, but the preferred view is that it is not obligatory.
3
Examine the dispute on sender liability
For the second case, locate the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. Imam holds the sender liable; the Sahibayn say no liability. Identify their proofs: Imam argues the sender owned the game with respect and caused its death while in ihram. The Sahibayn argue the sender was commanding good (أمر بالمعروف) and thus falls under 'ما على المحسنين من سبيل'.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The commentator indicates that fatwa is given according to the Sahibayn's view.
4
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah)
The thamarah is clear: if a muhrim sends his game with a halal, is he liable if the halal kills it? According to Imam, yes; according to Sahibayn, no. The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's position, so in fatwa, he is not liable.
The text also discusses related issues like selling game in the Haram, which is permissible but disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج/ فصل إن قتل محرم صيداً وفي بيته أو قفصه صيد لا يرسله ولو أخذ حلال صيدا فأحرم ضمن مرسله ولو أخذه لو أخرج ظبية من الحرم فباعها أو ذبحها أو أكلها جاز البيع والأكل، ويكره لأنه مال مملوك لأنه قيام يده على الصيد وهما في الحل يفيد الملك له في الصيد كما لو أثبت اليد عليه ابتداء إلا أن الله تعالى فيه حقوقاً ورده إلى الحرم لكن حق الله تعالى في العين لا يمنع جواز البيع كبيع مال الذكاة والأضحية ا.هـ. فقوله في المختصر فإن «باعه أي الصيد وهو في الحرم لا مطلقاً قوله ( ومن أحرم وفي بيته أو قفصه صيد لا يرسله أي لا يجب إطلاقه لأن الصحابة كانوا يحرمون وفي بيوتهم صيود ودواجن ولم ينقل عنهم إرسالها وبذلك جرت العادة الفاشية وهي من إحدى الحجج، ولأن الواجب عدم التعرض وهو ليس بمتعرض من جهته لأنه محفوظ بالبيت والقفص لا به غير أنه في ملكه، ولو أرسله في مفازة فهو على ملكة فلا يعتبر ببقاء الملك. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان القفص في يده لأنه في القفص لا في يده بدليل جواز أخذ المصحف بغلافه للمحدث، وقيل يلزمه إرساله على وجه يضيع بأن يرسله في بيت أو يودعه عند إنسان بناء على كونه في يده بدليل أنه يصير غاصباً له بغصب القفص. وقيد بكونه في بيته أو قفصه لأنه لو كان بيده الجارحة لزمه إرساله اتفاقاً، فلو هلك وهو في يده لزمه الجزاء وإن كان مالكاً له للجناية على الإحرام بإمساكه. وفي المغرب : شاة داجن ألفت البيوت وعن الكرخي الدواجن خلاف السائمة ا هـ . فالمراد بالصيد نحو الصقر والشاهين وبالدواجن نحو الغزالة قوله : (ولو أخذ حلال صيد فأحرم ضمن مرسله) يعني عند الإمام . وقالا : لا يضمن لأن المرسل آمر بالمعروف ناه عن المنكر وما على المحسنين من سبيل. وله أنه ملك الصيد بالأخذ ملكاً محترماً فلا يبطل احترامه بإحرامه وقد أتلفه المرسل فيضمنه والواجب عليه ترك التعرض، ويمكنه ذلك بأن يخليه في بيته فإذا قطع يده عنه كان متعدياً. قال في : في الحرم أو بعد إخراجه إلى الحل وهذا حمل لكلام المتن على ما في المحيط قوله: (وقيل يلزمه إرساله الخ) أشار إلى ضعفه، قال في النهر وعبارة فخر الإسلام تؤذن بترجيح الأول حيث قال : ويستوي إن كان القفص في يده أو في رحله وقال بعض مشايخنا إن في يده يلزمه إرساله ا هـ قوله : (بأن يرسله في بيت الخ اعترضه ابن الكمال فقال : ومن قال بأن يخليه في بيته فكأنه غافل عن شمول المسألة للمحرم المسافر الذي لا بيت له ومن قال أو : فكأنه يودعه غافل عن أن يد المودع كيد المودع، كذا في حواشي مسكين عن الحموي . قلت : دفعه في النهر فقال: وأفاد في فوائد الظهيرية أن يد خادمه كرحله و به اندفع منع بعض المتأخرين إيداعه على القول بإرساله فإن يد المودع کیده فهلا كانت يد خادمه كيده قوله : فالمراد بالصيد نحو الصقر الخ) حمل في النهر الصيود على الصيود الوحشيات والدواجن على المستأنسة ثم قال : ومن خص الصيود بالطيور والدواجن بغيرها كالغزالة فقد أبعد ا.هـ. ومراده التعريض بصاحب غاية البيان فإن ما ذكره المؤلف مأخوذ منه قوله : (وهو يقتضي أن يفتي بقولهما وهو مقتضى ما في البرهان أيضاً. قال في الشرنبلالية. وفي البرهان
Book of Hajj. Chapter: If a Muhrim kills game, and in his house or cage there is game, he does not release it. And if a non-muhrim takes game and then becomes muhrim, the sender is liable. And if he takes it, if he takes a gazelle out of the Haram and sells it or slaughters it or eats it, the sale and eating are permissible, but it is disliked because it is owned property, because his hand is established on the game and they are in the Hal, which benefits ownership for him in the game just as if he had established his hand initially, except that Allah has rights in it and its return to the Haram, but the right of Allah in the object does not prevent the permissibility of sale, like the sale of property of slaughter (dhakat) and sacrifice (udhiya). End. So his statement in al-Mukhtasar: 'If he sells it' meaning the game while it is in the Haram, not absolutely. His statement: (And whoever enters ihram and in his house or cage there is game, he does not release it) meaning it is not obligatory to release it because the Companions used to enter ihram while in their houses there were game and domesticated animals, and it is not reported that they released them; and the prevalent custom has continued, and it is one of the proofs. And because the obligation is to avoid transgression, and he is not committing transgression from his side because it is confined by the house and cage, not by him, except that it is in his ownership. And if he releases it in a wilderness, it remains in his ownership, so it is not considered remaining ownership. He made it unrestricted, so it includes if the cage is in his hand because it is in the cage, not in his hand, as evidence by the permissibility of taking the Qur'an with its cover for one who has minor impurity. And it is said he must release it in a way that it is lost, such as releasing it in a house or depositing it with a person, based on it being in his hand, as evidence that he becomes a usurper of it by usurping the cage. And he restricted it to being in his house or cage because if it were in his hand as a predator, he must release it by agreement. So if it perishes while in his hand, he owes the penalty, even if he owns it, due to the offense against ihram by holding it. In al-Mughrib: 'dajin' (domesticated goat) which is accustomed to houses, and from al-Karkhi: al-dawajin (domesticated animals) as opposed to al-sa'ima (grazing livestock). End. So the intended meaning of 'sayd' is like the falcon and shaheen, and of 'dawajin' is like the gazelle. His statement: (And if a non-muhrim takes game and then becomes muhrim, the sender is liable) meaning according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he is not liable because the sender is commanding good and forbidding evil, and 'there is no way against the doers of good.' And his argument: He owned the game by taking it with respectable ownership; so its respect is not invalidated by his ihram, and the sender has destroyed it, so he is liable for it. And the obligation on him is to avoid transgression, and he can do that by leaving it in his house; if he cuts off his hand from it, he is transgressing. He said in [...] in the Haram or after taking it out to the Hal, and this is a carrying of the statement of the text to what is in al-Muhit. His statement: (And it is said he must release it, etc.) He indicated its weakness. He said in al-Nahr: The expression of Fakhr al-Islam indicates the preference of the first, for he said: It is the same whether the cage is in his hand or in his saddlebag. And some of our teachers said: if it is in his hand, he must release it. End. His statement: (by releasing it in a house, etc.) Ibn al-Kamal objected: He who said 'leave it in his house' is as if he is unaware of the inclusion of the case of a traveling muhrim who has no house; and he who said 'or deposit it' is as if he is unaware that the hand of the depositary is like the hand of the depositor. As in the margins of Muskayyan from al-Hamawi. I said: He refuted it in al-Nahr: And it was mentioned in Fawa'id al-Zahiriyya that the hand of his servant is like his saddlebag, and with this the objection of some later scholars about depositing it based on the opinion of releasing it is refuted, for the hand of the depositary is like his hand, so why is the hand of his servant not like his hand? His statement: (So the intended meaning of 'sayd' is like the falcon, etc.) In al-Nahr he carried 'sayd' on wild game and 'dawajin' on domesticated animals. Then he said: And whoever specifically defines 'sayd' as birds and 'dawajin' as other than birds like the gazelle goes far. End. And his intention is to allude to the author of Ghayat al-Bayan, for what the author mentioned is taken from him. His statement: (And it necessitates giving fatwa according to the two, and that is also the implication of al-Burhan. He said in al-Shurnubalaliyya: And in al-Burhan...
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq covers two related issues. First: a person who enters ihram while having game in his house or cage is not required to release it. The commentator supports this by the practice of the Companions who had game in their homes while in ihram, and by custom. The obligation is only to avoid direct interference, and the game is already confined by the house/cage, not by the muhrim. There is a difference of opinion if the cage is in his hand: some later scholars say he must release it, but the preferred view is that it is not necessary. Second: if a halal (non-muhrim) takes game, and then the person who sent it (the owner) becomes muhrim, the sender is liable according to Abu Hanifa, because he caused the death of the game while he is duty-bound to protect it. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he is not liable because the sender was commanding good (the halal to take the game) and the doer of good should not be blamed. The commentator notes that this dispute has practical consequences for fatwa, and the text suggests that fatwa is given according to the two Sahibayn.

Key Terms
داجن (dājin): Domesticated animal that lives in houses, as opposed to wild game.
مرسل (mursil): The sender; the owner who sends his game with another person (the halal) to hunt.
قفص (qafas): Cage or enclosure for game.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the passage, if a muhrim sends his game with a halal and the halal kills it, what is the ruling?
A) The muhrim must pay the penalty.
B) The muhrim does not pay the penalty.
C) The halal must pay the penalty.
D) The game is considered lost and no penalty applies.

Key Takeaway
A muhrim does not need to release confined game, and if he sends game with a halal and becomes muhrim, the later Hanafi fatwa relieves him of liability.

Ruling on Game in the House or Cage of a Muhrim
Ruling that a muhrim need not release game already in his house or cage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muhrim's game in his house or cage and explain the proof from the Companions' practice.

Core Idea
A muhrim need not release game already in his house or cage; confinement suffices for non-interference.

This lesson examines a specific fiqh ruling regarding a person in ihram who already possesses game in his home or cage. The key question is whether he must release it upon entering ihram. The Hanafi school, relying on the practice of the Companions and legal reasoning, rules that he is not required to release the game. We will explore the evidence, conditions, and internal school differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? What is the hukm (is it obligatory, prohibited, etc.)? The act is keeping game in one's house or cage during ihram; the ruling is that it is not obligatory to release it.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The practice of the Companions (رضي الله عنهم) who entered ihram with game in their houses and did not release it, along with the widespread custom that became a legal proof.
The proof is from the Companions' action (amal al-sahaba) and the established custom (urf).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this dalil prove the ruling? The Companions' lack of release shows that releasing was not required; their inaction in the presence of game indicates permissibility of keeping it confined.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school or scholar disagree? Within the Hanafi school, some later scholars held that if the cage is in the muhrim's hand, he must release it. The text discusses this difference.
The majority and relied-upon view is that no release is required even if the cage is in hand.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon and why? The preferred view is no release, supported by the absolute wording of the matn and the ruling that the game is confined by the cage, not by the hand.
The tarjih is based on the principle that confinement removes direct interference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي بيته أو قفصه صيد لا يرسله أي لا يجب إطلاقه لأن الصحابة كانوا يحرمون وفي بيوتهم صيود ودواجن ولم ينقل عنهم إرسالها وبذلك جرت العادة الفاشية وهي من إحدى الحجج، ولأن الواجب عدم التعرض وهو ليس بمتعرض من جهته لأنه محفوظ بالبيت والقفص لا به غير أنه في ملكه، ولو أرسله في مفازة فهو على ملكة فلا يعتبر ببقاء الملك. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان القفص في يده لأنه في القفص لا في يده بدليل جواز أخذ المصحف بغلافه للمحدث، وقيل يلزمه إرساله على وجه يضيع بأن يرسله في بيت أو يودعه عند إنسان بناء على كونه في يده بدليل أنه يصير غاصباً له بغصب القفص. وقيد بكونه في بيته أو قفصه لأنه لو كان بيده الجارحة لزمه إرساله اتفاقاً، فلو هلك وهو في يده لزمه الجزاء وإن كان مالكاً له للجناية على الإحرام بإمساكه. وفي المغرب: شاة داجن ألفت البيوت وعن الكرخي الدواجن خلاف السائمة ا هـ . فالمراد بالصيد نحو الصقر والشاهين وبالدواجن نحو الغزالة.
And if in his house or his cage there is game, he does not release it, i.e., it is not obligatory to set it free because the Companions used to enter ihram while there were game animals and domesticated animals in their houses, and it is not narrated from them that they released them, and thus the widespread custom became a proof. And because the obligation is non-interference, and he is not interfering on his part because it is confined by the house or cage, not by him, but it is in his ownership. If he releases it in a desert, it remains in his ownership, so it is not considered that ownership remains. The author's statement is absolute, so it includes the case where the cage is in his hand because the game is in the cage, not in his hand, as evidenced by the permissibility of a person in a state of minor impurity taking a mushaf with its cover. And it is said that he is obliged to release it in a way that it gets lost, such as releasing it in a house or entrusting it to a person, based on the view that it is in his hand as evidenced by the fact that he becomes a usurper by usurping the cage. And the condition of it being in his house or cage is because if it were in his hand by a predatory animal, he must release it by agreement. If it perishes while in his hand, he owes compensation even if he owns it, due to the offense against ihram by holding it. And in al-Mughrib: a domestic sheep that has become accustomed to houses. Al-Karkhi said: al-dawājin are the opposite of grazing livestock. So the meaning of 'game' (sayd) is like the falcon and shahin, and 'domesticated animals' (dawājin) is like the gazelle.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the practice of the Companions (رضي الله عنهم) and from legal reasoning. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq comments on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The ruling: a muhrim who already has game in his house or cage is not required to release it. The proof: the Companions would enter ihram while there were game and domesticated animals in their homes, and no report exists that they released them. This established a widespread practice that serves as a legal proof (hujja). The reasoning: the obligation during ihram is to avoid directly interfering with game; since the game is already confined by the house or cage, the muhrim is not actively interfering. The game remains in his ownership. If he were to release it into the wilderness, it stays his property. The absolute wording of the matn covers even if the cage is in his hand, because the animal is contained by the cage, not by his hand. This is supported by the analogy of a person in minor impurity taking a mushaf with its cover (the hand touches the cover, not the mushaf). Some scholars hold that if the cage is in his hand, he must release it in a way that the animal is lost (e.g., release it inside a house or entrust it to someone), because his hand is considered in direct contact. The author notes that if the game is held by a predatory animal (bird of prey) in his hand, he must release it by consensus. If it perishes while in his hand, he owes compensation even if he owned it, because holding it is an offense against ihram. The text also clarifies the terms: 'sayd' here refers to birds like falcons, and 'dawājin' refers to animals like gazelles that have become domesticated. The overall ruling is that confinement substitutes for the muhrim's direct action.

Key Terms
صيد (sayd): Game animals that are wild and permissible to hunt outside ihram; here it includes birds of prey like falcons.
دواجن (dawājin): Domesticated animals that have become accustomed to homes, like gazelles that live near people.
إرسال (irsāl): Releasing the game from confinement; whether obligatory or not depends on context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a muhrim has a falcon in its cage in his house, must he release it?
A) Yes, because he is in ihram and cannot own game.
B) No, because the game is confined and he is not interfering.
C) Yes, if the cage is in his hand, but not if it is in his house.
D) No, only if the game is domesticated.

Key Takeaway
A muhrim is not required to release game already confined in his house or cage, as the obligation is non-interference, and confinement fulfills that.

Liability of Releasing Game from a Muhrim: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability of releaser when taker becomes muhrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the liability of a person who releases game taken by a non-muhrim who then enters ihram, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When a non-muhrim catches game and then becomes muhrim, the releaser of the game is not liable according to the relied-upon fatwa.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute concerning property rights and the obligation to avoid sin during ihram. Imam Abu Hanifa holds the releaser liable because the taker owned the game and the releaser destroyed property. The two companions (Sahibayn) argue that the releaser is a doer of good by helping the muhrim avoid a prohibited act, and thus incurs no liability. The later preferred view follows the Sahibayn, as analogized from the case of breaking musical instruments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Understand the scenario: a halal person (non-muhrim) catches game, then becomes muhrim. Another person (mursil) releases the game, causing its loss. The key question: is the releaser liable for compensation (damān)?
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that the taker owned the game by capture (a protected ownership). Ihram does not nullify that ownership. The releaser destroyed it, so he must compensate. The taker can avoid sin by keeping the game in his house.
Property rights are protected even during ihram.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that the releaser is commanding good and forbidding evil by helping the muhrim avoid a prohibited act. They cite the principle 'there is no way against the doers of good' (Qur'an 9:91). Thus, no liability.
Their view prioritizes the avoidance of sin over property rights in this context.
4
Understand the tarjih by analogy
The author of al-Hidayah analogizes this dispute to the one about breaking musical instruments (ma'āzif): Abu Hanifa holds the breaker liable, the Sahibayn do not. The fatwa in that case is according to the Sahibayn, implying the same for the game case.
The analogy shows that the principle of commanding good overrides property rights when the object is inherently prohibited to the owner.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn: the releaser is not liable. This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولو أخذ حلال صيد فأحرم ضمن مرسله) يعني عند الإمام. وقالا: لا يضمن لأن المرسل آمر بالمعروف ناه عن المنكر وما على المحسنين من سبيل. وله أنه ملك الصيد بالأخذ ملكاً محترماً فلا يبطل احترامه بإحرامه وقد أتلفه المرسل فيضمنه والواجب عليه ترك التعرض، ويمكنه ذلك بأن يخليه في بيته فإذا قطع يده عنه كان متعدياً. قال في الهداية: ونظيره الاختلاف في كسر المعازف ا هـ. وهو يقتضي أن يفتى بقولهما هنا لأن الفتوى على قولهما في عدم الضمان بكسر المعازف ا هـ . وهي آلات اللهو كالطنبور.
His statement: (If a non-muhrim takes game and then becomes muhrim, the one who releases it is liable) means according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He is not liable because the releaser is commanding good and forbidding evil, and there is no way against the doers of good. And for him (Abu Hanifa) is that he (the taker) owned the game by taking it, a protected ownership, so its protection is not nullified by his ihram, and the releaser has destroyed it, so he guarantees it. And the obligation on him (the taker) is to avoid interference, and he can do that by leaving it in his house. If he removes his hand from it, he is transgressing. He said in al-Hidayah: Its analogy is the difference of opinion regarding breaking musical instruments. And this implies that fatwa should be given according to their view here because fatwa is given according to their view regarding no liability for breaking musical instruments. And they are instruments of amusement like the tanbur.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the liability of a person who releases game after it has been taken by a non-muhrim who subsequently enters ihram. The case: A person (halal) catches game, then becomes muhrim. Another person (the 'mursil') releases the game, causing it to be lost. Is the releaser liable? Imam Abu Hanifa says yes: the taker owned the game by taking it (a protected ownership), and that ownership is not invalidated by his ihram. The releaser destroyed that property, so he must compensate (damān). The taker can avoid violation by keeping the game in his house; if he releases his control (by entrusting it or letting it go), he is not forced to. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say no liability, because the releaser is seen as commanding good (enjoining right and forbidding wrong) by helping the muhrim avoid a prohibited act (possessing game). They cite the verse 'There is no way against the doers of good.' The author of al-Hidayah analogizes this dispute to the one regarding breaking musical instruments (ma'āzif): Abu Hanifa holds the breaker liable, the Sahibayn do not, and the fatwa is given according to the Sahibayn. Hence, in this game case, the fatwa is also according to the Sahibayn (no liability). The text clarifies that the relied-upon position is that the releaser is not liable.

Key Terms
ضمن (damān): Liability; obligation to compensate for loss or destruction of property.
مرسل (mursil): The person who releases the game from captivity.
آمر بالمعروف (āmir bil-ma'rūf): One who enjoins what is right; here used to justify releasing game to prevent sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon fatwa (mufta bihi), if a non-muhrim catches game, then becomes muhrim, and someone else releases the game causing its loss, what is the ruling?
A) The releaser must pay compensation to the taker.
B) The releaser is not liable because he is commanding good.
C) The taker must pay compensation for not securing the game.
D) The game is considered ownerless.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that the releaser of game from a muhrim is not liable, following the Sahibayn's view that he is commanding good.

If a Muhrim Takes Game, He Does Not Own It: The Hanafi Position
Ruling with proof and exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muhrim's ownership of game through voluntary vs. compulsory means and apply the qiyas to determine the validity of a sale by a muhrim.

Core Idea
Game taken by a muhrim is like wine and pig—no ownership arises; only inheritance grants ownership.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a key fiqh principle: a person in ihram cannot own game through any voluntary acquisition. The ruling is derived by analogy to wine and pig, which are inherently prohibited and thus unownable. However, an important exception exists for inheritance, which is a compulsory transfer. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the law regarding hunting and trade during hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states that if a muhrim takes game, he is not liable and does not own it. Note that this applies to voluntary means of acquisition.
2
Understand the reason (ta'lil): analogy to wine and pig
The reason given is that game is prohibited for the muhrim, so it becomes like wine and pig—items that cannot be owned by a Muslim. The analogy is explicit: 'so it becomes like wine and pig'.
This is a qiyas based on the shared attribute of prohibition.
3
Distinguish voluntary vs. compulsory means
The passage clarifies that 'means' refers to voluntary acquisitions like purchase, gift, charity, bequest. Compulsory means like inheritance are an exception: a muhrim does own game inherited from a relative.
This distinction is critical for applying the ruling correctly.
4
Apply to the scenario of release and recapture
The passage examines two situations: (1) if the muhrim owned the game before releasing it, after becoming halal he can reclaim it from the catcher; (2) if he never owned it (e.g., he took it in ihram), he cannot reclaim it.
The key factor is whether ownership was established prior to release.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولو أخذه محرم لا يضمن) أي لا يضمن مرسله من يده اتفاقاً لأنه لم يملكه بالأخذ لأن المحرم لا يملك الصيد بسبب من الأسباب محرم عليه فصار كالخمر والخنزير. كذا قالوا ومقتضاه أنه لو باعه المحرم فبيعه غير منعقد أصلاً، وقد صرح في المحيط بفساد البيع. والمراد من قولهم المحرم لا يملك الصيد بسبب من الأسباب الاختيارية كالشراء والهبة والصدقة والوصية وأما السبب الجبري فيملكه به كما إذا ورث من قريبه صيداً كما صرح به في المحيط. وأشار إلى أنه لو أرسله المحرم فأخذه حلال ثم حل مرسله فإنه يأخذه مرسله في الصورة الأولى ممن هو في يده لأنه لم يخرج آخر ضمنا ملكه ولا يأخذه في الثانية لأنه لم يكن مالكاً أصلاً.
His statement: (If a muhrim takes it, he is not liable) i.e., the one who releases it from his hand is not liable by agreement, because he (the muhrim) did not own it by taking, since the muhrim does not own game through any [voluntary] means that are prohibited for him, so it becomes like wine and pig. Thus they said, and its implication is that if the muhrim sells it, his sale is not valid at all, and it is explicitly stated in al-Muhit that the sale is void. And what is meant by their statement 'the muhrim does not own game through any of the means' is the optional means like purchase, gift, charity, and bequest. As for a compulsory means, he owns it through it, such as if he inherits game from his relative, as stated in al-Muhit. And he indicated that if the muhrim releases it and a non-muhrim takes it, then the releaser becomes halal, then the releaser takes it in the first situation from the one in whose hand it is, because his ownership did not exit except with liability, and he does not take it in the second situation because he was not an owner at all.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling that if a muhrim takes game, he is not liable (i.e., he does not owe compensation if it is lost) and importantly, he does not own it. The reason: a muhrim cannot own game through any voluntary means (like purchase, gift, charity, bequest) because game is forbidden for him. Therefore, taking it is like taking wine or pig—it does not confer ownership. Consequently, if he sells it, the sale is void (batil). However, an exception exists for compulsory means: if he inherits game from a relative, he does own it, because inheritance does not involve a voluntary acquisition. The text then discusses a scenario: if a muhrim releases the game, then a halal person catches it, then the muhrim exits ihram (becomes halal). The original releaser can take it back from the catcher in the first situation (where he had owned it) because his ownership did not end except with liability; but in the second situation (where he was a muhrim who never owned it), he cannot take it. This clarifies that ownership of game is suspended during ihram only for voluntary acquisitions.

Key Terms
أسباب اختيارية (asbāb ikhtiyāriyya): Voluntary means of acquiring ownership, such as purchase, gift, charity, bequest.
سبب جبري (sabab jabrī): Compulsory means, like inheritance, where ownership is forced upon the heir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A muhrim inherits a falcon from his deceased father. According to the Hanafi school, does he own it?
A) No, because a muhrim cannot own any game.
B) Yes, because inheritance is a compulsory means of ownership.
C) Yes, but only if he releases it immediately.
D) No, because the falcon is prohibited in ihram.

Key Takeaway
A muhrim does not own game taken by voluntary means; only compulsory means like inheritance confer ownership.

Liability and Recovery When a Muhrim Kills Game Taken by Another Muhrim
Ruling with proof: joint liability and recovery for game taken and killed by muhrims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on joint liability when a muhrim kills game held by another muhrim, explain the qiyas analogy to a mudabbar, and identify the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Both muhrims aggress, each pays a full penalty, but prior taking creates a right to recover from the killer.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq tackles a specific scenario in Hajj: a muhrim takes game, and another muhrim kills it. The text establishes that both commit aggression and each owes the full jaza' (penalty for violating ihram). However, the taker can recover from the killer the value he paid, because his prior taking creates a quasi-ownership right that attaches to the substitute. The ruling is supported by qiyas to a usurper of a mudabbar, but the Sahibayn prefer istihsan, creating an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two aggressions
The taker aggresses by taking (preventing free movement), the killer by killing. Each act independently violates ihram.
The jaza' is wajib for each violation.
2
Understand the liability and recovery
Each pays a full jaza'. The taker recovers from the killer because paying the guarantee establishes ownership in the substitute, manifested by prior taking.
Analogy: usurper of mudabbar recovers from killer.
3
Analyze the qiyas dalil
The text draws an analogy to a usurper of a mudabbar: even though the usurper doesn't own the slave, his possession gives him a right to recover from someone who kills it. Here, the taker's right is even stronger because a muhrim can own game through inheritance.
The dalil is qiyas; no direct nass.
4
Distinguish variations in killer's status
If killer is non-muhrim: penalty depends on location (Haram only), but taker still recovers. If killer is non-Muslim or child: no religious penalty, but taker recovers value as a right of people. If animal kills: only taker liable, no recovery.
The recovery is consistent across these variants.
5
Note the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa holds the ruling as qiyas; the Sahibayn consider it istihsan (similar to their view on destroying musical instruments). The mufta bihi is not stated in this passage, but in the analogous case the fatwa follows the Sahibayn.
This shows how istihsan can override qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فإن قتله محرم آخر ضمناً ورجع آخذه على قاتله) لوجود الجناية منهما الآخذ بالأخذ والقاتل بالقتل فلزم كل واحد جزاء كامل، ورجع الآخذ على القاتل بما غرم لأن أداء الضمان يوجب ثبوت الملك في المضمون بالأخذ السابق وقد تعذر إظهاره في عين الصيد فأظهرناه في بدله لأنه قائم مقام الملك في حق الرجوع ببدله كمن غصب مدبراً وقتله إنسان في يده يرجع بما ضمن على القاتل وإن لم يملك المدبر فكذا هذا، بل أولى لأن المدبر لا يملك بسبب ما والمحرم يملك الصيد بسبب الإرث كما قدمناه وإنما قيد بكون القاتل محرماً آخر لقوله «ضمناً» فإن القاتل لو كان حلالاً فإن كان الصيد في الحرم لزمه الجزاء، وإن كان من صيد الحل لا ضمان عليه بالقتل لكن يرجع عليه الآخذ بما ضمن فالرجوع لا فرق فيه بين المحرم والحلال. وفي المحيط: ولو كان القاتل نصرانياً أو صبياً فلا جزاء عليه الله تعالى ويرجع عليه الآخذ بقيمته لأنه يلزمه حقوق العباد دون حقوق الله تعالى. وقيد بكون القاتل آدمياً فإنه لو قتله بهيمة إنسان فإن الجزاء على الآخذ وحده ولا رجوع للآخذ على أحد كما ذكره الأسبيجابي. وأطلق في الرجوع فشمل ما إذا كان الآخذ كفر بالصوم فيرجع الآخذ بالقيمة مطلقاً وهو ظاهر ما قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله هو القياس، وقولهما استحسان وهذا نظير اختلافهم فيمن أتلف المعازف.
His statement: (If another muhrim kills it, both are liable and the taker recovers from the killer) because there is aggression from both: the taker by taking and the killer by killing, so each owes a full penalty (jaza'), and the taker recovers from the killer what he paid, because paying the guarantee establishes ownership in the guaranteed item by prior taking, and it was impossible to manifest it in the actual game, so we manifested it in its substitute because it stands in the place of ownership regarding the right to recover its substitute. Like one who usurps a mudabbar (slave promised freedom upon owner's death) and another kills it in his hand; he recovers what he paid from the killer, even though he does not own the mudabbar. So this is similar, rather more so, because the mudabbar is not owned by any means, while the muhrim owns game through inheritance as we mentioned. And the condition that the killer is another muhrim is due to his statement 'both are liable'. If the killer were non-muhrim, then if the game was in the haram, he owes penalty; if it was from game of the halal (outside haram), he owes no penalty for killing, but the taker recovers from him what he paid. So the recovery does not differ between muhrim and non-muhrim. And in al-Muhit: If the killer were a Christian or a child, there is no penalty on him (by rights of Allah), but the taker recovers its value from him because he is liable for the rights of people, not the rights of Allah. And it is conditioned that the killer is human; if an animal kills it, then the penalty is only on the taker, and the taker has no recovery from anyone, as mentioned by al-Asbijabi. And he gave absolute recovery, including the case where the taker expiates by fasting, so the taker recovers the value absolutely. This is apparent from the statement of Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) that it is qiyas, and their statement is istihsan, and this is similar to their difference regarding one who destroys musical instruments.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific scenario: a muhrim takes game (but does not own it), and then another muhrim kills it. Both commit aggression: the taker by taking (preventing the free movement of the game) and the killer by killing. Therefore, each owes a full penalty (jaza') for violating ihram. However, the taker can recover from the killer the amount he paid, because the taker's earlier taking created a quasi-ownership right that is manifested in the substitute (the penalty value). The text draws an analogy with a usurper of a mudabbar slave: if another kills the mudabbar, the usurper can recover from the killer, even though the usurper does not own the mudabbar. Here, the taker's right is even stronger because a muhrim can own game by inheritance. The killer is specified as another muhrim because if the killer were a non-muhrim (halal), the ruling differs: if the game is within the Haram, the halal killer owes a penalty for killing in the Haram; if the game is outside the Haram, the halal killer has no penalty for killing, but the taker still recovers from him. If the killer is a non-Muslim or a child, they are not liable for the religious penalty (jaza'), but they are liable for the value to the taker because it is a right of people. If an animal kills the game, the penalty is only on the taker (he is solely liable) and he cannot recover from anyone else. The text also mentions that according to Abu Hanifa, this ruling (liability and recovery) is based on qiyas (analogy), while the Sahibayn consider it istihsan (juristic preference), similar to their difference regarding destruction of musical instruments. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) in that analogous case is the Sahibayn's view (no liability), so perhaps here too? The text does not explicitly resolve, but the discussion shows the school's method.

Key Terms
جزاء (jaza'): Penalty for violating ihram by killing game; can be offering an animal, feeding the poor, or fasting.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the owner's death (tadbir).
قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning; here Abu Hanifa's view is based on qiyas.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; the Sahibayn prefer a different ruling based on equity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a muhrim takes game, and then another muhrim kills it, what is the ruling on the liability according to the text?
A) Only the killer is liable.
B) Only the taker is liable.
C) Both are liable, and the taker can recover from the killer.
D) Neither is liable because game is not owned.

Key Takeaway
When a muhrim takes game and another muhrim kills it, both owe the full penalty, but the taker recovers from the killer due to the right established by prior taking.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Recourse for a Fasting Muhrim
Intra-Hanafi dispute on recourse when taker fasts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether a muhrim who takes game can recover its value from another muhrim who kills it, particularly when the taker expiates by fasting, and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
In an intra-Hanafi dispute, the relied-upon view is that fasting bars recourse, exemplifying istihsan overriding qiyas in compensatory claims.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq examines a nuanced scenario: a muhrim (person in ihram) takes game (which he cannot own), and then another muhrim kills it. Both incur a penalty, but the taker may have recourse (ruju) against the killer for the value paid. The central dispute arises when the taker expiates by fasting rather than paying a monetary penalty: does he still have the right to claim compensation? Abu Hanifa says yes (qiyas), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say no (istihsan). The passage resolves that the fatwa follows the Sahibayn, making this a key example of how istihsan can override qiyas in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Case
Read the passage to identify the exact scenario: a muhrim takes game, another muhrim kills it. Both are liable for one complete penalty each. The taker pays (or expiates) and then seeks recourse from the killer.
Also note variations: killer non-muhrim, child, animal, etc.
2
Locate the Intra-Madhhab Dispute
The dispute centers on whether the taker's recourse depends on the form of expiation. Abu Hanifa holds he can always recover the value (qiyas). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that if he fasts (no monetary payment), he loses the right to recourse (istihsan).
The key phrase is 'kffara bil-sawm' (expiated by fasting).
3
Analyze the Analogies
The text analogizes to the case of breaking musical instruments: there, the fatwa follows the Sahibayn (no guarantee). By analogy, the same applies here. Also, the case of a mudabbir (contingently freed slave) is used to illustrate how payment establishes ownership of the substitute.
Identify the qiyas (Abu Hanifa) and istihsan (Sahibayn) reasoning.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The passage explicitly says the fatwa is given by the Sahibayn's view in the analogous case, so here the relied-upon position is that if the taker fasts, he has no recourse. Note that later authorities (Fath al-Qadir) also prefer this view.
This is an example of tarjih (preference) based on later practice.
5
Evaluate the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether the killer must pay the taker if the taker fasted. Under Abu Hanifa's view, the killer must pay; under the Sahibayn's view, the killer is free from any claim by the taker.
This difference affects real-world claims for compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج/ فصل إن قتل محرم صيداً
محرم لا يضمن فإن قتله محرم آخر ضمناً ورجع آخذه على قاتله
الهداية : ونظيره الاختلاف في كسر المعازف ا هـ. وهو يقتضي أن يفتى بقولهما هنا لأن الفتوى على قولهما في عدم الضمان بكسر المعازف ا هـ . وهي آلات اللهو كالطنبور. أطلق في الإرسال فشمل ما إذا أرسله من يده الحقيقية أو الحكمية أي من بيته لكن يضمنه في الثاني اتفاقاً. كذا في شرح ابن الملك للمجمع قوله : (ولو أخذه محرم لا يضمن) أي لا يضمن مرسله من يده اتفاقاً لأنه لم يملكه بالأخذ لأن المحرم لا يملك الصيد بسبب من الأسباب محرم عليه فصار كالخمر والخنزير. كذا قالوا ومقتضاه أنه لو باعه المحرم فبيعه غير منعقد أصلاً، وقد صرح في المحيط بفساد البيع. والمراد من قولهم المحرم لا يملك الصيد بسبب من الأسباب الاختيارية كالشراء والهبة والصدقة والوصية وأما السبب الجبري فيملكه به كما إذا ورث من قريبه صيداً كما صرح به في المحيط. وأشار إلى أنه لو أرسله المحرم فأخذه حلال ثم حل مرسله فإنه يأخذه مرسله في الصورة الأولى ممن هو في يده لأنه لم يخرج عن ملكه ولا يأخذه في الثانية لأنه لم يكن مالكاً أصلاً قوله : (فإن قتله محرم آخر ضمنا ورجع الآخذ على القاتل لوجود الجناية منهما الآخذ بالأخذ والقاتل بالقتل فلزم كل «ضمناً» فإن القاتل لو كان حلالاً فإن كان الصيد في الحرم لزمه الجزاء، وإن كان من صيد الحل لا ضمان عليه بالقتل لكن يرجع عليه الآخذ بما ضمن فالرجوع لا فرق فيه بين المحرم والحلال. وفي المحيط : ولو كان القاتل نصرانياً أو صبياً فلا جزاء عليه ويرجع عليه الآخذ بقيمته لأنه يلزمه حقوق العباد دون حقوق الله تعالى. وقيد بكون القاتل آدمياً فإنه لو قتله بهيمة إنسان فإن الجزاء على الآخذ وحده ولا رجوع للآخذ على Book of Hajj / Section: If a muhrim kills game. A muhrim does not guarantee, but if another muhrim kills it, they both guarantee and the taker has recourse against the killer. Al-Hidayah: Its analogy is the difference in breaking musical instruments. It implies that fatwa is given by their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) opinion here because fatwa is on their opinion regarding no guarantee for breaking musical instruments. They are instruments of amusement like the tanbur. He made absolute in sending, so it includes whether he sent it from his actual hand or constructive hand, i.e., from his home, but he guarantees it in the second case by agreement. As in Sharh Ibn al-Malik for al-Majma. He said: 'If a muhrim takes it, he does not guarantee' i.e., the sender does not guarantee from his hand by agreement because he did not own it by taking because the muhrim does not own game by any cause as it is prohibited to him, so it becomes like wine and pig. They said this, and its implication is that if the muhrim sold it, his sale is not valid at all, and al-Muhit explicitly states the sale is void. What they mean by 'muhrim does not own game by any cause' is by voluntary causes like purchase, gift, charity, bequest, but by a compulsory cause he owns it, such as when he inherits game from his relative, as clarified in al-Muhit. He indicated that if the muhrim released it and a non-muhrim caught it, then the releaser's ihram ended, he takes it from the one in whose hand it is in the first case because it did not leave his ownership, and he does not take it in the second because he was never the owner. He said: 'If another muhrim kills it, they both guarantee, and the taker has recourse against the killer' due to the offense from both: the taker by taking, the killer by killing, so each owes a complete penalty, and the taker has recourse against the killer for what he paid because paying the guarantee establishes ownership of the guaranteed thing by the prior taking, but since it is impossible to manifest it in the actual game, we manifest it in its substitute because it stands in place of ownership in terms of recourse for its substitute. Like one who seizes a mudabbir and a person kills it in his hand, he has recourse for what he guaranteed against the killer, even though he does not own the mudabbir. This is even more so because the mudabbir is not owned by any cause, while the muhrim owns game through inheritance as we mentioned. He restricted it to the killer being another muhrim because of his saying 'both guarantee'. If the killer were non-muhrim, then if the game is in the Haram, he owes the penalty, and if it is game of the Hill, there is no guarantee on him for killing, but the taker has recourse against him for what he paid. The recourse is the same whether the killer is muhrim or non-muhrim. In al-Muhit: If the killer was a Christian or a child, there is no penalty on him, and the taker has recourse against him for its value because obligations to people are binding, not obligations to Allah. He restricted it to the killer being human, for if an animal killed it, the penalty is solely on the taker, and the taker has no recourse against anyone, as mentioned by al-Asbijabi. He made absolute in recourse, so it includes the case where the taker expiated by fasting; the taker has recourse for the value absolutely, which is the apparent meaning of Abu Hanifa's statement: it is qiyas, while their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) statement is istihsan, and this is analogous to their difference in the one who destroys musical instruments. He said: 'As for the compulsory cause...' Al-Nahr said: But in al-Siraj that he does not own it by inheritance, and that is apparent as will come. He said: 'In the first case', the author's statement: 'If a non-muhrim took it', and the second case refers to his statement 'If a muhrim took it'. He said: 'And it is difficult to manifest it' i.e., manifest ownership in the guaranteed thing since it was previously stated that he does not own it by any cause. In al-Nihaya: But al-Muhit states from al-Muntaqa that if he expiated by fasting, he has no recourse because he did not pay compensation. The commentator resolved it and it was chosen in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute passage expanding on a ruling from the matn. The passage addresses the case where a muhrim takes game (which he cannot own due to his state of ihram) and then another muhrim kills that game. The ruling establishes that both are liable for the penalty (jaza) — the taker for taking and the killer for killing. However, the taker has recourse (ruju) against the killer to recover the value he paid as compensation. The reasoning is that payment of the guarantee retroactively establishes ownership by the prior taking, and since the actual game cannot be owned, its substitute (value) stands in. An analogy is drawn to a mudabbir (a slave whose manumission is contingent on the master's death) which is seized and then killed: the seizer, though not the owner, can claim compensation from the killer. The text then discusses variations: if the killer is non-muhrim, the taker still has recourse, but if the game is outside the Haram, the non-muhrim killer owes no penalty to Allah, only recourse to the taker. If the killer is a child or a non-Muslim, he owes no penalty (since they are not addressed for ritual penalties), but he is liable for the value as a property right. The key intra-madhhab dispute is about recourse when the taker expiates by fasting (instead of paying value): Abu Hanifa (qiyas) holds that the taker can still recover the value from the killer, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (istihsan) hold that he cannot because he did not actually pay a monetary amount. The passage notes that the fatwa is given according to the Sahibayn in the analogous case of breaking musical instruments, implying the same here. Later, a note from al-Nihaya reports that the preferred position is no recourse if he fasted, as chosen in Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
المحرم (al-muhrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
الضمان (al-daman): Financial liability or guarantee; here it refers to the obligation to pay the value or penalty for the game.
الرجع (al-ruju): Recourse or the right to claim compensation from another party who is jointly liable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in this passage, if a muhrim takes game, another muhrim kills it, and the taker expiates by fasting, does the taker have recourse (ruju) against the killer?
A) Yes, because Abu Hanifa holds qiyas allows recourse.
B) No, because the fatwa follows the Sahibayn who say no recourse if fasting.
C) Yes, because the taker always has recourse regardless of how he expiates.
D) No, because the killer is not liable if the taker fasts.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the taker of game in ihram loses the right to recourse from the killer if he expiates by fasting, following the Sahibayn's position which is adopted in fatwa.

Ruling on Cutting Plants in the Haram
Explanation of the ruling on cutting grass and trees in the Haram with conditions and exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on cutting vegetation in the Haram, identify the conditions and exceptions, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on double liability.

Core Idea
Cutting fresh vegetation of the Haram is haram and requires a value guarantee, unless dry or specifically exempted like idhkhir.

The Haram of Makkah enjoys a special sanctity; its vegetation is protected. This lesson explains what happens if someone cuts grass or a tree in the Haram. We will examine the ruling from the matn, the proof from hadith, the conditions that trigger liability, and a nuanced disagreement among the Hanafi imams regarding whether a landowner can also claim compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is cutting fresh (non-dry) grass or a tree in the Haram that is not owned and not cultivated by people. The ruling is that it is haram and incurs a guarantee (daman) of the plant's value.
Dry plants are excluded; also excluded are idhkhir and plants grown by people.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith in Sahih Bukhari and Muslim: 'لا يختلي خلاها ولا يعضد شوكها' (Its lush grass shall not be cut, nor its thorns broken). This establishes the prohibition.
The hadith is mutawatir in meaning, though ahad in transmission.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The negation of permission (لا يختلي) indicates a prohibition, which in Hanafi usul implies haram. The 'khala' is interpreted as fresh herbage, so the ruling covers fresh plants; dry ones are not covered.
The definition of 'khala' vs 'hashish' is discussed by linguists and jurists.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on double liability. If a tree grows on owned land without cultivation, according to Abu Hanifa only one value is owed (to the Haram), while according to the Sahibayn two values are owed: one to the Haram and one to the landowner.
This arises from differing views on whether Haram land can be privately owned.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text follows Abu Hanifa's view, as the matn's restriction 'non-owned' aligns with the Imam's position. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that only one value is owed unless the plant was cultivated by a person.
Al-Hidayah and other reliable works prefer Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن قطع حشيش الحرم أو شجر غير مملوك ولا مما ينبته الناس ضمن قيمته إلا فيما جف) لحديث الصحيحين لا يختلي خلاها ولا يعضد شوكها والخلا بالقصر الحشيش واختلاؤه قطعه، والعضد قطع الشجر من باب ضرب كذا في المغرب. وفي فتح القدير : الرطب من الكلأ والشجر اسم للقائم الذي بحيث ينمو فإذا جف فهو حطب. وقد ذكر النووي عن أهل اللغة أن العشب والخلا اسم للرطب والحشيش اسم لليابس، وأن الفقهاء يطلقون الحشيش على الرطب واليابس مجازاً، وسمي الرطب حشيشاً باعتبار ما يؤول إليه ا هـ . فقد أفاد الحديث أن المحرم هو المنسوب إلى الحرم والنسبة إليه على الكمال عند عدم النسبة إلى غيره. قيد بكونه غير مملوك لأنه لو قطع ما أنبته الناس فإنه لا يضمن للحرم بل يضمن قيمته لمالكه، وقيد بقوله «مما لا ينبته الناس لأنه لو قطع ما نبت بنفسه وهو من جنس ما ينبته الناس فإنه لا ضمان عليه لأنه إنما نبت ببذر وقع فيه فصار كما إذا علم أنه أنبته الناس ولهذا يحل قطع الشجر المثمر لأنه أقيم كونه مثمراً مقام إنبات الناس لأن إنبات الناس في الغالب للثمر. وقال في المحيط وغيره : ولو نبت شجر أم غيلان بأرض رجل فقطعه آخر لزمه قیمتان قيمة للشرع وقيمة للمالك كالصيد المملوك في الحرم أو الإحرام ا هـ. وهي واردة على المصنف فالمراد من قوله أو شجراً غير مملوك الشجر الذي لم ينبته أحد، سواء كان مملوكا أو لا، ولذا لم يذكر الملك في أكثر الكتب إنما ذكروا ما لم ينبته الناس. فالحاصل أن النابت في الحرم إما أذخراً وغيره، فالأول سيستثنيه، والثاني على ثلاثة إما أن يجف أو مثله سقط الضمان وإلا فلا ا هـ . أي وإن لم يعد مكانه مثله بل أخلف دون الأول لا يسقط الضمان بل كان عليه ما نقص، وإن جف أصله كان عليه قيمته (شرح) قوله : (لأنه لو قطع ما أنبته الناس الخ) فيه أن هذا خارج بقول المصنف ولا مما ينبته الناس فيلزم عليه التكرار وإغناء أحد القيدين عن الآخر فإن الثاني يشمل النابت بنفسه والمستنبت تأمل قوله : (وهي واردة على المصنف) قال في النهر : والحق أن هذا القيد يعني قوله غير مملوك إنما هو لإخراج ما لو أنبته إنسان فلا شيء بقطعه لملكه إياه، ولا يرد ما مر - أي عن المحيط - لأن المتون إنما هي على قول الإمام وإن رجح خلافه، وقد علمت أن تملك أرض الحرم على قول الإمام غير متحقق فوجوب القيمتين غير متصور، وهذا مما خفى على كثير من الناظرين في هذا المقام. وبهذا التقرير استغنى عن قوله في البحر «المراد بغير المملوك الذي لم ينبته أحد سواء كان مملوكاً أولاً اهـ. وفيما يأتي من كلام الفتح إشارة إلى هذا الجواب لكن لا يخفى ما فيه على المتأمل النبيه لأن الاحتراز عما لو أنبته إنسان إنما يتأتى على قولهما بتحقق ملك الحرم وما يستنبت فيه لا على قول الإمام قوله : (فما) فيه الجزاء هو ما نبت بنفسه الخ
He said: 'If he cuts grass of the Haram or a tree that is not owned and not of what people grow, he guarantees its value except when it has dried.' Due to the hadith in the Two Sahihs: 'Its lush grass shall not be cut, nor its thorns broken.' 'Khala' (with shortening) is grass, and 'ikhtila' is cutting it; 'adad' is cutting trees from the chapter of darb as in al-Mughrib. In Fath al-Qadir: 'The moist of herbage and tree is a name for the standing that grows, and when it dries, it is firewood.' Al-Nawawi mentioned from the language scholars that 'ushb and khala are names for moist, and hashish is a name for dry, and jurists use hashish for both moist and dry metaphorically, and the moist is called hashish considering its future state. So the hadith indicates that what is prohibited is that which is ascribed to the Haram, and the ascription is complete when there is no ascription to another. He restricted it to being not owned because if he cuts what people grew, he does not guarantee for the Haram but guarantees its value to its owner. He restricted it by his saying 'of what people do not grow' because if he cuts what grew by itself and it is of the kind that people grow, there is no guarantee because it grew from a seed that fell, so it becomes as if he knew that people grew it. Hence, cutting fruit-bearing trees is permissible because its fruitfulness is regarded as people's growth, since people's growth is mostly for fruit. In al-Muhit and elsewhere: 'If a tree of umm ghilan grows on a man's land and another cuts it, he owes two values: a value for the Sharia and a value for the owner, like owned game in the Haram or ihram.' This is an objection against the author, so the meaning of his saying 'or a tree not owned' is a tree that no one grew, whether it is owned or not. Therefore, ownership is not mentioned in most books; they only mention what people did not grow. In summary, the growth in the Haram is either idhkhir or other. The first will be exempted. The second is of three types: either it dries, or similar, then the guarantee drops; otherwise not. That is, if its place does not produce similar but produces inferior, the guarantee does not drop but he owes the deficiency; and if its root dries, he owes its value. (Explanation) He said: 'Because if he cuts what people grew...' It contains that this is excluded by the author's statement 'and not of what people grow', so there is repetition and one of the two restrictions renders the other redundant, as the second includes naturally grown and cultivated. Consider his saying: 'This is an objection against the author.' Al-Nahr said: 'The truth is that this restriction, i.e. his saying 'not owned', is only to exclude what a person grew, so there is nothing for cutting it due to his ownership, and the objection from al-Muhit does not apply because the texts are according to the Imam's statement even if the contrary is preferred, and you know that ownership of Haram land according to the Imam is not actual, so the imposition of two values is not conceivable, and this is hidden from many observers. With this explanation, the statement in al-Bahr becomes superfluous: 'The meaning of not owned is that which no one grew, whether owned or not.' In the coming words of al-Fath, there is an indication of this answer, but it is not hidden from the attentive scholar, because the avoidance of what a person grew only applies according to their (Sahibayn) view of actual ownership of the Haram and what is grown in it, not according to the Imam. He said: 'So what' therein the penalty is that which grew by itself.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on cutting plants in the Haram. The matn states: if a person cuts grass or a tree that is not owned and not among what people cultivate, he guarantees its value, except if it has dried. The proof is the hadith from Sahih Bukhari and Muslim: 'Do not cut its lush grass, nor break its thorns.' The commentary defines key terms: 'khala' is fresh grass, 'ikhtila' is cutting it, 'adad' is cutting trees. The hadith establishes the sanctity of the Haram's vegetation. The conditions are: the plant must not be owned (i.e., not privately owned), and it must not be from what people normally grow (e.g., cultivated crops). If it is cultivated by someone, the cutter owes the value to the owner, not to the Haram. If it grew naturally but is of a type that people usually grow (e.g., fruit trees), then there is no guarantee because it is considered as if people grew it. An important exception is idhkhir (a type of fragrant grass), which is allowed to be cut as per the Sunnah. The passage also discusses a nuance from al-Muhit: if a tree grows on someone's land without cultivation and another cuts it, he owes two values: one for the Sharia (since it is in the Haram) and one for the landowner. This seems to contradict the author's wording, but the commentator resolves it by noting that according to Abu Hanifa, the Haram itself is not owned by anyone, so the owner cannot claim a separate value; thus the author's restriction to 'non-owned' is meant to exclude cultivated plants. The final summary: vegetation in the Haram is either idhkhir (exempted) or other; if other, if it dries or regrows similarly after cutting, no guarantee; if not, guarantee remains for the deficiency or full value.

Key Terms
الحشيش (al-hashish): Fresh grass or herbage; literally means dry grass but jurists use it for both moist and dry metaphorically.
الخلا (al-khala): Fresh grass that is green and growing; from the hadith.
المحرم (al-muharram): Here: that which is sacred and prohibited to violate; specifically the vegetation of the Haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a person in the Haram cuts a fresh tree that grew by itself and is of a type that people normally grow (e.g., a fruit tree), what is the ruling?
A) He owes the value to the Haram because it is in the sacred precinct.
B) He owes nothing because it is considered as if people grew it, so it is like cultivated land.
C) He owes double the value: one for the Haram and one for the owner.
D) He owes the value only if the tree does not regrow.

Key Takeaway
Cutting fresh vegetation in the Haram is haram and requires a value guarantee, with specific exceptions for dry, idhkhir, and cultivated plants.

Ruling on Cutting Vegetation in the Haram
Ruling with proof on cutting vegetation in the Haram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on cutting fresh vs. dry vegetation in the Haram and identify the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Fresh vegetation in the Haram is inviolable; cutting it requires compensation, but dry wood is free.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents the Hanafi ruling on cutting plants and trees in the sacred precinct of Makkah. The ruling distinguishes between living, growing vegetation and dried matter, with a clear basis in the prophetic hadith. Understanding this distinction is essential for anyone performing Hajj or entering the Haram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
Identify the act being ruled upon: cutting grass (hashish) or a tree in the Haram that is not owned and not cultivated by people.
2
Determine the ruling
The ruling is that the person must guarantee (daman) the value of what was cut, except if the vegetation is already dried (jaffa). Compensation is wajib.
The ruling applies to both muhrim and non-muhrim.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith in Sahih Bukhari and Sahih Muslim: 'لا يختلي خلاها ولا يعضد شوكها' meaning its fresh herbage shall not be cut and its thorns shall not be broken.
This hadith is explicit in prohibiting cutting living vegetation.
4
Analyse the linguistic explanation
The passage explains that 'khala' refers to fresh herbage (hashish), 'ikhtila' means cutting, and 'adad' means cutting or breaking trees.
Understanding these terms clarifies the scope of the prohibition.
5
Apply the exception
The exception is for dried vegetation (jaffa), which becomes firewood (hatab) and is no longer considered protected.
Thus, dry wood may be taken freely without compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قطع حشيش الحرم أو شجراً غير مملوك ولا مما ينبته الناس ضمن قيمته إلا فيما جف لحديث الصحيحين لا يختلي خلاها ولا يعضد شوكها والخلا بالقصر الحشيش واختلاؤه قطعه، والعضد قطع الشجر من باب ضرب كذا في المغرب. وفي فتح القدير : الرطب من الكلأ والشجر اسم للقائم الذي بحيث ينمو فإذا جف فهو حطب.
For if he cuts the grass of the Haram or a tree that is not owned and not from what people cultivate, he guarantees its value except in what has dried, based on the hadith in the two Sahihs: 'Its grass (khala) shall not be cut (yukhtala) and its thorns shall not be broken (yu'addad).' Khala with qasr means hasheesh; ikhtilaa is cutting it; and 'addad is cutting the tree from the category of daraba as in al-Mughrib. And in Fath al-Qadir: The moist from herbage and tree is a name for the standing that grows, so when it dries it is firewood.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with its proof. It states that if a person (whether muhrim or not) cuts the grass (hashish) or any tree in the Haram, provided the tree is not owned by anyone and is not cultivated by people, then that person must pay compensation equal to its value. The exception is vegetation that has already dried (jaffa), because that is considered firewood, not living growth, and may be taken freely. The proof is the famous hadith from Sahih Bukhari and Muslim about the sanctity of Makkah's vegetation: 'لا يختلي خلاها ولا يعضد شوكها' – meaning its fresh herbage must not be cut and its thorns/trees must not be broken. The commentary explains the linguistic meanings: khala refers to fresh herbage, 'ukhtila' means cutting, and 'addad means cutting trees. Fath al-Qadir adds that the wet herbage and trees are those that are still growing, so when they dry out they become firewood (hatab) and are no longer subject to the prohibition. This ruling reinforces the inviolability of the Haram even for non-muhrim individuals.

Key Terms
الخلا (al-khala): Fresh grass/herbage that is still growing in the Haram.
العضد (al-'adad): Cutting off tree branches or breaking thorns from trees in the Haram.
الحشيش (al-hashish): In the context, it refers to herbage/plants; linguistically it is dry but often used for fresh as well.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the linguistic meaning of 'al-khala'?
A) Dry grass
B) Fresh grass
C) All types of grass
D) Trees

Key Takeaway
Cutting fresh, non-owned vegetation in the Haram incurs a compensation wajib, based on the hadith; dry vegetation is exempt.

Classification of Haram Vegetation and the Ownership Dispute
Expands on exceptions and disputes regarding cutting Haram vegetation and ownership.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify Haram vegetation into categories with their rulings and explain how the intra-Hanafi dispute on land ownership affects compensation.

Core Idea
Only naturally grown, non-cultivated-type, fresh, unbroken, non-idhkhir vegetation requires compensation; ownership of the tree follows payment.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the rules for cutting vegetation in the Haram. It clarifies which plants are exempt from penalty—such as dried wood and idhkhir—and which incur compensation. It also delves into an important intra-Hanafi disagreement: whether the land of the Haram can be owned, and how that affects the amount of compensation owed. Understanding these details is crucial for correctly applying the sacred law in the Haram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general prohibition and its exceptions
The hadith prohibits cutting young, fresh vegetation in the Haram. The passage lists exceptions: idhkhir, dried wood, broken twigs, and anything cultivated by people. These are not subject to compensation.
The exceptions are cumulative; if even one condition is met, no penalty.
2
Classify vegetation into the compensating and non-compensating categories
Using the author's classification, determine if the plant is idhkhir, dry, broken, or cultivated. If none of these, and it grew naturally and is not of a type people plant, then compensation is due.
Fruit trees are treated as cultivated because fruit cultivation is the norm.
3
Understand the legal effect of paying compensation
Once the cutter pays the value, he becomes the owner of the tree. However, using it (e.g., selling) is makruh tahrimi because it would encourage further cutting. The buyer, however, may use it freely.
This ownership is unique to trees; game in the Haram is never owned despite penalty.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on land ownership in the Haram
Abu Hanifa holds that no one can own land in the Haram; it is a public endowment. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow ownership. This affects a case where a tree grows on someone's claimed land: Abu Hanifa says only one value (for the Haram) is due; the Sahibayn say two values (Haram + owner). The mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa.
Al-Hidayah notes that the Sahibayn's view is also a narration from Abu Hanifa, but the dominant view is the one in the matn.
5
Apply the rulings to branch cases
The passage discusses branches: if the origin (root) is in the Haram, branches in the Halal are still subject to compensation. If the origin is in the Halal, branches in the Haram are free. If split, compensation is due regardless of which side the branch grows.
This follows the principle that the tree follows its root.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
