When the Qarin Owes Only One Dam: The Miqat Exception
Exception to double penalty for Qarin passing miqat without ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rules that a Qarin who passes the miqat without ihram owes one dam, and distinguish Zufr's opposing view and its rebuttal.

Core Idea
Passing the miqat without ihram introduces deficiency only into one ritual, so only one dam is owed.

In Hajj, the Qarin (performer of Hajj and Umrah together) normally owes double penalties for violations because he has two ihrams. However, a key exception arises when he passes the miqat without being in ihram. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that only one dam is obligatory, and it refutes the dissenting view of Zufr. It also lists several other cases where the Qarin incurs a single penalty, demonstrating that the 'double penalty' rule is not absolute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed act
The act: a person passes the miqat (the boundary for ihram) without being in ihram, and later enters ihram as a Qarin (for both Hajj and Umrah). The dispute: how many dam (penalty) does he owe?
The matn's phrase 'إلا أن يجاوز الميقات غير محرم' sets up this exception.
2
State the majority Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa and the majority say: one dam is wajib. The commentator explains that the obligation at the miqat was only one of the two rituals (either Hajj or Umrah), so the deficiency affects only that one.
The reasoning is that the miqat is a single obligation; the person missed ihram for one ritual, not both.
3
Analyze Zufr's opposing view
Zufr argued that since the person enters as a Qarin, the deficiency (missing the miqat) is introduced into both ihrams, therefore two dams are due.
Zufr's view is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, but it is considered weak (marjuh) in the school.
4
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal
The commentator refutes Zufr: the deficiency is only on what was obligatory at the miqat — which was one ritual. Entering as a Qarin does not multiply the original deficiency; it merely adds a second ritual that was not initially required at the miqat.
Thus the thamarah al-khilaf (practical result) is one dam vs two dams.
5
Explore the analogous cases from Ghayat al-Bayan
The passage lists five other situations where the Qarin owes only a single penalty, analogous to the Mufrid: (1) departing Arafah before the Imam, (2) performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah in a state of impurity after returning home, (3) killing game after standing at Arafah, (4) shaving before slaughtering, (5) cutting a tree of the Haram. These confirm that not every violation doubles for the Qarin.
Each case involves a violation that relates to the overall ritual or to only one of the two ihrams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (إلا أن يجاوز الميقات غير محرم) استثناء منقطع لأنه ليس داخلاً فيما قبله لأن صدر الكلام إنما هو فيما لزم المفرد بسبب الجناية على إحرامه والمجاوز بغير إحرام لم يكن محرماً ليخرج لأنه يلزمه دم، سواء أحرم بعد ذلك بحج أو عمرة أو بهما أو لم يحرم أصلاً فلا حاجة إلى استثنائه في كلامهم لكن على تقدير أن يحرم بعد المجاوزة فقد أدخل نقصاً في إحرامه وهو ترك جزء منه بين الميقات والموضع الذي أحرم فيه فتوهم زفر أنه إذا أحرم قارناً أنه أدخل هذا النقص على الإحرامين فأوجب دمين وقلنا إن الواجب عليه عند دخول الميقات أحد النسكين فإذا جاوزه بغير إحرام ثم أحرم بهما فقد أدخل النقص على ما لزمه وهو أحدهما فلزمه جزاء واحد. وأورد في غاية البيان على اقتصارهم في الاستثناء على هذه المسألة مسائل منها : أن القارن إذا أفاض قبل الإمام يجب عليه دم واحد كالمفرد ومنها إذا طاف طواف الزيارة جنباً أو محدثاً وقد رجع إلى أهله يجب عليه دم واحد ومنها أن القارن إذا وقف بعرفة ثم قتل صيداً فعليه قيمة واحدة كما في الأجناس ومنها إذا حلق قبل أن يذبح فإنه يلزمه دم واحد. ومنها أن القارن إذا قطع شجر الحرم فإنه يلزمه قيمة واحدة كالمفرد ا هـ. فالحاصل أن الحجتين أو العمرتين على هذا لو أحرم بمائة حجة أو عمرة ثم جن قبل رفضها فعليه مائة جزاء ا هـ قوله : (وقد قدمنا أن المذهب الخ) أي عند قول المتن فإذا حلق يوم النحر حل من إحراميه» قوله : (فلا حاجة إلى استثنائه قال في الشرنبلالية لكن ذكر لبيان قول زفر ا هـ أي للتنصيص على مخالفته قوله : (وأورد في غاية البيان الخ أقول : أوصل في اللباب المستثنيات إلى اثني عشر وفي شرحه كلام طويل فراجعهما . قوله : (وأما مسألة الحلق قبل الذبح (الخ ما أجاب به هنا قد عزاه فيما سبق إلى العناية، وقدمنا
His saying: (Unless he passes the miqat without being in ihram) is a disconnected exception because it is not included in what preceded, since the opening of the speech was about what is obligated on the Mufrid due to violation of his ihram, and the one who passes without ihram is not a muhrim to be excluded; because a dam is obligated upon him, whether he enters ihram afterwards for Hajj or Umrah or both, or does not enter ihram at all. So there is no need to except it in their speech. However, on the assumption that he enters ihram after passing, he has introduced a deficiency into his ihram, which is leaving a part of it between the miqat and the place where he entered ihram. Zufr mistakenly thought that if he enters as a Qarin, he has introduced this deficiency into both ihrams, thus obligating two dams. But we said: what is obligatory upon him at the miqat is one of the two rituals; so if he passes it without ihram and then enters ihram for both, he has introduced the deficiency upon what was obligatory upon him, which is one of them, so one penalty is owed. And in Ghayat al-Bayan, objections are raised regarding their limiting the exception to this case, including: that if the Qarin departs before the Imam, one dam is obligated upon him like a Mufrid; and if he performs the Tawaf al-Ziyarah in a state of janabah or without wudu and has returned to his family, one dam is obligated; and if the Qarin stands at Arafah and then kills game, he owes a single value, as in al-Ajnas; and if he shaves before slaughtering, one dam is obligated; and if the Qarin cuts a tree of the Haram, he owes a single value like a Mufrid. End. So the conclusion is that with two Hajjs or two Umrahs, if he enters ihram for one hundred Hajjs or Umrahs and then commits a violation before abandoning them, one hundred penalties are owed. End. His saying: (And we have stated that the madhhab...) i.e., according to the text: 'When he shaves on the Day of Sacrifice, he becomes free from both ihrams.' His saying: (So there is no need to except it) He said in al-Sharnabliyyah: 'But it was mentioned to clarify the statement of Zufr.' End. i.e., to explicitly state his disagreement. His saying: (And in Ghayat al-Bayan, objections...) I say: In al-Lubab, the exceptions reached twelve, and in its commentary there is a lengthy discussion, so refer to both. His saying: (And as for the case of shaving before slaughtering...) what is responded to here has been attributed previously to al-Inayah, and we have stated.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage addresses an important exception to the general rule that the Qarin owes double penalties. The matn states: 'Unless he passes the miqat without being in ihram.' The commentator explains that this is a disconnected exception (istithna' munqati'), meaning it does not really fall under the general rule. The reason is that a person who passes the miqat without ihram is not yet a muhrim, so the rule about penalties for violations of ihram does not apply. However, if he later enters ihram (as a Qarin), he has missed the obligation of ihram at the miqat. This missing of the miqat is considered a deficiency that he introduces into his ihram. Zufr (a Hanafi scholar) thought that because he enters as a Qarin, he introduces this deficiency into both ihrams, thus two dams are owed. The correct Hanafi position is that only one dam is owed because the obligation at the miqat was only one of the two rituals (either Hajj or Umrah), not both. Therefore, the deficiency affects only one ihram. The passage then lists several other cases from Ghayat al-Bayan where the Qarin also owes only a single penalty, analogous to a Mufrid: 1) departing from Arafah before the Imam; 2) performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in a state of major or minor impurity after returning home; 3) standing at Arafah and then killing game (only one value owed); 4) shaving before slaughtering; 5) cutting a tree of the Haram. These show that not every violation multiplies; some violations relate to actions that are specific to one of the two ihrams or to the overall ritual, so only one penalty is incurred. The passage ends with a related discussion that if one combines multiple Hajjs or Umrahs, the penalties multiply accordingly, and a note that the exceptions mentioned in al-Lubab number twelve.

Key Terms
استثناء منقطع (istithna' munqati'): A disconnected exception where the excepted item does not belong to the category of the general rule.
الميقات (al-miqat): The designated boundary for entering ihram for Hajj and Umrah.
زفر (Zufr): Zufr ibn al-Hudhayl, a student of Abu Hanifa, known for some dissenting views.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a Qarin stands at Arafah and then kills game, how many penalties does he owe?
A) One dam
B) Two dams
C) One value (qimah)
D) Two values

Key Takeaway
A Qarin who passes the miqat without ihram owes only one dam because the original obligation at the miqat was a single ritual.

Multiple Penalties for a Qarin and the Exception for Passing Miqat
Explains the Hanafi ruling on double penalties for a Qarin and the exception for passing miqat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of Dam owed by a Qarin for a violation committed after standing at Arafah, and explain why the exception for passing the miqat does not affect this ruling.

Core Idea
A Qarin owes two Dam for any violation until shaving; passing miqat without ihram incurs only one Dam because the deficiency is on one mandatory rite.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq tackles a key fiqh question: how many penalties does a Qarin owe when he violates ihram prohibitions? The author affirms the ruling that two Dam are due, rebuts a weaker view that limits it to one after standing, and then clarifies an apparent exception regarding passing the miqat. Understanding this ruling requires tracing how the Hanafi school handles the dual ihram of a Qarin and the effect of a deficiency introduced before ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? The violation of ihram prohibitions by a Qarin. The ruling: two Dam are due according to Abu Hanifa.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the matn statement that shaving releases from both ihrams, implying the Qarin is in two ihrams until shaving.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The fact that he is in two separate ihrams means he must compensate for each; hence two Dam.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some mashayikh say the Umrah ihram ends at standing, so only one Dam after standing. The author refutes this.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author declares the view of two Dam as the correct madhhab, citing the matn.
The exception for passing miqat is also explained: only one Dam because the deficiency affects only one obligation.

العناية، وقدمنا
Ihram: Whoever combines two Hajjs (i.e., performs Qiran) and commits a violation before starting the rituals is liable for two Dam according to Abu Hanifa because he is in two ihrams like the Qarin. He made it absolute that two Dam are due, so it includes whether before standing at Arafah or after. There is no dispute regarding before; but regarding after, we have previously presented the difference of the mashayikh: some say the ihram of Umrah for the Qarin ends at standing, so they do not say multiplicity (of Dam); others say it remains, so they say multiplicity. Shaykh al-Islam mentioned that the obligation of two Dam on the Qarin is when the violation is before standing, whether in intercourse or other; after standing, in intercourse two Dam are due, in other prohibitions one Dam. We have previously presented that the madhhab is that the ihram of the Qarin’s Umrah remains after tawaf until shaving, so he is liable for two Dam after standing, whether intercourse, killing game, or other. We have presented that the correct view is that it ends with shaving, even regarding women; so if the Qarin had intercourse after shaving, nothing is due for the Umrah. Thus what is in al-Ajnas, as quoted in Ghayat al-Bayan, that the Qarin if he kills game after standing owes one Dam, is based on the view that Umrah ihram ends with standing, and you know its weakness. His statement: (except that he passes the miqat without ihram) is a disconnected exception because it is not included in what preceded, since the beginning of the speech is about what is owed by the mufrid due to a violation of his ihram, and the one who passes without ihram is not in ihram to be excluded, because he is liable for a Dam, whether he later assumes ihram for Hajj or Umrah or both, or does not assume ihram at all. So there is no need for excluding him in their speech, but on the assumption that he assumes ihram after passing, he has introduced a deficiency into his ihram by leaving part between the miqat and the place he assumed ihram. Zufar thought that if he assumes ihram for Qiran, he introduced this deficiency into both ihrams, thus obligating two Dam; we said that what is obligatory upon him upon entering the miqat is one of the two rites, so when he passed it without ihram then assumed ihram for both, he introduced the deficiency into what was obligatory on him, which is one of them, so he is liable for one penalty. In Ghayat al-Bayan, they objected to limiting the exception to this issue with several issues: including that the Qarin if he does ifadah before the Imam owes one Dam like the mufrid; including that if he performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah while junub or without wudu and then returned to his family, he owes one Dam; including that the Qarin if he stood at Arafah then killed game, he owes one value as in al-Ajnas; including that if he shaved before slaughtering, he is liable for one Dam; including that the Qarin if he cuts the trees of the Haram, he owes one value like the mufrid. So the conclusion is that regarding two Hajjs or two Umrahs, if one assumes ihram for a hundred Hajjs or Umrahs then commits a violation before abandoning them, he owes a hundred penalties. His statement: (We have presented that the madhhab...) i.e., concerning the matn's statement: 'When he shaves on the Day of Nahr, he is released from both ihrams.' His statement: (So there is no need to exclude him) said in al-Sharnablaliyyah, but it was mentioned to clarify the statement of Zufar, i.e., to specify his opposition. His statement: (and mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan...) I say: In al-Lubab, the excluded issues reached twelve, and in its commentary there is lengthy speech, so refer to both. His statement: (and regarding the issue of shaving before slaughtering...) what he answered here he attributed earlier to al-Inayah, and we have presented.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling-with-proof discussion. The author explains the Hanafi position on the number of penalties (Dam) incurred by a Qarin (one who performs Hajj and Umrah together in a single ihram) when he commits a prohibited act during his pilgrimage. The core ruling, attributed to Abu Hanifa, is that a Qarin who commits a violation before starting the rituals (or after, but the view is debated) owes two Dam, because he is considered to be in two ihrams simultaneously. The author then notes a disagreement among later Hanafi scholars about whether the ihram of Umrah for a Qarin ends at standing at Arafah or at shaving. The relied-upon view (madhhab) is that it ends with shaving, so even after standing, two Dam are due for any violation. He critiques the view in al-Ajnas that after standing only one Dam is due, calling it weak. Next, he addresses an exception in the matn: 'except that he passes the miqat without ihram.' He explains this is a disconnected exception because the person passing the miqat without ihram is not yet in ihram, so the general rule about penalties for violations does not apply. Zufar erroneously thought that if such a person then becomes a Qarin, he owes two Dam for the deficiency, but the author refutes this, arguing that the deficiency only affects the one obligatory rite he had to perform. The author then lists several cases from Ghayat al-Bayan where some claimed only one Dam is due, such as doing ifadah before the Imam, performing tawaf while impure, killing game after standing, shaving before slaughter, or cutting trees of the Haram. He concludes that the correct principle is that the multiplicity of Dam corresponds to the number of ihrams, and if a Qarin commits a violation before abandoning any of them, he owes as many Dam as the number of ihrams he is in.

Key Terms
قارن (qārin): One who performs Hajj and Umrah together in a single ihram (Qiran).
دم (dam): A penalty of slaughtering a sheep (or equivalent) for violating an ihram prohibition.
استثناء منقطع (istithnāʾ munqaṭiʿ): A disconnected exception where the excluded item is not part of the general category.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, how many Dam does a Qarin owe if he kills game after standing at Arafah but before shaving?
A) One Dam
B) Two Dam
C) No Dam
D) One Dam if before shaving, two if after

Key Takeaway
A Qarin owes two Dam for any violation committed before shaving, because the Umrah ihram remains until then; passing the miqat without ihram only incurs one Dam because the deficiency is on a single obligation.

Joint Killing of Game: Jaza' al-Fi'l vs Jaza' al-Mahall
Ruling statement distinguishing types of penalty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to DISTINGUISH between jaza' al-fi'l and jaza' al-mahall and DETERMINE the liability when multiple persons, including muhrims and halals, jointly kill game in the Haram.

Core Idea
The muhrim's penalty multiplies, the halal's in the Haram does not.

Killing game while in ihram or within the Haram carries a specific penalty (dam or value). This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies how liability is distributed when multiple people are involved. The key distinction lies in whether the penalty attaches to the act itself (jaza' al-fi'l) or to the sanctity of the place (jaza' al-mahall). Understanding this principle is essential for correctly determining what each participant owes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core distinction
Recognize that the text sets up two categories: the penalty for a muhrim is jaza' al-fi'l (penalty of the act), while for a halal in the Haram it is jaza' al-mahall (penalty of the place). This determines whether the penalty is multiplied or shared.
This is a legal maxim in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Apply to the muhrim case
When two muhrims jointly kill game, each owes a full penalty because the liability is tied to each person's prohibited act. The penalty multiplies.
Analogous to kaffarah for accidental killing.
3
Apply to the halal case
When two halals jointly kill game within the Haram, they owe a single penalty divided equally because the liability is tied to the sanctity of the place, which is unitary.
Analogous to diyah for accidental killing.
4
Handle mixed case
When a muhrim and a halal jointly kill game in the Haram, the muhrim pays the full value (for his act) and the halal pays half (share of the place penalty).
The muhrim's penalty is not divided.
5
Extend to more than two or special participants
If there are more than two halals, divide the penalty by the number. If a co-participant is a disbeliever or minor (no liability), the halal only pays his proportional share.
The text also discusses a case from al-Jami' al-Kabir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو قتل المحرمان صيداً تعدد الجزاء ولو حلالان لا أي لا يتعدد الجزاء بقتل صيد الحرم لما قدمنا أن الضمان في حق المحرم جزاء الفعل وهو متعدد وفي صيد الحرم جزاء المحل وهو ليس بمتعدد كرجلين قتلا رجلاً خطأ يجب عليهما دية واحدة لأنها بدل المحل، وعلى كل واحد منهما كفارة لأنها جزاء الفعل أشار المصنف إلى أنه لو اشترك محرم وحلال في قتل صيد الحرم فعلى المحرم جميع القيمة وعلى الحلال نصفها لما أن الضمان يتبعض في حق الحلال، وإلى أنه لو كانوا أكثر من اثنين في صيد الحرم قسم الضمان على عددهم، وإني أنه لو اشترك مع الحلال من لا يجب عليه الجزاء من كافر أو وجب على الحلال بقدر ما صبي يخصه من القيمة إذا قسمت على العدد وفي الجامع الكبير : لو أخذ حلال صيد الحرم فقتله نصراني أو بهيمة في يده فعلى الحلال قيمته ولا شيء على النصراني والصبي، ويرجع الحلال بما ضمن عليهما لأنه لولا قتلهما لتمكن الحلال من إرساله وذكر الأسبيجابي أنه لو صبي عن السعدية ما فيه فالأوجه ذكر ما قدمه هناك عن غاية البيان من أنه لم يجن إلا على إحرام الحج لفراغه من أفعال العمرة فيلزمه دم واحد وهو الذي مشى عليه في السعدية وقدمنا ما فيه أيضاً
His statement: (If two muhrims kill game, the penalty is multiple; if two halals, it is not) i.e., the penalty is not multiple for killing game in the Haram, because we have presented that the guarantee (daman) for the muhrim is a penalty for the act, which is multiple; and for the game of the Haram, it is a compensation for the place (mahall), which is not multiple. It is like two men who kill a man by mistake: one diyah is obligatory upon them because it is compensation for the place (the victim), and upon each of them is a kaffarah because it is a penalty for the act. The author indicated that if a muhrim and a halal jointly kill game of the Haram, the muhrim owes the full value, and the halal owes half, because the guarantee is divisible for the halal; if they are more than two, the guarantee is divided by their number; and if a halal is joined by someone on whom the penalty is not obligatory, such as a disbeliever or a minor, then the halal owes only his share. In al-Jami' al-Kabir: If a halal takes game of the Haram and a Christian or an animal kills it in his hand, the halal owes its value, nothing on the Christian or animal, and the halal can reclaim what he paid from them because were it not for their killing, he could have released it. Al-Asbijabi mentioned that regarding … the sound view is to mention what he presented there from Ghayat al-Bayan that he only violated the ihram of Hajj because he finished the actions of Umrah, so he owes one Dam, and that is what al-Sa'diyyah followed, and we have presented its weakness also.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement (matn commentary) on the liability for killing game jointly. The author explains the principle: when two muhrims (pilgrims in ihram) jointly kill a game animal, each is liable for a full penalty (i.e., multiple penalties). But when two halals (non-muhrims) kill game in the Haram (sanctuary), they owe only one joint penalty. The reason is that the penalty for a muhrim is a 'penalty for the act' (jaza' al-fi'l), which is multiplied by the number of perpetrators, similar to kaffarah for accidental killing. For a halal killing game in the Haram, the penalty is a 'compensation for the place' (jaza' al-mahall), which is not multiplied, like diyah for accidental death where only one diyah is owed by the group. The author then extends the ruling: if a muhrim and a halal jointly kill game in the Haram, the muhrim pays the full value and the halal pays half, because the halal's share is divisible. If there are more than two, the compensation is divided among them equally. Special cases: if the co-participant is a disbeliever or a minor (who are not liable for penalties), the halal only pays his proportional share. The author also references al-Jami' al-Kabir regarding a case where a halal captures game and someone else kills it in his hand. Finally, he notes a brief discussion about a muhrim who has completed Umrah actions – the correct view is that he owes one Dam for the Hajj ihram only, as he is free from the Umrah ihram.

Key Terms
جزاء الفعل (jazāʾ al-fiʿl): A penalty that attaches to the act itself, thus multiplied by the number of perpetrators.
جزاء المحل (jazāʾ al-maḥall): A compensation that attaches to the place (the Haram), thus not multiplied among multiple perpetrators.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two muhrims jointly kill a single game animal, what is the penalty according to the Hanafi school?
A) They jointly owe one Dam
B) Each owes a full Dam
C) Only the one who struck first owes Dam
D) No Dam, only repentance

Key Takeaway
The ruling hinges on whether the penalty attaches to the act (multiplied) or the place (shared).

Penalty Multiplicity for Joint Killing: Muhrims vs Non-Muhrims
Explaining the rule when muhrims jointly kill game versus non-muhrims in the Haram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for joint killing of game by muhrims and non-muhrims, explain the distinction between jaza' al-fi'l and badal al-mahall, and apply the analogy with accidental homicide.

Core Idea
The penalty for a muhrim is per act (multiple); compensation for the Haram is per place (single) — the distinction determines multiplicity.

This lesson unpacks a key fiqh principle in the Hajj chapter: when two or more people jointly kill game, does the penalty multiply? The answer depends on whether the killers are in ihram or are non-muhrims within the Haram. The Hanafi school uses a powerful analogy with accidental homicide to justify the differing outcomes. By the end, you will see how the same action produces different legal consequences based on the legal capacity of the actors and the sanctity of the location.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The matn contrasts 'two muhrims killing game' (penalty multiplies) with 'two non-muhrims killing game in the Haram' (penalty does not multiply). First, clearly separate the two cases.
The ruling for muhrims applies when the game is killed outside the Haram; the ruling for non-muhrims applies only inside the Haram.
2
Understand the distinction: jaza' al-fi'l vs badal al-mahall
The commentary explains that for a muhrim, the penalty is a 'jaza' al-fi'l' — a personal expiation for violating ihram, so it is owed per person. For a non-muhrim in the Haram, the payment is 'badal al-mahall' — compensation for violating the sanctity of the place, so it is a single obligation shared among the participants.
This distinction is the key legal theory (talil) underlying the rule.
3
Analyze the qiyas with accidental homicide
The text provides an analogy: two men who accidentally kill a man owe one diya (blood money) together, but each owes a separate kaffarah (expiation). The diya is like badal al-mahall (shared), the kaffarah is like jaza' al-fi'l (individual). Trace how each element maps.
The diya compensates for the victim (place), the kaffarah expiates each killer's personal act.
4
Apply to mixed and multiple perpetrators
The commentary extends the rule: if a muhrim and a non-muhrim jointly kill game in the Haram, the muhrim owes the full value (his penalty for ihram) and the non-muhrim owes half (his share of the place compensation). For more than two non-muhrims, the value is divided equally. When a non-muhrim is joined by a child or disbeliever (who are not liable), the non-muhrim pays the whole value but can recover from the others.
Note that the muhrim does not share his penalty; it is individual.
5
Summarize the practical ruling
From all cases, the operative rule is: the penalty for a muhrim is always individual (full); the compensation for the Haram is always collective (divided) among those liable. Mixed cases combine both principles.
This sub-rule is from al-Jami' al-Kabir and is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو قتل المحرمان صيداً تعدد الجزاء ولو حلالان لا أي لا يتعدد الجزاء بقتل صيد الحرم لما قدمنا أن الضمان في حق المحرم جزاء الفعل وهو متعدد وفي صيد الحرم جزاء المحل وهو ليس بمتعدد كرجلين قتلا رجلاً خطأ يجب عليهما دية واحدة لأنها بدل المحل، وعلى كل واحد منهما كفارة لأنها جزاء الفعل أشار المصنف إلى أنه لو اشترك محرم وحلال في قتل صيد الحرم فعلى المحرم جميع القيمة وعلى الحلال نصفها لما أن الضمان يتبعض في حق الحلال، وإلى أنه لو كانوا أكثر من اثنين في صيد الحرم قسم الضمان على عددهم، وإني أنه لو اشترك مع الحلال من لا يجب عليه الجزاء من كافر أو صبي وجب على الحلال بقدر ما يخصه من القيمة إذا قسمت على العدد وفي الجامع الكبير : لو أخذ حلال صيد الحرم فقتله نصراني أو بهيمة في يده فعلى الحلال قيمته ولا شيء على النصراني والصبي، ويرجع الحلال بما ضمن عليهما لأنه لولا قتلهما لتمكن الحلال من إرساله.
His saying: (If two muhrims kill game, the penalty multiplies, but if two non-muhrims [do so], it does not). That is, the penalty does not multiply by killing game of the Haram because we already stated that the guarantee in the case of a muhrim is a penalty for the act, and it is multiple, while in the case of game of the Haram, it is a compensation for the place, and it is not multiple, like two men who kill a man by mistake: one diya is obligatory upon them because it is a substitute for the place, and upon each one is a kaffarah because it is a penalty for the act. The author indicated that if a muhrim and a non-muhrim join in killing game of the Haram, then upon the muhrim is the full value, and upon the non-muhrim is half of it, because the guarantee is divisible with respect to the non-muhrim; and that if there are more than two in [killing] game of the Haram, the guarantee is divided among their number; and that if one joins the non-muhrim who is not obligated to pay penalty, such as a disbeliever or a child, then upon the non-muhrim is the amount that belongs to him from the value when divided by the number. And in al-Jami' al-Kabir: If a non-muhrim takes game of the Haram and a Christian or an animal in his hand kills it, then upon the non-muhrim is its value, and nothing upon the Christian and the child, and the non-muhrim recovers from them what he guaranteed, because if not for their killing, he could have released it.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This is the commentary expanding the matn ruling on joint killing. The author explains that when two muhrims together kill game (outside the Haram), the penalty multiplies because each muhrim owes a separate penalty for his act. But if two non-muhrims kill game inside the Haram, only one compensation (value) is due because it is compensation for the sanctity of the place, not for the act. The author draws an analogy with accidental homicide: two killers owe one diya (blood money) because diya is compensation for the victim's life, but each owes a kaffarah (expiation) because kaffarah is for the act of killing. Here, the penalty for a muhrim is like kaffarah (per act), while the compensation for game of the Haram by a non-muhrim is like diya (per victim/place). Then the author explains sub-rules: if a muhrim and a non-muhrim jointly kill game of the Haram, the muhrim owes the full value (penalty for his ihram) and the non-muhrim owes half (as compensation for the Haram, divided among perpetrators). Similarly, with more than two, the value is divided. If a non-muhrim is joined by someone not liable (disbeliever, child), the non-muhrim pays the whole value but can recover from the others proportionally, because he could have released the game if not for their interference.

Key Terms
جزاء (jaza'): Penalty or compensation due for killing game; for a muhrim it is a penalty for violating ihram, for a non-muhrim in the Haram it is compensation for the sanctity of the Haram.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or liability to pay the value or penalty; here it can be divided among non-muhrims but not among muhrims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two non-muhrims jointly kill a wild animal inside the Haram, what is the ruling on the penalty?
A) Each owes a full penalty
B) One penalty is due from both, divided equally
C) Only the one who struck the first blow owes penalty
D) No penalty because it is joint

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school sharply distinguishes between a muhrim's penalty (individual, per act) and a non-muhrim's compensation for the Haram (collective, per place); the qiyas with accidental homicide confirms this duality.
